Q1. The complex numbers z = x + iy which satisfy the equation $\left|\frac{z-3 i}{z+3 i}\right|=1$ lie on
    (A) on x axis.
    (B) the straight line y = 3
    (C) the x-axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a circle passing through the origin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given$\left|\frac{z-3 i}{z+3 i}\right|=1$
Putting z = x + iy , we get
$\left|\frac{x+i y-3 i}{x+i y+3 i}\right|=1$
$\Rightarrow\left| {{{x+iy - 3i} }} \right| =\left| {{{x+iy + 3i} }} \right|$
$\Rightarrow\left| {{{x+i(y - 3)} }} \right| =\left| {{{x+i(y + 3)} }} \right|$
$\Rightarrow \sqrt { { x }^{ 2 }+{ \left( { y-3 } \right) }^{ 2 } } =\sqrt { { x }^{ 2 }+{ \left( { y+3 } \right) }^{ 2 } } $ $\left[ \because \left| x+iy \right| =\sqrt { { x }^{ 2 }+{ y }^{ 2 } } \right]$
Squaring on both sides, we get
${ x }^{ 2 }+{ \left( { y-3 } \right) }^{ 2 }={ x }^{ 2 }+{ \left( { y+3 } \right) }^{ 2 }$
$ \Rightarrow { x }^{ 2 }+{ y }^{ 2 }-6y+9={ x }^{ 2 }+{ y }^{ 2 }+6y+9$
$ \Rightarrow 12y=0$
$ \Rightarrow y=0$
Which means the X-axis.

Q2. The inequality |z - 4| < |z - 2| represents the region given by
    (A) Re(z) $<$ 0
    (B) y > 4
    (C) Re(z) > 0
    (D) x > 3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given |z - 4| < |z - 2|
Putting z = x + iy, we get
|x + iy - 4| < |x + iy - 2|
$\Rightarrow$ |(x - 4) + iy| < |(x - 2) + iy| 
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(x-4)^{2}+y^{2}}$ < $\sqrt{(x-2)^{2}+y^{2}}$ [$\because$ |x + iy| = $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$]
Squaring on both sides we get
(x - 4)^2 + y^2 < (x - 2)^2 + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 16 - 8x + y^2 < x^2 + 4 - 4x + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 16 - 4 < 8x - 4x
$\Rightarrow$ 12 < 4x
$\Rightarrow$ x > 3

Q3. If Z = $\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}+\frac{i}{2}$, Z^3 then equals
    (A) -i
    (B) -1
    (C) 1
    (D) i   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given Z = $\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}+\frac{i}{2}$ 
Z^3 = $\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}+\frac{i}{2}\right)^{3}$ [$\because$ (a + b)^3 = a^3 + b^3 + 3ab(a + b)]
$\Rightarrow$ Z^3 = $\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}^{3}+\frac{i^{3}}{2}^{3}+3 \cdot \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2} \cdot \frac{i}{2}\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}+\frac{i}{2}\right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ Z^3 = $\frac{3 \sqrt{3}}{8}+\frac{i^{3}}{8}+\frac{3 \sqrt{3} i}{8}(\sqrt{3}+i)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ Z^3 = $\frac{3 \sqrt{3}-i+9 i-3 \sqrt{3}}{8}$ [$\because$ i^2 = -1]
$\Rightarrow$ Z^3 = $\frac{8 i}{8}$ = i

Q4. $2\sqrt { - 9} \sqrt { - 16}$, is equals to
    (A) -48
    (B) -24   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 24
    (D) 48
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $2\sqrt { - 9} \sqrt { - 16} $ 
= $2\sqrt { 9.(-1)} \sqrt {( -1). 16} $ 
= $2\sqrt { 9} \sqrt { 16}\sqrt { -1} \sqrt { -1}$ 
= $2\sqrt { 9} \sqrt { 16}.i.i$ [ $\because$ i^2 = -1]
= 2.3.4.(-1)
= -24

Q5. If ${\left( {\sqrt 3 + i} \right)^{10}} = a + ib;a,b \in R,$ then a and b are respectively :
    (A) 64 and - 64$\sqrt 3 $
    (B) 512 and - 512$\sqrt 3 $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 128 and 128$\sqrt 3 $
    (D) $1024 \ and \ 1024\sqrt 3$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: First we will find the polar representation of the complex number $\sqrt { 3 } +i$
Let $\sqrt{3}+i=r(\cos \theta+i \sin \theta) \Rightarrow r \cos \theta=\sqrt{3} a n d \quad r \sin \theta=1$
$\therefore r^{2}\left(\cos ^{2} \theta+\sin ^{2} \theta\right)=3+1=4 \Rightarrow r^{2}=4 \Rightarrow r=2$
Now $cos\theta =\frac { \sqrt { 3 } }{ 2 } ,\quad sin\theta =\frac { 1 }{ 2 } $ , both are positive .
So Amplitude $=\theta =\frac { \Pi }{ 6 } $
Hence $\sqrt { 3 } +i=2\left( cos\frac { \Pi }{ 6 } +isin\frac { \Pi }{ 6 } \right) =2{ e }^{ \frac { i\Pi }{ 6 } }$
Now,
$(\sqrt{3}+i)^{10}=\left(2 e^{\frac{i \pi}{6}}\right)^{10}=2^{10} e^{\frac{i 5 \pi}{3}}=2^{10}\left(\cos \left(\frac{5 \Pi}{3}\right)+i \sin \left(\frac{5 \Pi}{3}\right)\right)$
$=2^{10}\left(\cos \left(2 \Pi-\frac{\Pi}{3}\right)+i \sin \left(2 \Pi-\frac{\Pi}{3}\right)\right)=2^{10}\left(\cos \left(\frac{-\pi}{3}\right)+i \sin \left(\frac{-\pi}{3}\right)\right)$
$=2^{10}\left(\cos \left(\frac{\Pi}{3}\right)-i \sin \left(\frac{\Pi}{3}\right)\right)=2^{10}\left(\frac{1}{2}-i \frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}\right)=2^{10}\left(\frac{1-\sqrt{3} i}{2}\right)=2^{9}(1-\sqrt{3} i)$
Hence ${\left( {\sqrt 3 + i} \right)^{10}} = a + ib$ $\Rightarrow { 2 }^{ 9 }\left( 1-\sqrt { 3 } i \right) =a+ib$
$\Rightarrow a={ 2 }^{ 9 }=512\quad and\quad b={ -2 }^{ 9 }\sqrt { 3 } =-512\sqrt { 3 } \\ $

Q6. Let $x,y \in R,$then x + iy is a non real complex number if
    (A) y = 0
    (B) x = 0
    (C) x $ \ne $ 0
    (D) y $ \ne $ 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If a complex number has to be a non real complex number then its imaginary part should not be zero $\Rightarrow iy\neq 0\Rightarrow y\neq 0$

Q7. Let x, y $ \in$ R, then x + iy is a purely imaginary number if
    (A) x = 0, y $ \ne $ 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x $ \ne $ 0, y = 0
    (C) x $ \ne $ 0, y $ \ne $ 0
    (D) x = 0, y = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A purely imaginary number is a complex number which has only an imaginary part (iy) 
But if y = 0 the complex number iy will become 0 which is real.
Hence the condition for a number to be purely imaginary is x = 0 and $ y\neq 0$

Q8. Multiplicative inverse of the non zero complex number x + iy (x, y $\in$ R)
    (A) $-\frac{x}{x^2+y^2}+\frac{y}{x^2+y^2} i$
    (B) $\frac{x}{x^2+y^2}-\frac{y}{x^2+y^2} i$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{x}{x+y}-\frac{y}{x+y} i$
    (D) $-\frac{x}{x+y}+\frac{y}{x+y} i$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Multiplicative inverse of the complex number x + iy = $\frac{1}{x+i y}=\frac{1}{x+i y} \cdot \frac{x-i y}{x-i y}=\frac{x-i y}{x^2+y^2}$ [$\because$ i^2 = -1]

Q9. If z_1 and z_2 are non-real complex numbers such that z_1 and z_2 and z_1z_2 are real numbers, then
    (A) ${z_1} = \overline {{z_1}} $ and ${z_2} = \overline {{z_2}} $
    (B) ${z_1} = - \overline {{z_2}} $
    (C) ${z_2} = \overline {{z_2}} $
    (D) ${z_1} = \overline {{z_2}} $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let z_1 = x_1 + iy_1 and z_2 = x_2 + iy_2 
Given z_1 and z_2 are non-real complex numbers, so we have ${ y }_{ 1 }\neq 0,{ y }_{ 2 }\neq 0$ 
z_1 + z_2 = (x + iy_1) + (x_2 + iy_2) = (x_1 + x_2) + i(y_1 + y_2) 
z_1 + z_2 is a real number 
$\Rightarrow$ y_1 + y_2 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ y_1 = -y_2 .....(i)
Now z_1z_2 = (x_1 + iy_1) $\cdot$ (x_2 + iy_2) = (x_1x_2 - y_1y_2) + i(x_1y_1 + x_1y_2)
z_1z_2 is a real number $\Rightarrow$ x_2y_1 + x_1y_2 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ x_2y_1 = -x_1y_2 ....(ii)
Now from (i) and (ii) we get $\Rightarrow$ x_2y_1 = x_1y_1 $\Rightarrow$ x_2 = x_1 
Hence we get z_1 = x_2 - iy_2 and z_2 = x_2 + iy_2 
So ${z_1} = \overline {{z_2}} $

Q10. The inequality |z - 6| < |z - 2| represents the region given by
    (A) Re(z) > 2
    (B) Re(z) < 2
    (C) Re(z) < 4
    (D) Re(z) > 4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given |z - 6| < |z - 2|
Putting z = x + iy, we get
|x + iy - 6| <|x + iy - 2|
$\Rightarrow$ |(x - 6) + iy| < |(x - 2) + iy|
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(x-6)^{2}+y^{2}}$ < $\sqrt{(x-2)^{2}+y^{2}}$ [$\because$ |x + iy| = $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$]
Squaring on both sides we get
(x - 6)^2 + y^2 < (x - 2)^2 + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 36 - 12x + y^2 < x^2 + 4 - 4x + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 36 - 4 < 12x - 4x
$\Rightarrow$ 32 < 8x
$\Rightarrow$ x > 4

Q11. z + $\overline {z} \ne 0$ if and only if
    (A) Re(z) $ \ne $ 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Im (z) $ \ne $ 0
    (C) ${\text{| z | }} \ne {\text{ }}0$
    (D) z $ \ne $ 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let Z = x + iy then we have $\bar { Z } $ = x - iy
So Z + $\bar { Z }$ = 2x
Now z + $\overline {z} \ne 0$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 2x $\ne$ 0 
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ne$ 0
$\Rightarrow$ Re(z) $\ne$ 0

Q12. Distance of the representative of the number 1 + i from the origin (in Argand’s diagram) is
    (A) $\sqrt 2 $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) 3
    (D) 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let P(x, y) represent the complex number Z = x + iy in the complex plane(Argand plane) and let O(0, 0) be the origin
Then we have OP =$\sqrt { { x }^{ 2 }+{ y }^{ 2 } } $ 
Here Z = 1 + i so that P(x, y) = P(1, 1)
Hence OP =$\sqrt { 1+1 } =\sqrt { 2}$

Q13. If $\omega $ is a cube root of unity, then $\left( {1 + \omega } \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^2}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^4}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^8}} \right)...$ upto 2n factors is
    (A) 0
    (B) 1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2
    (D) -1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\left( {1 + \omega } \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^2}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^4}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^8}} \right)$ .... upto 2n factors
= $\left( {1 + \omega } \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^2}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^3.\omega}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^3.\omega ^3.\omega^2}} \right)...$ upto 2n factors
= $\left( {1 + \omega } \right)\left( {1 + {\omega ^2}} \right)\left( {1 +{\omega}} \right)\left( {1 + {\omega^2}} \right)....$ upto 2n factors [ since ${ \omega }^{ 3 }=1$ ]
=$\left(- {\omega ^2 } \right)\left( {- {\omega }} \right)\left(- {\omega ^2 } \right)\left( {- {\omega }} \right)...$ upto 2n factors $\left[ \because 1+\omega +{ \omega }^{ 2 }=0 \right] $ 
= $\left(- {\omega ^2 } \right)\left( {- {\omega }} \right)\left(- {\omega ^2 } \right)\left( {- {\omega }} \right)...$upto 2n factors 
= $\left[\left(-\omega^{2}\right)(-\omega)\right]\left[\left(-\omega^{2}\right)(-\omega)\right]$ ... n factors
= $\omega^{3} \cdot \omega^{3} \cdot \omega^{3} \dots$ n factors [Since ${ \omega }^{ 3 }$ = 1]
= 1.1.1 .... n factos
= 1^n = 1

Q14. If |z - 2| = |z - 6| then locus of z is given by :
    (A) a straight line parallel to x axis
    (B) a circle
    (C) a straight line parallel to y axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a square
    Answer: C
    Explanation: |z - 2| = |z - 6|
$\Rightarrow$ |x - 2 + iy| = |x - 6 + iy|
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(x-2)^{2}+y^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{(x-6)^{2}+y^{2}}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 4 - 4x + y^2 = x^2 + 36 - 12x + y^2
$\Rightarrow$ 8x = 32
$\Rightarrow$ x = 4
We have any line of the form x = a constant is a line parallel to Y-axis.

Q15. If k, l, m, n are four consecutive integers, then i^k + i^l + i^m + i^n is equal to :
    (A) 2
    (B) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1
    (D) 4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given k, l, m, n are four consecutive integers,
So we have l = k + 1, m = k + 2, n = k + 3
i^k + i^l + i^m + i^n
= i^k + i^k+1 + i^k+2 + i^k+3
= i^k (1 + i + i^2 + i^3) 
= i^k(1 + i - 1 - i)
= i^k.0 = 0 [$\because$ i^2 = -1 and i^3 = -i]

========================================================================
Quadratic Equations Test 02  (id 623) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Complex Numbers and Quadratic Equations
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
========================================================================

Q1. i^2 + i^4 + i^6 + ..... up to 2k + 1 terms, for all k belongs to natural numbers N.
    (A) -1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1
    (C) 2
    (D) 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: i^2 + i^4 + i^6 + ..... upto 2k + 1 terms
i^2 + (i^2)^2 + (i^2)^4 ..... upto 2k + 1 terms
= (i^2)^1 + (i^2)^2 + (i^2)^3 ..... + (i^2)^2k + (i^2)^2k + 1 
= (i^2)^1 + [(i^2)^2 + (i^2)^3] + [((i^2)^4 + (i^2)^5] + ..... + [(i^2)^2k + (i^2)^2k + 1] [$\because$ i^2 = -1]
= (-1) + [1 + (-1)] + [1 + (-1)] + .....+ [1 + (-1)]
= -1

Q2. 1 + i + i^2 + i^3 + .... up to 4n terms is equal to
    (A) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) 1
    (D) -1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: 1 + i + i^2 + i^3 + i^4 + i^5 + ..... up to 4n terms
= $1 + i + {i^2} + {i^2} .i+ {i^2} .{i^2}+ {i^2} .{i^2}.i+...$ up to 4n terms
= $1 + i + {(-1)} + {(-1.i)} + {(-1).(-1)} + {(-1).(-1).i} +...$ up to 4n terms
= $1 + i + {(-1)} + {(-i)} + {(1)} + {(i)} +.......$ up to 4n terms
= $[1 + i + {(-1)} + {(-i)} ]+ [ {(1)} + {(i)} + {(-1)} + {(-i)}]...$ up to 4n terms [combining four terms to get a single term]
= 0 + 0 + 0 ... up to n terms
= 0.n = 0

Q3. $1 + {i^2} + {i^4} + {i^6} + {i^8} + .......$ up to 1001 terms is equal to
    (A) 0
    (B) -1
    (C) 2
    (D) 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $1+i^{2}+i^{4}+i^{6}+i^{8}+\ldots \ldots \ldots . \text { upto } 1001 \text { terms }$
$=\left(i^{2}\right)^{0}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{1}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{2}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{3}+\ldots \ldots . \text { upto } 1001 \quad \text { terms }$
$=\left(i^{2}\right)^{0}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{1}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{2}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{3}+\ldots \ldots \ldots+\left(i^{2}\right)^{1000}$
$=\left[\left(i^{2}\right)^{0}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{1}\right]+\left[\left(i^{2}\right)^{2}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{3}\right]+\ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots+\left[\left(i^{2}\right)^{998}+\left(i^{2}\right)^{999}\right]+\left[\left(i^{2}\right)^{1000}\right]$
$=[1-1]+[1-1]+\ldots \ldots \ldots+[1-1]+1$
=1

Q4. If $\omega $ is a non-real cube root of unity and ${\left( {1 + \omega } \right)^9} = a + b\omega ;a,b \in R,$ then a and b are respectively the numbers :
    (A) 1, 0
    (B) 0, -1
    (C) -1, 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0, 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have $(1+\omega)^{9}$ = $\left(-\omega^{2}\right)^{9}$ = $(-1)^{9}\left(\omega^{2}\right)^{9}$ = $-\omega^{18}$ = $-\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{6}$ = (-1)^6 = -1 [$\because$ $\omega^{3}=1,1+\omega+\omega^{2}$ = 0]
Given ${\left( {1 + \omega } \right)^9} = a + b\omega $ 
$\Rightarrow$ -1 = a + b$\omega$ 
$\Rightarrow$ -1 + 0.$\omega$ = a + b$\omega$
$\Rightarrow$ a = -1, b = 0

Q5. If |z| = 1, then $\frac{z-1}{z+1}, z \neq-1$ is
    (A) non-real
    (B) Complex number
    (C) purely imaginary or zero   <-- CORRECT
    (D) purely real
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let Z = x + iy
Given |z| = 1 $\Rightarrow \sqrt { { x }^{ 2 }+{ y }^{ 2 } } =1$ $\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 = 1
Now, $\frac{Z-1}{Z+1}=\frac{x+i y-1}{x+i y+1}=\frac{x-1+i y}{x+1+i y}$ 
= $\frac{x-1+i y}{x+1+i y} \cdot \frac{x+1-i y}{x+1-i y}$ = $\frac{\left(x^{2}-1\right)+y^{2}+i[y(x+1)-y(x-1)]}{(x+1)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ 
= $\frac{x^{2}+y^{2}-1+2 i y}{(x+1)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ = $\frac{1-1+2 i y}{(x+1)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ [$\because$ x^2 + y^2 = 1] 
$\therefore$ $\frac{Z-1}{Z+1}$ = 0 + $\frac{2 y}{(x+1)^{2}+(y)^{2}} i$
Which is purely imaginary number.
Also when y = 0, the number will become zero

Q6. The equation |4z - 1| = 4|z - 5| represents :
    (A) a parabola
    (B) a circle
    (C) a straight line   <-- CORRECT
    (D) an ellipse
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given |4z - 1| = 4|z - 5|
Let Z = x + iy 
$\Rightarrow$ |4(x + iy) - 1| = 4|x + iy - 5|
$\Rightarrow$ |(4x - 1) + 4iy| = 4(x - 5) + iy|
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(4 x-1)^{2}+(4 y)^{2}}$ = $4 \sqrt{(x-5)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ 
Squaring on both sides we get
(4x - 1)^2 + (4y)^2 = 16[(x - 5)^2 + (y)^2]
$\Rightarrow$ 16x^2 + 1 - 8x + 16y^2 = 16[x^2 + 25 - 10x + y^2]
$\Rightarrow$ 16x^2 + 1 - 8x + 16y^2 - 16x^2 - 400 + 160x - 16y^2 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 152x - 399 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ x = $\frac{399}{152}$
We have x = a constant is a straight line parallel to Y-axis.

Q7. If ${\left( { - 1 + \sqrt 3 i} \right)^n} + {\left( { - 1 - \sqrt 3 i} \right)^n} = {2^n}\alpha $ then $\alpha $ is equal to :
    (A) $ { \left( \omega \right) }^{ n }+{ \left( { \omega }^{ 2 } \right) }^{ n } $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -1
    (C) 1
    (D) 2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have $-1+i \sqrt{3}=2 \omega$ and $-1-i \sqrt{3}=2 \omega^{2}$ 
Now 
$(-1+\sqrt{3} i)^{n}+(-1-\sqrt{3} i)^{n}$ = $(2 \omega)^{n}+\left(2 \omega^{2}\right)^{n}$ = $2^{n}\left[(\omega)^{n}+\left(\omega^{2}\right)^{n}\right]$

Q8. If ( x + iy ) ( 3 – 4i ) = (5 + 12i ) , then $\sqrt {{x^2} + {y^2}} = $
    (A) 16
    (B) 13/5   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5/13
    (D) 65
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given ( x + iy ) ( 3 – 4i ) = (5 + 12i )
$\Rightarrow x+i y=\frac{5+12 i}{3-4 i}=\frac{(5+12 i)(3+4 i)}{(3-4 i)(3+4 i)}$
$\frac{(15-48)+i(20+36)}{9+16}=\frac{-33+56 i}{25}$
$\Rightarrow x=\frac{-33}{25}, y=\frac{56}{25}$
$\therefore \sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}=\sqrt{\left(\frac{-33}{25}\right)^{2}+\left(\frac{56}{25}\right)^{2}}$
$=\sqrt{\frac{1089+3136}{625}}=\sqrt{\frac{4225}{625}}=\frac{65}{25}=\frac{13}{5}$

Q9. The locus of the equation $\left|\frac{3 z-1}{z-1}\right|$ = 1 is
    (A) a circle   <-- CORRECT
    (B) an ellipse
    (C) a straight line
    (D) a hyperbola
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let Z = x + iy
Now $\left|\frac{3 z-1}{z-1}\right|$ = 1
$\Rightarrow$ |3z - 1| = |z - 1|
$\Rightarrow$ |(3 (x + iy) - 1| = |(x + iy) - 1|
$\Rightarrow$ |(3x - 1) + 3iy| = |(x - y) + iy| 
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(3 x-1)^{2}+(3 y)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{(x-1)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ (3x - 1)^2 + (3y)^2 = (x - 1)^2 + (y)^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 9x^2 + 1 - 6x + 9y^2 = x^2 + 1 - 2x + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 8x^2 + 8y^2 - 4x = 0
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 - $\frac{1}{2}$x = 0
We have this is a circle with centre ($\frac{1}{4}$, 0) and radius = $\frac{1}{4}$.

Q10. $\sqrt { - 8} \sqrt { - 18} \sqrt { - 4} $ is
    (A) 24
    (B) -24i   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 24i
    (D) -24
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\sqrt{-8} \sqrt{-18} \sqrt{-4}$ 
= $\sqrt{8} \cdot \sqrt{-1} \cdot \sqrt{18} \cdot \sqrt{-1} \cdot \sqrt{4} \cdot \sqrt{-1}$ = $2 \sqrt{2} . i .3 \sqrt{2} . i .2 . i$ = 24i^3 = -24i [$\because$ i^2 = -1]

Q11. If $\alpha = \frac z {\overline z}$, then ${\text{|}}\alpha {\text{|}}$ is equal to:
    (A) 1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) -1
    (D) 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Given $\alpha = {\frac z {z }}$ 
Then $|\alpha|$ = $\left|\frac{z}{\bar{z}}\right|=\frac{|z|}{|\bar{z}|}$ = 1 [$\because$ $\left|\frac{z_{1}}{z_{2}}\right|=\frac{\left|z_{1}\right|}{\left|z_{2}\right|}$, $|z|=|\bar{z}|$]

Q12. If z = x + iy ; x, y $\in $ R then :
    (A) $z\bar z < {\left| z \right|^2}$
    (B) $z\bar z \ne {\left| z \right|^2}$
    (C) $z\bar z = {\left| z \right|^2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $z\bar z > {\left| z \right|^2}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: If z = x + iy then $\bar { Z }$ = x - iy
Now $z \bar{z}$ = (x + iy) $\cdot$ (x - iy) = x^2 + y^2 = |z|^2 [$\because$ |z| = $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$]

Q13. The smallest positive integer n for which $\left(\frac{1+i}{1-i}\right)^n=$ 1 is :
    (A) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 8
    (C) 6
    (D) 2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have $\frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } =\frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } \times \frac { 1+i }{ 1+i } =\frac { { \left( 1+i \right) }^{ 2 } }{ 1+1 } $$=\frac { 1+2i-1 }{ 2 } =\frac { 2i }{ 2 } =i$
Therefore $\left(\frac{1+i}{1-i}\right)^n=i^n$
By inspection we have the smallest positive integer such that ${{i} ^n}=1$ is n=4.

Q14. If $\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}+\frac{i}{2}\right)^5+\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}-\frac{i}{2}\right)^5$, then
    (A) Im (z) > 0
    (B) Im (z) = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Im (z) $<$ 0
    (D) Re (z) $> $0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\frac{\sqrt{3}+i}{2}=r(\cos \theta+i \sin \theta) \Rightarrow r \cos \theta=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}$, $ r \sin \theta=\frac{1}{2}$
$\therefore r^2\left(\cos ^2 \theta+\sin ^2 \theta\right)=\frac{3+1}{4}=1 $ $\Rightarrow r^2=1 \Rightarrow r=1$
$\cos \theta=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{2}, \quad \sin \theta=\frac{1}{2}$
$\therefore$ Amplitude = $\theta=\frac{\pi}{6}$
$\frac { \sqrt { 3 } +i }{ 2 } =1\left( cos\frac { \pi }{ 6 } +isin\frac { \pi }{ 6 } \right) ={ e }^{ \frac { i\pi }{ 6 } }$ ...(i)
Since $\frac { \sqrt { 3 } -i }{ 2 } $ lies in the fourth quadrant, the amplitude $=-\theta =-\frac { \pi }{ 6 } $
$\frac { \sqrt { 3 } -i }{ 2 } =1\left( cos\frac { -\pi }{ 6 } +isin\frac { -\pi }{ 6 } \right) ={ e }^{ \frac { -i\pi }{ 6 } }$ ...(i)
$z=\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}+i}{2}\right)^5+\left(\frac{\sqrt{3}-i}{2}\right)^5$
$\Rightarrow z=\left(e^{\frac{ { i\pi }}{6}}\right)^5+\left(e^{\frac{-i \mathrm{\pi}}{6}}\right)^5=e^{\frac{i 5 \mathrm{\pi}}{6}}+e^{-\frac{i 5 \mathrm{\pi}}{6}}$ = $=\cos \left(\frac{5 \pi}{6}\right)+i \sin \left(\frac{5 \pi}{6}\right)+\cos \left(\frac{-5 \pi}{6}\right)$$+i \sin \left(\frac{-5 \pi}{6}\right)=2 \cos \left(\frac{5 \pi}{6}\right)$
Which is purely real [imaginary part of z = 0]

Q15. If the cube roots of unity are 1, $\omega ,{\omega ^2},$ then roots of the equation (x - 1)^3 + 8 = 0 are :
    (A) 1, 1, 1
    (B) $ - 1, - 1 + 2\omega ,1 + 2{\omega ^2}$
    (C) -1, -1, -1
    (D) $ - 1,1 - 2\omega ,1 - 2{\omega ^2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: (x - 1)^3 + 8 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (x - 1)^3 = -8
$\Rightarrow$ (x - 1)^3 = (-2)^3
$\Rightarrow$ $\left(\frac{x-1}{-2}\right)^{3}$ = 1
Let $\frac { x-1 }{ -2 } $ = m (say)
So we get m^3 = 1 $\Rightarrow m=1, \omega ,{\omega ^2}$ [cube roots of unity]
Now m = 1 $\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x-1}{-2}$ = 1 $\Rightarrow$ x - 1 = -2 $\Rightarrow$ x = -1
m = $\omega$ $\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x-1}{-2}=\omega$ $\Rightarrow$ x - 1 = -2$\omega$ $\Rightarrow$ x = 1 - 2$\omega$ 
Also m = $\omega^2$ $\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x-1}{-2}=\omega^{2}$ $\Rightarrow$ x -1 = $-2 \omega^{2}$ $\Rightarrow$ x = 1 - $2 \omega^{2}$ 
Hence the roots of the given equation are $ - 1,1 - 2\omega ,1 - 2{\omega ^2}$

Q1. The value of arg (x) when x < 0 is:
    (A) $\pi /{\rm{2}}$
    (B) $\pi $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) -$\pi $
    (D) 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given x $\in $ R and x $<$ 0, therefore the number is $-x+0i$ and this will be a point inthe second quadrant as x is negative 
We have arg($-x+0i$)=$\theta =$ $\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { y }{ x } \right| } =\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { 0 }{ -1 } \right| } =\tan ^{ -1 }{ 0 } =0$
We have in the second quadrant the principal value of argument= $\Pi -\theta =\Pi -0 =\Pi$
Hence Arg. ( x ) , x $\in $ R and x $<$ 0 is $\pi $

Q2. The number of solutions of the equation Im (z^2) = 0, |z| = 2 is
    (A) 3
    (B) 2
    (C) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy, then we have $\bar { z }$ = x - iy 
x^2 = (x + iy)^2 = x^2 - y^2 + 2xyi 
$\therefore$ im(z^2) = 0 $\Rightarrow$ 2xy = 0 .....(i)
|z| = 2 $\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$ = 2 $\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 = 4 .....(ii)
(x^2 - y^2)^2 = (x^2 + y^2)^2 - 4x^2y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ (x^2 - y^2)^2 = 16
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 - y^2 = $\pm$ 4 .....(iii)
When x^2 - y^2 = 4 from (ii) and (iii) we get 2x^2 = 8 $\Rightarrow$ x^2 = 4 $\Rightarrow$ x = $\pm$ 2
Now from (i) we get y = 0
Hence z = $\pm 2$ 
Now when x^2 - y^2 = -4 from (ii) and (iii) we get 2y^2 = 8 $\Rightarrow$ y^2 = 4 $\Rightarrow$ y = $\pm$ 2
Now from (i) we get x = 0
Hence z = $\pm 2i$ 
Therefore the solutions of the equation Im (z^2) = 0, |z| = 2 are z = $\pm 2i$ and z = $\pm 2$ and so number of solutions = 4.

Q3. Amp. (z - 2 - 3i) = $\frac{\pi}{4}$ then locus of z is
    (A) x - y = 2
    (B) x + y = 2
    (C) x – y + 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x + y = 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy
Then z - 2 - 3i = (x + iy) - 2 - 3i = (x - 2) + i(y - 3)
Let $\theta $ be the amplitude of z.
Then Amp (z - 2 - 3i) = $\frac{\pi}{4}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ tan^-1$\left(\frac{y-3}{x-2}\right)$ = $\frac{\Pi}{4}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{y-3}{x-2}=\tan \frac{\Pi}{4}$ = 1
$\Rightarrow$ y - 3 = x - 2
$\Rightarrow$ x - y + 1 = 0

Q4. If z_1 and z_2 are non-real complex numbers such that |z_1| = |z_2| and Amp. z_1 + Amp. z_2 = $\pi$, then z_1 =
    (A) $\overline {{z_2}} $
    (B) z_2
    (C) $ - \overline {{z_2}} $   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -z_2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let z_1 = $r_{1}\left(\cos \theta_{1}+i \sin \theta_{1}\right)$ and z_2 = $r_{2}\left(\cos \theta_{2}+i \sin \theta_{2}\right)$, where r_1 = |z_1|, r_2 = |z_2| and $\theta_{1}, \theta_{2}$ are the amplitudef of the complex numbers.
Given |z_1| = |z_2| and$Amp.{z_{1}} + Amp.{z_2} = \pi $ $\Rightarrow$ r_1 = r_2 and $ { \theta }_{ 1 }+{ \theta }_{ 2 }=\pi $ 
Now z_1 = ${ r }_{ 1 }\left( cos{ \theta }_{ 1 }+isin{ \theta }_{ 1 } \right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ z_1 = $r_{2}\left[\cos \left(\pi-\theta_{2}\right)+i \sin \left(\pi-\theta_{2}\right)\right]$ 
$\Rightarrow$ z_1 = $r_{2}\left(-\cos \theta_{2}+i \sin \theta_{2}\right)$ = $-\left[r_{2}\left(\cos \theta_{2}-i \sin \theta_{2}\right)\right]$ = $-\overline{z_{2}}$

Q5. The complex numbers sinx + i cos2x and cosx – i sin2x are conjugate to each other, for
    (A) no value of x   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $x=\left(n+\frac{1}{2}\right) \frac{\pi}{2}$
    (C) x = ${\rm{n}}\pi $
    (D) x = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let
z_1 = sinx + icos2x and z_2 = cosx–isin2x
$\Rightarrow$$\overline z$_1 = sinx − icos2x, $\overline z$_2 = cosx + isin2x
Given that z_1 = $\overline z$_2 and z_2 = $\overline z$_1
$\Rightarrow$ sinx + icos2x = cosx + isin2x and cosx − isin2x = sinx − icos2x
$\Rightarrow$ sinx = cosx......(i) and cos2x = sin2x........(ii)
Now cos2x = sin2x $\Rightarrow$ 2cos2x − 1 = 2sinx cosx
$\Rightarrow$ 2sin^2x − 2sin^2x = 1using(i)
$\Rightarrow$ 0 = 1
Which is not possible.
Hence we can say there is no solution for the system of equations

Q6. The value of ${\left( { - 1 + \sqrt { - 3} } \right)^2} + {\left( { - 1 - \sqrt { - 3} } \right)^2}$is
    (A) -4   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 4
    (C) 8
    (D) -2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have $\sqrt { -3 } =\sqrt { -1.3 } =\sqrt { -1 } \sqrt { 3 } = \sqrt { 3 }i$
$\therefore-1+\sqrt{-3}=-1+i \sqrt{3}=2 \omega \quad \text { and } \quad-1-\sqrt{-3}=-1-i \sqrt{3}=2 \omega^{2}$
$\left[\because \omega=\frac{-1+i \sqrt{3}}{2} \quad \text { and } \quad \omega^{2}=\frac{-1-i \sqrt{3}}{2}\right]$
$(-1+\sqrt{-3})^{2}+(-1-\sqrt{-3})^{2}$ $=(2 \omega)^{2}+\left(2 \omega^{2}\right)^{2}=4 \omega^{2}+4 \omega^{4}=4\left(\omega^{2}+\omega^{3} \cdot \omega\right)$
=$4\left(\omega^{2}+\omega\right)=4 \times-1=-4$ $\left[\because \omega^{3}=1,1+\omega+\omega^{2}=0\right]$

Q7. If $\alpha $ is a complex number such that ${\alpha ^2} + \alpha + 1 = 0$ then ${\alpha ^{31}}$ is
    (A) 0
    (B) 1
    (C) $\alpha $   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${\alpha ^2}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ${\alpha ^2} + \alpha + 1 = 0$ $\Rightarrow \alpha =\frac { -1\pm \sqrt { 1-4 } }{ 2 } =\frac { -1\pm i\sqrt { 3 } }{ 2 } =\omega ,{ \omega }^{ 2 }$ 
When $\alpha=\omega \Rightarrow \alpha^{31}=\omega^{31}$ = $\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{10} \cdot \omega=1 \cdot \omega=\omega=\alpha$ 
Also when $\alpha=\omega^{2} \Rightarrow \alpha^{31}=\left(\omega^{2}\right)^{31}$ = $\omega^{62}=\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{20} \cdot \omega^{2}=1 . \omega^{2}=\omega^{2}=\alpha$ 
Hence ${\alpha ^{31}}$ = $\alpha $

Q8. The value of $\left(\frac{1+\omega}{\omega^2}\right)^3$ is
    (A) 2
    (B) 1
    (C) 0
    (D) -1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\left(\frac{1+\omega}{\omega^{2}}\right)^{3}$ = $\left(\frac{-\omega^{2}}{\omega^{2}}\right)^{3}$ = (-1)^3 = -1 [$\because$ $1+\omega+\omega^{2}$ = 0]

Q9. If n is any integer, then i^n is
    (A) -i
    (B) 1, -1
    (C) 1, -1, i, -i   <-- CORRECT
    (D) i
    Answer: C
    Explanation: i^0 = 1, i^1 = i, i^2 = -1, i^3 = i^2.i = -i
Now we can see for n = 0, 4, 8....... the value of i^n = 1
For n = 1, 5, 9....... the value of i^n = i
For n = 2, 6, 10....... the value of i^n = -1 
For n = 3, 7, 11....... the value of i^n = -i
Similarly for all negative integers also n takes any one value among 1, -1, i, -i

Q10. The points z = x + iy which satisfy the equation |z| = 1 lie on
    (A) the line x = 1
    (B) the line y = 1
    (C) the circle whose centre is origin and radius = 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the line x + y = 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: z = x + iy
Now |z| = 1 $\Rightarrow$ |x + iy| = 1
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$ = 1 $\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 = 1
Which is the equation of a circle whose centre is origin and radius = 1

Q11. The equation z^2 = $ \bar z$ has
    (A) two solutions   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a unique solution
    (C) four solutions
    (D) no solution
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy
z^2 = $\bar z$ $\Rightarrow$ (x + iy)^2 = x - iy 
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 - y^2 + 2xyi = x - iy
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 - y^2 = x .....(i) and 2xy = -y .....(ii)
From (ii) we get x = $\frac { -1 }{ 2 } $ 
Now from (i) we have y^2 = $\frac { 1 }{ 4 } +\frac { 1 }{ 2 } =\frac { 3 }{ 4 } \Rightarrow \pm \frac { \sqrt { 3 } }{ 2 } $ 
Hence z = $\frac { -1 }{ 2 } \pm i\frac { \sqrt { 3 } }{ 2 } $

Q12. The points of the complex plane given by the condition arg. (z) = (2n + 1) $\pi $, n $\in $ I lie on
    (A) the negative real semi axis z = x, x < 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the positive real semi axis z = x, x > 0
    (C) the imaginary semi axis z = iy, y > 0
    (D) the imaginary semi axis z = iy, y < 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy then value of $\theta$ which satisfies the equation $tan\theta =\frac { y }{ x } $ is called an argument or amplitude.
Then Arg (z)= $\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left( \frac { y }{ x } \right) } $ 
Now arg. (z) = (2n + 1) $\pi $ $\Rightarrow\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left( \frac { y }{ x } \right) } = ( 2n + 1 ) \pi$ 
$\Rightarrow$ tan (2n + 1)$\pi $ = $\frac{y}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{\sin (2 n+1) \pi}{\cos (2 n+1) \pi}$ = $\frac{y}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{0}{(-1)^{2 n+1}}$ = $\frac{y}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{0}{-1}$ = $\frac{y}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ -y = 0
Hence the points lie on the negative real semi-axis z = x, x < 0

Q13. If z = x + yi ; x ,y $\in $ R, then locus of the equation $\bar bz + b\overline {z} = c$, where c $\in $ R and b $\in $ C, b $ \ne $ 0 are fixed, is
    (A) a straight line   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a circle
    (C) a parabola
    (D) a hyperbola
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let z_1 = $\bar{b} z$ then $\overline{z_{1}}=b \bar{z}$ 
Now $\bar{b} z+b \bar{z}$ = c $\Rightarrow$ $z_{1}+\overline{z_{1}}$ = c
$\Rightarrow$ 2Rez_1 = c $\Rightarrow$ Rez_1 = $\frac{c}{2}$ 
Which is a straight line.

Q14. The complex number z which satisfies the condition $\left|\frac{i+z}{i-z}\right|=1$, lies on
    (A) the line x + y =1
    (B) circle x^2 + y^2 = 1
    (C) the x - axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the y - axis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\left|\frac{i+z}{i-z}\right|=1$
$\Rightarrow|i+z|=|i-z|$
$\Rightarrow|i+x+i y|=|i-(x+i y)|$
$\Rightarrow \sqrt{(1+y)^2+x^2}=\sqrt{-(x)^2+(1-y)^2}$
$\Rightarrow(1+y)^2+x^2=-(x)^2+(1-y)^2$
$\Rightarrow y^2+2 y+1+x^2=x^2+y^2-2 y+1$
$\Rightarrow$ 4y = 0
$\Rightarrow$ y = 0
which is the X-axis.

Q15. (1 + i)^2n + (1 - i)^2n, n $ \in$ N, is
    (A) a purely imaginary number
    (B) a real complex number
    (C) a purely real number   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a non-real complex number
    Answer: C
    Explanation: (1 + i)^2n + (1 - i)^2n = [(1 + i)^2]^n + [(1 - i)^2]^n = [1 + 2i - 1]^n + [1 - 2i - 1]^n = (2i)^n + (-2i)^n = 2^n[(i)n + (-i)n]
When n is an odd natural number say n = 2k + 1, (-i)^n = -(i)^2k+1 so that (i)^n + (-i)^n = (i)^2k+1 - (i)^2k+1 = 0
When n is an even natural number say n = 2k, (-i)^n = (-i)^2k = (i)^2k so that, (i)^n + (-i)^n = (i)^2k + (i)^2k = 2(i^2)^k = 2(-1)^k, k $\in$ N
Hence (1 + i)^2n + (1 - i)^2n is always a purely real number.

Q1. $A m p \cdot\left(\sin \frac{6 \pi}{5}+i\left(1+\cos \frac{6 \pi}{5}\right)\right)$ is equal to
    (A) $\frac {6\pi } {10}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac {6\pi } {5}$
    (C) $\frac {7\pi } {10}$
    (D) $\frac {5\pi }{ 6}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have for a complex number x + iy the argument or amplitude is a value of $\theta $ satisfying $tan\theta =\frac { y }{ x } $
z = x + it = $\sin \frac{6 \pi}{5}+i\left(1+\cos \frac{6 \pi}{5}\right)$
$\therefore \tan \theta=\frac{y}{x}$ $\Rightarrow \tan \theta=\frac{1+\cos \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{5}}{\sin \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{5}}=\frac{2 \cos ^2 \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{10}}{2 \sin \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{10} \cos \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{10}}=\tan \frac{6 \mathrm{\pi}}{10}$ $\left[\because 1+\cos \theta=2 \cos ^2 \frac{\theta}{2}, \sin \theta=2 \sin \frac{\theta}{2} \cos \frac{\theta}{2}\right]$
$\Rightarrow \theta=\frac{6 \pi}{10}$

Q2. If z = $\frac{\sqrt{3}+i}{2}$, then z^69 is equal to
    (A) 1
    (B) -1
    (C) i
    (D) -i   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given z = $\frac{\sqrt{3}+i}{2}$ 
iz = $i\left[\frac{\sqrt{3}+i}{2}\right]$ = $\frac{-1+i \sqrt{3}}{2}=\omega$ 
$\Rightarrow$ z = $\frac{\omega}{i}$ 
Then z^69 = $\left[\frac{\omega}{i}\right]^{69}$ = $\frac{\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{23}}{\left(i^{2}\right)^{34} \cdot i}$ = $\frac{1}{(-1)^{34} . i}=\frac{1}{i}$ = -i [$\because$ $\omega^3$ = 1, i^2 = -1]

Q3. If $\omega $ is a cube root of unity, then the linear factors of x^3 + y^3 in complex numbers are
    (A) (x + y)(x + y$\omega$)(x - y$\omega^2$)
    (B) (x - y) (x + y$\omega$) (x + y$\omega^2$)
    (C) (x + y)(x + y$\omega$)(x + y$\omega^2$)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (x + y)(x - y$\omega$)(x - y$\omega^2$)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have x^3 + y^3 = (x + y)(x^2 - xy + y^2)
Now consider x^2 - yx + y^2 = 0 which is a quadratic equation in x with a = 1, b = -y and c = y^2
Hence the roots are 
x = $\frac{-(-y) \pm \sqrt{(-y)^{2}-4 \cdot 1 \cdot y^{2}}}{2 \cdot 1}$ = $\frac{y \pm \sqrt{-3 y^{2}}}{2}$ = $\frac{y \pm i y \sqrt{3}}{2}$ = $\frac{y(1 \pm i \sqrt{3})}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x = y$\omega$ or y$\omega^2$ 
Hence, x^3 + y^3 = (x + y)(x^2 - xy + y^2) = (x + y)(x + y$\omega$)(x + y$\omega^2$)

Q4. $\left( {z + 1} \right)\left( {\overline z + 1} \right)$ can be expressed as
    (A) |z + 1|^2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) |z|^2 + 1
    (C) |z|^2 + 2
    (D) |z + 2|^2
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have $z\bar { z } ={ \left| z \right| ^{ 2 } }$ 
Now $\left( { z+1 } \right) \left( { \overline { z } +1 } \right) =\left( { z+1 } \right) \left( \overline { z+1 } \right) $ = |z + 1|^2

Q5. If $\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $ are non-real cube roots of unity then $\alpha \beta $ + ${\alpha ^5} + {\beta ^5}$ equals
    (A) -1
    (B) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If $\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $ are non-real cube roots of unity then we have either $\alpha=\omega, \beta=\omega^{2}$ or $\alpha=\omega^{2}, \beta=\omega$ 
$\alpha=\omega, \beta=\omega^{2}$ $\Rightarrow$ $\alpha^{5}+\beta^{5}+\alpha \cdot \beta$ = $\omega^{5}+\left(\omega^{2}\right)^{5}+\omega \cdot \omega^{2}$ = $\omega^{3} \cdot \omega^{2}+\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{3} \cdot \omega^{1}+\omega^{3}$ = $1 . \omega^{2}+1 . \omega+1$ = 0
$\alpha=\omega^{2}, \beta=\omega$ $\Rightarrow$ $\alpha^{5}+\beta^{5}+\alpha . \beta$ = $\left(\omega^{2}\right)^{5}+\omega^{5}+\omega . \omega^{2}$ = $\left(\omega^{3}\right)^{3} \cdot \omega^{1}+\omega^{3} \cdot \omega^{2}+\omega^{3}$ = $1 . \omega+1 . \omega^{2}+1$ = 0 [$\because$ $\omega^{3}=1,1+\omega+\omega^{2}=0$ ]

Q6. The complex numbers z = x + iy; x , y $\in $ R which satisfy the equation $\left|\frac{z-3 i}{z+3}\right|=1$ lies on
    (A) the line parallel to y axis
    (B) the y axis
    (C) the line x + y = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) the x axis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let z=x+iy
Now $\left|\frac{z-3 i}{z+3}\right|=1$
$\Rightarrow|z-3 i|=|z+3|$
$\Rightarrow|(x+i y)-3 i|=|x+i y+3|$
$\Rightarrow|x+i(y-3)|=|(x+3)+i y|$
$\Rightarrow \sqrt{(y-3)^{2}+x^{2}}=\sqrt{(x+3)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$
$\Rightarrow(y-3)^{2}+x^{2}=(x+3)^{2}+(y)^{2}$
$\Rightarrow y^{2}-6 y+9+x^{2}=x^{2}+6 x+9+y^{2}$
$\Rightarrow 6 x+6 y=0$
$\Rightarrow x+y=0$

Q7. If z_1 = 2+3i and z_2 = 5+2i, then find z_1-z_2.
    (A) 3-i
    (B) 7+5i
    (C) 7-5i
    (D) -3+1i   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: In subtracting one complex number from other, difference of corresponding parts of two complex numbers is calculated. So,
z_1-z_2 will be:
= (2-5) + (3-2) i
= -3+1i.

Q8. If z = $\bar z$, then
    (A) z is purely imaginary
    (B) z is purely real   <-- CORRECT
    (C) z is a complex number
    (D) z is a whole number
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy
Now z = $\bar{z} \Rightarrow$ x + iy = x - iy $\Rightarrow$ 2iy = 0 $\Rightarrow$ y = 0
Which means z is purely real.

Q9. The complex number $\frac{(1+i)^n}{(1-i)^{n-2}}$ is equal to
    (A) $2{i^{n - 2}}$
    (B) $2{i^{n - 1}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $4{i^{n - 2}}$
    (D) $2{i^{n - 4}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\frac { { \left( { 1+i } \right) }^{ n } }{ { \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ n-2 } } =\frac { { \left( { 1+i } \right) }^{ n } }{ { \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ n }.{ \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ -2 } } =\frac { { \left( { 1+i } \right) }^{ n }.{ \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ 2 } }{ { \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ n } } $ $={ \left( \frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } \right) }^{ n }.{ \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ 2 }$
Now $\frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } =\frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } .\frac { 1+i }{ 1+i } =\frac { { \left( { 1+i } \right) }^{ 2 } }{ 1+1 } =\frac { 1-1+2i }{ 1+1 } =\frac { 2i }{ 2 } =i$
$\therefore \frac { { \left( { 1+i } \right) }^{ n } }{ { \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ n-2 } } $ $={ i }^{ n }.{ \left( { 1-i } \right) }^{ 2 }={ i }^{ n }.\left( 1-1-2i \right) =-2i.{ i }^{ n }=-2{ i }^{ n+1 }$ $=-2.{ i }^{ 2 }.{ { i }^{ n-1 } }=-2.-1.{ { i }^{ n-1 } }=2.{ { i }^{ n-1 } }$

Q10. The least value of n for which ${ \left( \frac { 1+i }{ 1-i } \right) }^{ n }$ is a positive integer is
    (A) 8
    (B) 1
    (C) 2
    (D) 4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\frac{1+i}{1-i}$ = $\frac{1+i}{1-i} \cdot \frac{1+i}{1+i}$ = $\frac{(1+i)^{2}}{1+1}=\frac{1-1+2 i}{1+1}=\frac{2 i}{2}$ = i
$\therefore$ $\left(\frac{1+i}{1-i}\right)^{n}$ = i^n 
We have i^4 = 1 which is positive.
Hence the least value of n is 4.

Q11. If (x + iy)(p + iq) = (x^2 + y^2)i, then
    (A) p = x, q = y
    (B) p = ix, q = 0
    (C) p = y, q = x   <-- CORRECT
    (D) p = 0, q = ix
    Answer: C
    Explanation: (x + iy)(p + iq) = (x^2 + y^2)i 
$\Rightarrow$ (xp - yq) + i(xq + yp) = (x^2 + y^2)i 
$\Rightarrow$ xp - yp = 0 and xq = + yp = x^2 + y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ p = $\frac{y q}{x}$ ....(i) and xq + yp = x^2 + y^2 ...(ii)
Substituting (i) in (ii), we get 
xq + $y\left(\frac{y q}{x}\right)$ = x^2 + y^2 $\Rightarrow$ x^2q + y^2q = x(x^2 + y^2)
$\Rightarrow$ q(x^2 + y^2) = x(x^2 + y^2) $\Rightarrow$ q = x
Now from (i), we get p = y

Q12. If z = x + yi and w = $\frac{1-i z}{z-i}$, then |w| = 1 implies that, in the complex plane
    (A) z lies on the imaginary axis
    (B) z lies on the unit circle
    (C) z lies on the unit square
    (D) z lies on the real axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\left| { { w } } \right| =1\Rightarrow \left| \frac { 1-iz }{ z-i } \right| =1$
$\Rightarrow \left| { { 1-iz } } \right| =\left| { { z-i } } \right|$
$\Rightarrow \left| { { 1-i\left( x+iy \right) } } \right| =\left| { \left( x+iy \right) -i } \right|$
$\Rightarrow \left| { { \left( 1+y \right) -ix } } \right| =\left| { { x+i\left( y-1 \right) } } \right|$
$\Rightarrow \sqrt { { \left( 1+y \right) }^{ 2 }+{ \left( x \right) }^{ 2 } } =\sqrt { { \left( y-1 \right) }^{ 2 }+{ \left( x \right) }^{ 2 } }$
$\Rightarrow { \left( 1+y \right) }^{ 2 }+{ \left( x \right) }^{ 2 }={ \left( y-1 \right) }^{ 2 }+{ \left( x \right) }^{ 2 }$
$ \Rightarrow 1+{ y }^{ 2 }+2y+{ x }^{ 2 }=1+{ y }^{ 2 }-2y+{ x }^{ 2 }$
$\Rightarrow y=0$
Which is the real axis.

Q13. If p^2 + p + 1 = 0, then, the value of p^3n is equal to
    (A) 1
    (B) -1
    (C) 0
    (D) 1 or -1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: p^2 + p + 1 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ p = $\frac{-(1) \pm \sqrt{1^{2}-4 \cdot 1 \cdot 1}}{2}$ = $\frac{-1 \pm \sqrt{-3}}{2}=\frac{-1 \pm \sqrt{3} i}{2}=\omega, \omega^{2}$ 
Now p = $\omega$ $\Rightarrow$ p^3n = $(\omega^3)^n$ = 1^n = 1 or -1, depending n is even or odd
Also p = $\omega^2$ $\Rightarrow$ p^3n = $(\omega^2)^{3n}$ = $(\omega^3)^{2n}$ = 1^2n = 1
Hence p = 1, -1

Q14. The solution of the equation |z| = z + 1 + 2i is
    (A) $\frac{3}{2}$ - 2i   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{3}{2}$ + 2i
    (C) 3 + 2i
    (D) 3 – 2i
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy
Now 
|z| = z + 1 + 2i
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$ $\Rightarrow$ x + 1 + i(y + 2)
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}}$ = x + 1 and y + 2 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ y = -2 and x^2 + 4 = (x + 1)^2 
$\Rightarrow$ y = -2 and x = $\frac{3}{2}$ 
Hence z = $\frac{3}{2}$ - 2i

Q15. a + ib $ \leq $ c + id is meaningful only when
    (A) b^2 + d^2 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) b^2 + c^2 = 0
    (C) a^2 + d^2 = 0
    (D) a^2 + b^2 = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have in the complex numbers system it is meaningless to say one is smaller or bigger than the other since the order relation does not exist in complex numbers.
So a + ib $ \leq$ c + id will be meaningful only when these numbers are real which means their imaginary parts are zero.
$\Rightarrow$ b = 0 and d = 0 $\Rightarrow$ b^2 + d^2 = 0

Quadratic Equations Test 05  (id 626) [PAID]

Q1. Square roots of i are
    (A) $\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(1-i)$
    (B) -1
    (C) $\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(1+i)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $ \pm 1$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let $\sqrt { i }$ = x + iy
Squaring both sides, we get
i = (x + iy)^2 = x^2 - y^2 + 2xyi 
Subtracting (i) from (iii), we get
2y^2 = 1 $\Rightarrow$ y^2 = $\frac{1}{2}$ $\Rightarrow$ y = $\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$ 
Comparing real and imaginary parts, we get x^2 - y^2 = 0 ....(i) and 2xy = 1
We have (x^2 - y^2)^2 = (x^2 + y^2)^2 - 4x^2y^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 0 = (x^2 + y^2)^2 - (2xy)^2 = (x^2 + y^2)^2 - 1
$\Rightarrow$ (x^2 + y^2)^2 = 1
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 = 1 .....(iii)
Adding (i) and (iii) we get 
2x^2 = 1 $\Rightarrow$ x^2 = $\frac{1}{2}$ $\Rightarrow$ x = $\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$ 
Hence $\sqrt { i }$ = x + iy = $\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}(1+i)$

Q2. The value of $\frac{1}{1+\omega}+\frac{1}{1+\omega^2}$ =
    (A) -1
    (B) 2
    (C) 0
    (D) 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $1,\omega ,{ \omega }^{ 2 }$ are the three cube roots of unity and we have $1+\omega +{ \omega }^{ 2 }=0 , { \omega }^{ 3 }=1$
${1 \over {1 + \omega }} + {1 \over {1 + {\omega ^2}}} = $$ {1 \over { - {\omega ^2}}}+{1 \over {-\omega }} = $ $-1\left(\frac{1}{\omega^{2}}+\frac{1}{\omega}\right)=-1\left(\frac{\omega+\omega^{2}}{\omega^{2} \cdot \omega}\right)$ = $-1\left(\frac{-1}{\omega^{3}}\right)=\frac{1}{\omega^{3}}=1$ [$\because$ $\omega+\omega^{2}=-1, \omega^{3}=1$]

Q3. The values of x and y $\in $ R for which the numbers -3 + x^2yi, x^2 + y + 4i are conjugates of each other are
    (A) -1, -4
    (B) -1, 4
    (C) 1, -4
    (D) $ \pm 1, - 4$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let z_1 = -3 + x^2yi and z_2 = x^2 + y + 4i $\Rightarrow$ $\bar z_{1}$ = -3 - x^2yi, $\bar z_{2}$ = x^2 + y - 4i
Given the numbers are conjugates of each other $\overline{z_{1}}=z_{2}$ and $\overline{z_{2}}=z_{1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ -3 - x^2yi = x^2 + y + 4i and x^2 + y - 4i = -3 + x^2yi
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y = -3 and x^2y = -4
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-4}{y}$ + y = -3
$\Rightarrow$ y^2 + 3y - 4 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ (y + 4)(y - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ y = 1, -4
When y = 1 we get x^2 = 4 $\Rightarrow$ x = $\pm \sqrt{-4}=\pm 2 i$, which is not possible since given x is a real number.
When y = $-4$ we get $x^{ 2 }=1\Rightarrow x=\pm \sqrt { 1 } =\pm 1 $ 
Hence the possible values of x and y are $\pm 1,-4$

Q4. If $x = {\omega ^2} - \omega - 3,\omega $ being a non real cube root of unity, then the value of x^4 + 6x^3 + 10x^2 - 12x - 19 is
    (A) 12
    (B) 19
    (C) 5   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 17
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x = $\omega^{2}-\omega-3$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x + 3 $=\omega^{2}-\omega$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 6x + 9 = $\omega^{4}-2 \omega^{3}+\omega^{2}$ = $\omega-2+\omega^{2}$ = -3
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 6x + 12 = 0
Now x^4 + 6x^3 + 10x^2 - 12x - 19 = (x^2 - 2)(x^2 + 6x + 12) + 5 = (x^2 - 2) $\times$ 0 + 5 = 5

Q5. Square roots of - 48 – 14i are
    (A) (1 - 7i)
    (B) (1 + 7i)
    (C) $ \pm (1 - 7i$)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $ \pm (1 + 7i$)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have $\sqrt{z}=\sqrt{x+i y}$ = $\pm[\sqrt{\frac{|z|+x}{2}}-i \sqrt{\frac{|z|-x}{2}}]$, for y < 0
Now consider z = -48 - 14i
Here Re z = -48, Im z < 0 and |z| = $\sqrt{(-48)^{2}+(-14)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{2304+196}$ = $\sqrt{2500}$ = 50 
$\therefore$ $\sqrt{-48-14 i}$ = $\pm[\sqrt{\frac{50+(-48)}{2}}-i \sqrt{\frac{50-(-48)}{2}}]$ 
= $\pm[\sqrt{\frac{50-48}{2}}-i \sqrt{\frac{50+48}{2}}]$ = $\pm[1-i \sqrt{49}]$ = $\pm$ [1 - 7i]

Q6. The region of Argand’s plane represented by the inequality |1 - z| $\leq $ |1 + z| is
    (A) Re (z) $≥$ 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) Im (z) > 0
    (C) Re (z) $≤ $0
    (D) Im (z) < 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let Z = x + iy
Given |1 - z| $ \leq$ |1 + z| 
$\Rightarrow$ |1 - (x + iy)| $ \leq$ |1 + x + iy|
$\Rightarrow$ |(1 - x) - iy| $ \leq$ |(1 + x) + iy|
$\Rightarrow$ $\sqrt{(1-x)^{2}+y^{2}}$ $ \leq$ $\sqrt{(1+x)^{2}+(y)^{2}}$ 
Squaring on both sides we get 
(1 - x)^2 + y^2 $ \leq$ (1 + x)^2 + (y)^2 
$\Rightarrow$ 1 + x^2 - 2x + y^2 $ \leq$ 1 + x^2 + 2x + y^2
$\Rightarrow$ -2x $ \leq$ 2x 
$\Rightarrow$ 4x $ \geq$ 0
$\Rightarrow$ x $ \geq$ 0
Hence we get x = Re (z) $≥$ 0

Q7. If z is purely real and Re ( z) > 0, then Amp. (z) is
    (A) $\pi $
    (B) - $\pi $
    (C) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: To find the amplitude of a complex number Z = x + iy first find a value of $\theta $ which satisfy the equation $\theta =\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { y }{ x } \right| } ,0\le \theta \le \frac { \Pi }{ 2 } $ 
Now depending on the complex number lies in the first, second, third or fourth quadrants the amplitudes will be $\theta ,\left( \Pi -\theta \right) ,-\left( \Pi -\theta \right) ,-\left( \theta \right) $ respectively.
Given z is purely real and Re (z) > 0
$\therefore$ Z = x + 0i, x > 0
Now $\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { y }{ x } \right| } =\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { 0 }{ 1 } \right| } $ = tan^-1 0 = 0
Also Z = x + 0i, x > 0 lies in the first quadrant 
Hence Amp(Z) = 0

Q8. If z is purely real and Re(z) < 0, then Arg.(z) is
    (A) $\pi $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0
    (C) 1
    (D) -$\pi $
    Answer: A
    Explanation: To find the amplitude of a complex number Z = x + iy first find a value of $\theta $ which satisfy the equation $\theta =\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { y }{ x } \right| } ,0\le \theta \le \frac { \Pi }{ 2 } $ 
Now depending on the complex number lies in the first, second, third or fourth quadrants the amplitudes will be $\theta ,\left( \Pi -\theta \right) ,-\left( \Pi -\theta \right) ,-\left( \theta \right) $ respectively.
Given z is purely real and Re (z) $<$ 0
$\therefore$ Z = -x + 0i, x > 0
Now $\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { y }{ x } \right| } =\tan ^{ -1 }{ \left| \frac { 0 }{ -1 } \right| }$ = tan^-1 0 = 0
Also Z = -x + 0i, x > 0 lies in the second quadrant.
Hence Amp(Z) = $\Pi -\theta =\Pi -0=\Pi $

Q9. Find argument of the complex number (0 + 0i)
    (A) 0
    (B) $\pi $
    (C) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -$\pi $
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let Z = 0 + 0i = $r\left( cos\theta +isin\theta \right) $ 
Then comparing the real and imaginary parts, we get 
r cos $\theta$ = 0 and r sin $\theta$ = 0
$\therefore$ r^2 (cos^2 $\theta$ + sin^2 $\theta$) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^2 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ r = 0
$\Rightarrow$ cos $\theta$ = 0 and sin $\theta$ = 0 
Which is not possible for any value of $\theta$.

Q10. Find the Amplitude of i
    (A) $\frac \pi 2$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0
    (C) -$\frac \pi 2$
    (D) $\frac \pi 4$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let Z = i = $r\left( cos\theta +isin\theta \right) $ 
Then comparing the real and imaginary parts, we get
r cos $\theta$ = 0 and r sin $\theta$ = 1
$\therefore$ r^2(cos^2 $\theta$ + sin^2 $\theta$) = 1
$\Rightarrow$ r^2 = 1 $\Rightarrow$ r = 1
$\therefore$ cos $\theta$ = 0 and sin $\theta$ = 1 $\left[ cos\left( \frac { \Pi }{ 2 } \right) = 0, sin\left( \frac { \Pi }{ 2 } \right) =1 \right] $ [Format of amplitude is $\left( \Pi -\theta \right) $in the second quadrant]
Since $\theta$ lies in the second quadrant, we have the principal value of the argument (Amplitude) = $\left( \Pi -\theta \right) =\left( \Pi -\frac { \Pi }{ 2 } \right) =\frac { \Pi }{ 2 }$

Q11. 1/z is _________________ for complex number z.
    (A) additive identity element
    (B) multiplicative inverse   <-- CORRECT
    (C) additive inverse
    (D) multiplicative identity element
    Answer: B
    Explanation: multiplicative inverse
On multiplying reciprocal of complex number (1/z) to complex number z, we get multiplying inverse one i.e. z*1=z.

Q12. Find the Amplitude of -1 - i
    (A) $\frac{\pi}{4}$
    (B) $\frac{-3\pi}{4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{\pi}{2}$
    (D) $\frac{3\pi}{4}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let Z = -1 - i = $r\left( cos\theta +isin\theta \right) $ 
Then comparing the real and imaginary parts, we get
r cos $\theta$ = -1 and r sin $\theta$ = -1
$\therefore$ r^2(cos^2 $\theta$ + sin^2 $\theta$) = 2
$\Rightarrow$ r^2 = 2 $\Rightarrow$ r = $\sqrt{2}$ 
$\therefore$ $\sqrt{2} \cos \theta$ = -1 and $\sqrt{2} \sin \theta$ = -1
$\Rightarrow$ $\cos \theta=\frac{-1}{\sqrt{2}}$ and $\sin \theta=\frac{-1}{\sqrt{2}}$ [$\operatorname{cos}\left(\frac{\pi}{4}\right)=\sin \left(\frac{\pi}{4}\right)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$]
Since both sin $\theta$ and cos $\theta$ are negative and we have sin $\theta$ and cos $\theta$ are negative in the third quardrant, the principal value of the argument (Amplitude) = $-\left( \pi -\frac { \pi }{ 4 } \right) =-\frac { 3\pi }{ 4 } $

Q13. If z is any complex number, then $\frac{z-\bar{z}}{2 i}$ is
    (A) either 0 or purely imaginary
    (B) either 0 or purely real
    (C) purely imaginary
    (D) purely real   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let z = x + iy
Then $\bar {z }$ = x - iy
$\therefore$ z - $\bar { z}$ = (x + iy) - (x - iy) = 2iy
Now $\frac{z-\bar{z}}{2 i}$ = y
Hence $\frac{z-\bar{z}}{2 i}$ is purely real.

Q14. Which of the following is correct ?
    (A) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ${\text{2 }} + {\text{ 3i }} < {\text{ 3 }} + {\text{ 4i}}$
    (C) ${\text{3 }} - {\text{4i }} < {\text{ 2 }}-{\text{ 3i}}$
    (D) ${\text{1 }} + {\text{i }} < {\text{ 1}} - {\text{ i}}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: There is no linear ordering in the set of complex numbers.Hence it is not possible to say one complex number is smaller or bigger than the other

Linear Inequalities Test 01  (id 627) [FREE]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Identify the solution set for –( x – 3 ) < 5 – 2x
    (A) $( - \infty , 2)$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $( - \infty , - 1)$
    (C) $( - \infty , - 5)$
    (D) $( - \infty , - 2)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $-(x-3)<5-2 x$
$\Rightarrow-x+3<5-2 x$
$\Rightarrow-x+3+x<5-2 x+x$
$\Rightarrow 3<5-x$
$\Rightarrow 3-5<5-x-5$
$\Rightarrow-2<-x$
$\Rightarrow x \in(-\infty, 2)$

Q2. What is the solution set for $\frac{2(x-1)}{5} \leq \frac{3(2+x)}{7}$?
    (A) $( - 4,\infty )$
    (B) $[ - 44,\infty )$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $( - 12,\infty )$
    (D) $( - 24,\infty )$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given $\frac{2(x-1)}{5} \leq \frac{3(2+x)}{7}$ 
Multiplying both sides by LCM (5, 7) = 35, we get
$35 \cdot \frac{2(x-1)}{5} \leq 35 \cdot \frac{3(2+x)}{7}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 14(x - 1) $\le$ 15(2 + x)
$\Rightarrow$ 14x - 14 $\le$ 30 + 15x
$\Rightarrow$ 14x - 15x $\le$ 30 + 14
$\Rightarrow$ -x $\le$ 44
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ -44
Solution set is $\left[ -44,\infty \right) $

Q3. Identify the solution set for $\frac{(x-1)}{3}+4<\frac{(x-5)}{5}-2$
    (A) $( - \infty , - 50)$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) ($ - \infty $,-10)
    (C) $( - \infty , - 15)$
    (D) $( - \infty , - 5)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\frac{(x-1)}{3}+4<\frac{(x-5)}{5}-2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x-1+12}{3}<\frac{x-5-10}{5}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x+11}{3}<\frac{x-15}{5}$
Multiplying both sides by LCM (3, 5) = 15, we get
$\Rightarrow$ 5(x + 11) < 3(x - 15)
$\Rightarrow$ 5x + 55 < 3x - 45
$\Rightarrow$ 2x < -100
$\Rightarrow$ x < -50
So solution set is$( - \infty , - 50)$

Q4. What is the solution set for $\frac{2 x-3}{3 x-7}>0$?
    (A) $\left(-\infty,-\frac{1}{2}\right) \cup\left(\frac{7}{3}, \infty\right)$
    (B) $\left(-\infty,-\frac{3}{2}\right) \cup\left(\frac{5}{3}, \infty\right)$
    (C) $\left(-\infty, \frac{3}{2}\right) \cup\left(\frac{7}{3}, \infty\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\left(-\infty,-\frac{3}{2}\right) \cup\left(\frac{7}{4}, \infty\right)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\frac{2 x-3}{3 x-7}>0$
$\Rightarrow$ (2x - 3 > 0 and 3x - 7 > 0) or (2x - 3 < 0 and 3x - 7 < 0)
$\Rightarrow$ (x > $\frac { 3 }{ 2 }$ and x > $\frac { 7 }{ 3 }$) or (x < $\frac { 3 }{ 2 }$ and x < $\frac { 7 }{ 3 }$)
$\Rightarrow x>\frac { 7 }{ 3 }$ or $x<\frac { 3 }{ 2 }$
$\Rightarrow x\in \left( \frac { 7 }{ 3 } ,\infty \right) $ or $x\in \left( -\infty ,\frac { 3 }{ 2 } \right)$
Hence the solution set is $\left(-\infty, \frac{3}{2}\right) \cup\left(\frac{7}{3}, \infty\right)$

Q5. Identify the solution set for $\frac{7 x-5}{8 x+3}>4$
    (A) $\left(-\frac{25}{28},-\frac{3}{8}\right)$
    (B) $\left(-\frac{5}{7},-\frac{3}{8}\right)$
    (C) $\left(-\frac{17}{25},-\frac{3}{8}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\left(-\frac{31}{28},-\frac{3}{8}\right)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\frac{7 x-5}{8 x+3}>4$
$\Rightarrow \frac{7 x-5}{8 x+3}-4>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{7 x-5-4(8 x+3)}{8 x+3}>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{7 x-5-32 x-12}{8 x+3}>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{-(25 x+17)}{8 x+3}>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{(25 x+17)}{8 x+3}<0$
$\Rightarrow$ (25x + 17 > 0 and 8x + 3 < 0) or (25x + 17 < 0 and 8x + 3 > 0)
[$\because$ $\frac{a}{b}<0$ $\Rightarrow$ (a > 0 and b < 0) or (a < 0 and b > 0)]
$\Rightarrow\left(x>\frac{-17}{25} \text { and } x<\frac{-3}{8} \right)$ or $\left(x<\frac{-17}{25} \text { and } x>\frac{-3}{8}\right)$
$\Rightarrow \frac{-17}{25}<x<\frac{-3}{8}$ [Since x < $\frac{-17}{25}$ and x > $\frac{-3}{8}$ is not possible]

Q6. What is the solution set for $0<\frac{-x}{2}<3$
    (A) (-6, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (5, 6)
    (C) (-5, 6)
    (D) (-6, 6)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $0<\frac{-x}{2}<3$ 
Multiplying throughout by 2, we get
0 < -x < 6
$\Rightarrow$ 0 > x > -6
So solution set is (-6, 0)

Q7. Identify solution set for |4 - x| + 1 < 3?
    (A) (3, 6)
    (B) (2, 4)
    (C) (2, 6)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (2, 3)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: |4 - x| + 1 < 3
$\Rightarrow$ |4 - x| < 2
$\Rightarrow$ -2 < 4 - x < 2
$\Rightarrow$ -2 - 4 < -x < 2 - 4
$\Rightarrow$ -6 < -x < -2
$\Rightarrow$ 6 > x > 2
$\Rightarrow$ x $\in$ (2, 6)
So solution set is (2, 6)

Q8. What is the solution set for $\frac{|x-2|}{x-2}>0$?
    (A) (2, $\infty $)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (-$\infty $, -2)
    (C) (0, 2)
    (D) (-$\infty $, 2)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have |x - 2| $\ge$ 0 [ $\because $ |x| or absolute value of x is always positive or zero but never negative]
Now $\frac{|x-2|}{x-2}>0$ $\Rightarrow $ x - 2 > 0 [$\because$ $\frac{a}{b}$ > 0, a $\ge$ 0 $\Rightarrow$ b > 0] 
$\Rightarrow $ x > 2 
$\Rightarrow x\epsilon \left( 2,\infty \right) $

Q9. Identify the solution set for $\frac{1}{|x|-3}<\frac{1}{2}$?
    (A) $(5,\infty )$
    (B) $(-5,\infty )$
    (C) $( - \infty , - 5)\mathop \cup \nolimits \left( { - 3,3} \right)\mathop \cup \nolimits (5,\infty )$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ($ - \infty , - 5)\mathop \cup \nolimits^ (5,\infty )$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\frac{1}{|x|-3}<\frac{1}{2}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{1}{|x|-3}-\frac{1}{2}<0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{2-|x|+3}{2(|x|-3)}<0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{5-|x|}{(|x|-3)}<0$
$\Rightarrow$ (5 - |x| < 0 and |x| - 3 > 0) or (5 - |x| > 0 and |x| - 3 < 0)
$\Rightarrow$ (|x| > 5 and |x| > 3) or (|x| < 5 and |x| < 3)
$\Rightarrow$ |x| > 5 or |x| < 3 [$\because$ |x| > a $\Rightarrow$ x < -a or x > a and |x| < a $\Rightarrow$ -a < x < a]
$\Rightarrow$ (x < -5 or x > 5) or -3 < x < 3
$\Rightarrow$ x $\epsilon$ ($-\infty$, -5) or x $\epsilon$ (5, $\infty$) or x $\epsilon$ (-3, 3)
$\Rightarrow x \epsilon(-\infty,-5) \cup(5, \infty) \cup(-3,3)$

Q10. What is the solution set for $\left|\frac{2 x-1}{x-1}\right|>2$ ?
    (A) $\left(-\frac{1}{4}, 1\right) \cup(-1, \infty)$
    (B) $\left(-\frac{3}{4}, 1\right) \cup(1, \infty)$
    (C) $\left(\frac{3}{4}, 1\right) \cup(1, \infty)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\left(\frac{1}{4}, 1\right) \cup(1, \infty)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\left|\frac{2 x-1}{x-1}\right|>2$
$\Rightarrow { { { \frac { 2x-1 }{ x-1 } >2 } } }\quad or\quad \frac { 2x-1 }{ x-1 } <-2\quad \quad \quad \quad \quad \left[ \because \left| x \right| >a\Rightarrow x<-a\quad or\quad x>a \right] $
First consider $ \frac { 2x-1 }{ x-1 } >2$
$ \frac { 2x-1 }{ x-1 } -2>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{2 x-1-2(x-1)}{x-1}>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{2 x-1-2 x+2}{x-1}>0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{1}{x-1}>0$
$\Rightarrow x-1>0$
$\Rightarrow x>1$
$\Rightarrow x \epsilon(1, \infty)$
Now $ \frac { 2x-1 }{ x-1 } <-2$
$\Rightarrow \frac{2 x-1}{x-1}+2<0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{2 x-1+2(x-1)}{x-1}<0$
$\Rightarrow \frac{4 x-3}{x-1}<0$
$\Rightarrow(4 x-3>0 \text { and } x-1<0) \text { or }(4 x-3<0 \text { and } x-1>0)$
$\left[\because \frac{a}{b}<0 \Rightarrow(a>0 \text { and } b<0) \quad \text { or } \quad(a<0 \text { and } \quad b>0)\right]$
$\Rightarrow\left(x>\frac{3}{4} \quad \text { and } \quad x<1 \quad\right) \quad \text { or } \quad\left(x<\frac{3}{4} \quad \text { and } \quad x>1\right)$
$\left[\text { Since } \quad x<\frac{3}{4} \quad \text { and } \quad x>1 \text { is } \quad \text { not } \quad \text { possible }\right]$
$\Rightarrow x \in\left(\frac{3}{4}, 1\right)$

Q11. In the first three papers each of 100 marks , Rishi got 95 , 72 , 83 marks . If he wants an average of greater than or equal to 75 marks and less than 80 marks, find the range of marks he should score in the 4th paper .
    (A) 75 $ < {\text{ }} \times {\text{ }} < $80
    (B) $ 50 \le x \lt 70$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 25 $ < {\text{ }} \times {\text{ }} < $75
    (D) 73 $ < {\text{ }} \times {\text{ }} < $100
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the marks scored by Rishi in the fourth paper be x.
Then$75\le \frac { 95+72+83+x }{ 4 } <80$ 
$\\ \Rightarrow 75\le \frac { 250+x }{ 4 } <80$
Multipling the inequality throughout by 4 ,we get
$300\le 250+x<320$
$\\ \Rightarrow 300-250\le 250+x-250<320-250$
$\\ \Rightarrow 50\le x<70$

Q12. A man wants to cut three lengths from a single piece of board of length 91 cm. The second length is to be 3 cm longer than the shortest and third length is to be twice as long as the shortest. What are the possible lengths for the shortest board if the third piece is to be at least 5 cm longer than the second?
    (A) 8 $\le$ x $\le$ 22   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3 $\le$ x $\le$ 91
    (C) 3 $\le$ x $\le$ 5
    (D) 5 $\le$ x $\le$ 91
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let the length of the shortest piece be x cm. Then we have the length of the second and third pieces are x + 3 and 2x centimeters respectively.
According to the question,
x + (x + 3) + 2x $\le$ 91
$\Rightarrow$ 4x + 3 $\le$ 91
$\Rightarrow$ 4x $\le$ 88
$\Rightarrow$ x $\le$ 22
Also 2x $\ge$ (x + 3) + 5
$\Rightarrow$ 2x $\ge$ x + 8
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ 8
$\Rightarrow$ 8 $\le$ x $\le$ 22
Hence the shortest piece may be atleast 8 cm long but it cannot be more than 22cm in length.

Q13. Find all pairs of consecutive odd natural numbers, both of which are larger than 10, such that their sum is less than 40.
    (A) (11, 13), (13, 15), (15, 17), (17, 21)
    (B) (9, 11), (13, 15), (15, 17), (17, 19)
    (C) (11, 13), (13, 15), (15, 17), (17, 19)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (11, 13), (13, 15), (17, 19), (19, 21)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let the consecutive odd natural numbers be x and x + 2.
According to the question, x > 10 and x + (x + 2) < 40 
Now x + (x + 2) < 40 $\Rightarrow$ 2x < 38 $\Rightarrow$ x < 19
Hence the maximum value of x is 17 and minimum value is 11.
So the possible pairs of odd natural numbers are (11, 13), (13, 15), (15, 17), (17, 19)

Q14. The marks scored by Rohit in two tests were 65 and 70. Find the minimum marks he should score in the third test to have an average of atleast 65 marks.
    (A) 75
    (B) 60   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 65
    (D) 70
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Then
$\frac{65+70+x}{3} \geq 65$
$\Rightarrow 135+x \geq 195$
$\Rightarrow x \geq 60$
Hence Rohit should get a minimum of 60 marks to get an average of atleast 65 marks.

Q15. A solution is to be kept between 30^o C and 35^o C. What is the range of temperature in degree Fahrenheit. What is the range of temperature in degree Fahrenheit if conversion formula is given by C = $\frac { 5 }{ 9 } \left( F-32 \right) $ where C and F represent the temperature in degree Celcius and degree Fahrenheit?
    (A) Between 76^o F and 105^o F
    (B) Between 86^o F and 95^o F   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Between 40^o F and 60^o F
    (D) Between 30^o F and 35^o F
    Answer: B
    Explanation: According to the question 30 < C < 35
Since C = $\frac { 5 }{ 9 } \left( F-32 \right) $, we get 
30 < $\frac{5}{9}(F-32)$ < 35
$\Rightarrow$ $30 . \frac{9}{5}$ < (F - 32) < $35 . \frac{9}{5}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 54 < (F - 32) < 63
$\Rightarrow$ 54 + 32 < (F - 32) + 32 < 63 + 32
$\Rightarrow$ 80 < F < 95
Hence the range of temperature in degree Fahrenheit is between 86^o F and 95^o F

Q1. The longest side of a triangle is three times the shortest side and the third side is 2 cm shorter than the longest side if the perimeter of the triangles is at least 61 cm, find the minimum length of the shortest side.
    (A) 11 cm
    (B) 16 cm
    (C) 61 cm
    (D) 9 cm   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let the shortest side of a triangle be x cm. Then the length of the longest side is 3x cm and the length of the third side is (3x - 2) cm.
Given the perimeter of the triangles at least 61cm
$\Rightarrow$ x + 3x + (3x - 2) $\ge$ 61
$\Rightarrow$ 7x - 2 $\ge$ 61
$\Rightarrow$ 7x $\ge$ 63
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ 9 
Hence the minimum length of the shortest side = 9 cm

Q2. Which of the following is correct?
 If 0 > -7, then 0 < 7
 If -4 < 7, then 4 < - 7
 If 8 > 1, then -8 > -1
 If -2 < 5, then 2 > 5
    (A) C
    (B) B
    (C) D
    (D) A   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given 0 > -7
Multiplying throughout by -1, we get 0 < 7 [When both sides of an inequality are multiplied by a negative number, then the sign of inequality is reversed]

Q3. Solve the inequality 3 - 2x $ \leq$ 9
    (A) x $\ge$ -3   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x $ \leq$ -6
    (C) x $ \leq$ -3
    (D) x $\geq $ -6
    Answer: A
    Explanation: 3 - 2x $\le$ 9 
$\Rightarrow$ -2x $\le$ 9 - 3
$\Rightarrow$ -2x $\le$ 6
$\Rightarrow$ -x $\le$ 3
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ -3

Q4. Given that x is an integer, find the values of x which satisfy both 2x + 3 > 7and x + 4 < 10
    (A) 4
    (B) 3, 4, 5   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3
    (D) 4, 5
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 2x + 3 > 7 
$\Rightarrow$ 2x + 3 - 3 > 7 - 3
$\Rightarrow$ 2x > 4
$\Rightarrow$ x > 2
Since x is an integer the solution set = {x : x > 2, x $\in$ Z} = {3, 4, 5, 6, 7 .....}
Now x + 4 < 10
$\Rightarrow$ x + 4 - 4 < 10 - 4
$\Rightarrow$ x < 6
Since x is an integer the solution set = {x : x > 6, x $\in$ Z} = {.... -1, 0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5}
Hence the integer values which satisfy both the inequalities are {3, 4, 5, 6, 7 .....} $\cap$ {.... -1, 0, 1, 2, 3, 4, 5} = {3, 4, 5}

Q5. The solution for the simultaneous linear inequalities 2x - 3 $\leq$ 7 and -x $ \leq$ 2 is :
    (A) ${\text{ 2}} \leq {\text{x}} \leq {\text{5}}$
    (B) $ - {\text{ 2}} \leq {\text{x}} \leq {\text{5}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $ - {\text{ 1 }} < {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 2}}$
    (D) $ - {\text{ 5 }} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ }} - {\text{ 2}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 2x - 3 $ \leq$ 7 
$\Rightarrow$ 2x - 3 + 3 $ \leq$ 7 + 3
$\Rightarrow$ 2x $ \leq$ 10
$\Rightarrow$ x $ \leq$ 5
Now -x $ \leq$ 2
$\Rightarrow$ x $ \geq$ -2
Therefore the solution of the simultaneous linear equalities is $ - {\text{ 2}} \leq {\text{x}} \leq {\text{5}}$.

Q6. {4, 5, 6} is the solution set of
    (A) x $\ge$ 4 and x $\le$ 7, x $\in$ Z
    (B) x > 4 and x > 7, x $\in$ Z
    (C) x $\ge$ 4 and x < 7, x $\in$ N   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x > 4 and x < 7, x $\in$ Z
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x $\ge$ 4, x $\in$Z
$\Rightarrow$ x $\in$ {4, 5, 6, 7, 8, .....}
x < 7
$\Rightarrow$ x $\in$ {.... 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}
Hence solution set of the system is {4, 5, 6, 7, 8 ....} $\cap$ {...... 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}

Q7. What are the integer values of x which satisfy the inequalities x > -2 and x < 2?
    (A) -1, 0, 3, 4
    (B) - 1, 0, 1, 2, 3
    (C) - 1, 0, 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1, 2, 3, 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x > - 2 and x < 2
$\Rightarrow$ -2 < x < 2, x $\in$ Z
$\Rightarrow$ x = -1, 0, 1

Q8. Given that x is an integer, find the values of x which satisfy the simultaneous linear inequalities ${\text{2 }} + {\text{ x }} < {\text{ 6 and }} {\text{2}} - {\text{3x }} < {\text{ }} - {\text{ 1}}$.
    (A) 1 , 2 , 3
    (B) 1 , 2, 3, 4.
    (C) 2 , 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2 , 3, 4,
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have ${\text{2 }} + {\text{ x }} < {\text{ 6}}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 2 + x − 2 < 6 − 2 
$\Rightarrow x<4$ 
Now 
2 - 3x < -1
$\Rightarrow2-3x-2<-1-2$
$\Rightarrow$ -3x < -3
$\\ \\ \Rightarrow \frac { -3x }{ -3 } >\frac { -3 }{ -3 } $
$\Rightarrow $ x > 1
Hence the solution of the given system of equations is given by 1 < x < 4, $ x\in Z\quad $$\Rightarrow$ x = 2, 3

Q9. Solve : 30x < 200, when x is a natural number :
    (A) {2, 3, 4, 5, 6}
    (B) {4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9}
    (C) {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}   <-- CORRECT
    (D) {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7}
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 30x < 200
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{30 x}{30}<\frac{200}{30}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x < $\frac{20}{3}$ = $6\frac{2}{3}$, x $\in$ N
$\Rightarrow$ x = 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6

Q10. The solution set for: 3x - 7 > x + 3.
    (A) (- 5, $\infty $)
    (B) (5, -$\infty $)
    (C) (5, $\infty $)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (-5, 5)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 3x - 7 > x + 3
$\Rightarrow$ 3x - 7 + 7 > x + 3 + 7
$\Rightarrow$ 3x > x + 10
$\Rightarrow$ 2x > 10
$\Rightarrow$ x > 5

Q11. The solution set for (x + 3) + 4 > -2x + 5:
    (A) (- $\infty $, 2)
    (B) $\left( \frac { -2 }{ 3 } ,\infty \right) \quad \quad \quad $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (- $\infty $, - 2)
    (D) (2, $\infty $)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: (x + 3) + 4 > -2x + 5
$\Rightarrow$ x + 7 > -2x + 5
$\Rightarrow$ x + 7 + 2x > -2x + 5 + 2x
$\Rightarrow$ 3x + 7 > 5
$\Rightarrow$ 3x + 7 - 7 > 5 - 7
$\Rightarrow$ 3x > -2
$\Rightarrow$ x > $\frac{-2}{3}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $ x\in\left( \frac { -2 }{ 3 } ,\infty \right) $

Q12. Solve the system of inequalities 2x + 5 $\le$ 0, x - 3 $\le$ 0.
    (A) $ x ≥ - {\frac 52}$
    (B) $ x ≥ {\frac 52}$
    (C) $ x ≤ - {\frac 52}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $ x ≤ {\frac 52}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 2x + 5 $\le$ 0
$\Rightarrow$ 2x < -5
$\Rightarrow$ x $\le$ $\frac{-5}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $x \epsilon\left(-\infty, \frac{-5}{2}\right]$
Now x - 3 $\le$ 0
$\Rightarrow$ x $\le$ 3
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(-\infty, 3]$
Hence the solution set is $\left( -\infty ,\frac { -5 }{ 2 } \right] \cap { \left( -\infty ,3 \right] } $ = $\left( -\infty ,\frac { -5 }{ 2 } \right]$ 
$\Rightarrow$$ x ≤ - {\frac 52}$

Q13. Solve the system of inequalities x - 2 > 0, 3x < 18
    (A) -6 < x < -2
    (B) 3 < x < 18
    (C) 2 < x < 6   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1 < x < 3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x - 2 > 0
$\Rightarrow$ x > 2
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(2, \infty)$ 
Now 3x < 18
$\Rightarrow$ x < 6
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(-\infty, 6)$ 
So solution set is $\left( 2,\infty \right) \cap { \left( -\infty ,6 \right) }$ = (2, 6)
$\Rightarrow$ 2 < x < 6

Q14. Solve the system of inequalities ${\text{4x }} + {\text{ 3 }} \geq {\text{ 2x }} + {\text{ 17 }},{\text{ 3x }}-{\text{ 5 }} < {\text{ }} - {\text{ 2}}$ , for the values of x, then
    (A) $\left(-\frac{3}{2}, \frac{2}{5}\right)$
    (B) (-2, 2)
    (C) no solution   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $( - 4,12)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have given: $4 x+3 \geq 2 x+17$
$\Rightarrow 4 x-2 x \geq 17-3 \Rightarrow 2 x \geq 1$
$\Rightarrow x \geq \frac{14}{2}$ [Dividing by 2 on both sides]
$\Rightarrow$ $x \geq 7$ ..... (i)
Also we have 3x - 5 < -2
$\Rightarrow \quad 3 x<-2+5 \Rightarrow 3 x<3$
$\Rightarrow \quad x<1$
On combining (i) and (ii), we see that solution is not possible because nothing is common between these two solutions.(i.e., x < 1, x $\geq$ 7)

Q15. Solve the system of inequalities (x + 5) - 7(x - 2) $\ge$ 4x + 9, 2(x - 3) - 7(x + 5) $\le$ 3x - 9
    (A) $ - {\text{ 4 }} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 4}}$
    (B) $ - {\text{ 4 }} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 1}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $ - {\text{ 1 }} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 1}}$
    (D) $\frac{-9}{4} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 1}}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: (x + 5) - 7(x - 2) $\ge$ 4x + 9
$\Rightarrow$ x + 5 - 7x + 14 $\ge$ 4x + 9
$\Rightarrow$ -6x + 19 $\ge$ 4x + 9
$\Rightarrow$ -6x - 4x $\ge$ 9 - 19
$\Rightarrow$ -10x $\ge$ -10
$\Rightarrow$ x $\le$ 1
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(-\infty, 1]$ 
2(x - 3) - 7(x + 5) $\le$ 3x - 9
$\Rightarrow$ 2x - 6 - 7x - 35 $\le$ 3x < 9 
$\Rightarrow$ -5x - 41 $\le$ 3x - 9
$\Rightarrow$ -5x - 3x $\le$ 41 - 9
$\Rightarrow$ -8x $\le$ 32
$\Rightarrow$ -x $\le$ $\frac{32}{8}$ = 4
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ -4
$\Rightarrow$ $x \epsilon[-4, \infty)$
Hence the solution set is $\left[ -4,\infty \right) \cap { \left( -\infty ,1 \right] }$ = [-4, 1]
Which means $ - {\text{ 4 }} \leq {\text{ x }} \leq {\text{ 1}}$

Linear Inequalities Test 03  (id 629) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Linear Inequalities
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Solve the system of inequalities $ - {\text{ 4x }} + {\text{ 1 }} \geq {\text{ }}0{\text{ }},{\text{ 3 }}-{\text{ 4x }} < {\text{ }}0$
    (A) ( -2 , 3)
    (B) ( - 4 , 3 )
    (C) ( 1 , 3 )
    (D) no solution   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $- {\text{ 4x }} + {\text{ 1 }} \geq {\text{ }}0{\text{ }}$
$\Rightarrow -4x\ge -1\\ \Rightarrow \frac { -4x }{ -4 } \le \frac { -1 }{ -4 } \\ \Rightarrow x\le \frac { 1 }{ 4 } \\ \Rightarrow x\epsilon \left( -\infty ,\frac { 1 }{ 4 } \right]$
${\text{ 3 }}-{\text{ 4x }} < {\text{ }}0$
$\Rightarrow -4x<-3\\ \Rightarrow \frac { -4x }{ -4 } >\frac { -3 }{ -4 } \\ \Rightarrow x>\frac { 3 }{ 4 } \\ \Rightarrow x\epsilon \left( \frac { 3 }{ 4 } ,\infty \right) $
Hence solution set is $\left( -\infty ,\frac { -5 }{ 2 } \right] \bigcap { \left( \frac { 3 }{ 4 } ,\infty \right) } =\Phi $
which means no solution exist.

Q2. Solve the system of inequalities: x - 5 > 0, $\frac{2 x-4}{x+2}$ < 2
    (A) x > -5
    (B) x > 2
    (C) x < -2
    (D) x > 5   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: x - 5 > 0
$\Rightarrow$ x > 5
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(5, \infty)$ 
Now $\frac{2 x-4}{x+2}$ < 2
$\frac{2 x-4}{x+2}$ - 2 < 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{2 x-4-2(x+2)}{x+2}$ < 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{2 x-4-2 x-4}{x+2}$ < 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-8}{x+2}$ < 0
$\Rightarrow$ x + 2 > 0 [$\because$ $\frac{a}{b}$ < 0, a < 0 $\Rightarrow$ b > 0]
$\Rightarrow$ x > -2
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(-2, \infty)$ 
Hence the solution set is $\left( 5,\infty \right) \cap \left( -2,\infty \right) =\left( 5,\infty \right) $ 
Which means x > 5.

Q3. Solve the system of inequalities: $\frac{x+7}{x-8}>2, \frac{2 x+1}{7 x-1}>5$
    (A) no solution   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (2, 5)
    (C) (3, 6)
    (D) (4, 8)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\frac {x + 7} {x - 8} > 2$ 
$\Rightarrow \frac {x + 7} {x - 8} -2> 0$
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x+7-2(x-8)}{x-8}$ > 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{x+7-2 x+16}{x-8}$ > 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{(23-x)}{x-8}$ > 0 [$\because$ $\frac{a}{b}$ > 0 $\Rightarrow$ (a > 0 and b > 0) or (a < 0 and b < 0)]
$\Rightarrow$ (23 - x > 0 and x - 8 > 0) or (23 - x < 0 and x - 8 < 0)
$\Rightarrow$ (x < 23 and x > 8) or (x > 23 and x < 8)
$\Rightarrow$ 8 < x < 23 [Since x > 23 and x < 8 is not possible]
$\Rightarrow x\epsilon \left( 8,23 \right) $
Now ${{2x + 1} \over {7x - 1}}$ > 5 
$\Rightarrow \frac {2x + 1} {7x - 1}$ - 5 > 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{2 x+1-5(7 x-1)}{7 x-1}$ > 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{2 x+1-35 x+5}{7 x-1}$ > 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{(6-33 x)}{7 x-1}$ > 0 [$\because$ $\frac{a}{b}$ > 0 $\Rightarrow$ (a > 0 and b > 0) or (a < 0 and b < 0)]
$\Rightarrow$ (6 - 33x > 0 and 7x - 1 > 0) or (6 - 33x < 0 and 7x - 1 < 0)
$\Rightarrow$ (x < $\frac{6}{33}$ and x > $\frac{1}{7}$) or (x > $\frac{2}{11}$ and x < $\frac{1}{7}$)
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{7}<x<\frac{2}{11}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in\left(\frac{1}{7}, \frac{2}{11}\right)$ [Since x > $\frac{2}{11}$ and x < $\frac{1}{7}$ is not possible]
Hence, the solution of the system $\frac{x+7}{x-8}>2, \frac{2 x+1}{7 x-1}>5$ will be $\left( 8,23 \right) \cap \left( \frac { 1 }{ 7 } ,\frac { 2 }{ 11 } \right) =\phi $

Q4. Solve the system of inequalities -2 $ \leq$ 6x - 1 < 2
    (A) $-\frac{1}{7} \leq x>\frac{1}{2}$
    (B) $-\frac{1}{6} \leq x<\frac{1}{2} $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $-\frac{1}{6}<x<\frac{3}{2}$
    (D) $-\frac{1}{6}<x<\frac{5}{2}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: -2 $ \leq$ 6x - 1 < 2
$\Rightarrow$ -2 + 1 $ \leq$ 6x - 1 + 1 < 2 + 1
$\Rightarrow$ -1 $ \leq$ 6x < 3
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-1}{6} \leq \frac{6 x}{6}<\frac{3}{6}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-1}{6} \leq x<\frac{1}{2}$

Q5. Solve the system of inequalities -2 < 1 - 3x < 7
    (A) -2 < x < 2
    (B) -1 < x < 10
    (C) -2 < x < 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) -1 < x < 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: -2 < 1 - 3x < 7 
$\Rightarrow$ -2 - 1 < 1 - 3x - 1 < 7 - 1
$\Rightarrow$ -3 < -3x < 6
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-3}{-3}>\frac{-3 x}{-3}>\frac{6}{-3}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 1 > x > -2
$\Rightarrow$ -2 < x < 1

Q6. Solve the system of inequalities: $-15<\frac{3(x-2)}{5} \leq 0$
    (A) -23 < x < 23
    (B) -13 < x < 13
    (C) -13 < x < 2
    (D) -23 < x $\le$ 2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $-15<\frac{3(x-2)}{5} \leq 0$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $-15 \cdot \frac{5}{3}<\frac{3(x-2)}{5} \cdot \frac{5}{3} \leq 0 \cdot \frac{5}{3}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ -25 < (x - 2) $\le$ 0 + 2
$\Rightarrow$ -25 + 2 < x - 2 + 2 $\le$ 2
$\Rightarrow$ -23 < x $\le$ 2

Q7. The solution set for |3x - 2| $\leq \frac{1}{2}$
    (A) [$\frac{5}{6}$, $\frac{1}{2}$]
    (B) [$\frac{5}{6}$, $\frac{2}{3}$]
    (C) [$\frac{2}{3}$, $\frac{2}{3}$]
    (D) [$\frac{1}{2}$, $\frac{5}{6}$]   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: |3x - 2| $\le$ $\frac{1}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-1}{2} \leq 3 x-2 \leq \frac{1}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{-1}{2}+2 \leq 3 x-2+2 \leq \frac{1}{2}+2$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{3}{2} \leq 3 x \leq \frac{5}{2}$ [$\because$ $|x| \leq a \Leftrightarrow-a \leq x \leq a$]
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{3}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{3} \leq 3 x \cdot \frac{1}{3} \leq \frac{5}{2} \cdot \frac{1}{3}$ 
 $\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{2} \leq x \leq \frac{5}{6}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in\left[\frac{1}{2}, \frac{5}{6}\right]$

Q8. The solution set for |x| > 7
    (A) (-7, $\infty $)
    (B) $\left( { - \infty , - 7} \right)\mathop \cup \;(7,\infty )$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\left( { - \infty , - 7} \right)\mathop \cap \; (7,\infty )$
    (D) (7, $\infty $)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: |x| > 7
$\Rightarrow$ -7 > x > 7
$\Rightarrow$ x < -7 or x > 7 [$\because$ |x| > a $\Leftrightarrow$ x < -a or x > a]
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(-\infty,-7)$ or $x \in(7, \infty)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $x \epsilon(-\infty,-7) \cup(7, \infty)$

Q9. The solution set for: $\frac{|x|-1}{|x|-2} \geq 0, x \neq \pm 2$
    (A) (-2, 2)
    (B) $\left( { - 1,2} \right)\mathop \cup (3,\infty )$
    (C) ($ - \infty , - 2)\mathop \cup (2,\infty )$
    (D) $( - \infty , - 2)\mathop \cup \nolimits \left( { - 1,1} \right)\mathop \cup \nolimits (2,\infty )$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given$\frac{|x|-1}{|x|-2} \geq 0, x \neq \pm 2$ 
$\frac{|x|-1}{|x|-2} \geq 0$
$\Rightarrow$ |x| - 1 $\ge$ 0 and |x| - 2 $\ge$ 0 or |x| - 1 $\le$ 0 and |x| - 2 $\le$ 0 [$\because$ $\frac{a}{b} \geq 0$ $\Rightarrow$ (a $\ge$ 0 and b $\ge$ 0) or (a $\le$ 0 and b $\le$ 0)]
$\Rightarrow$ |x| $\ge$ 1 and |x| $\ge$ 2 or |x| $\le$ 1 and |x| $\le$ 2
$\Rightarrow$ |x| $\ge$ 2 or |x| $\le$ 1 [$\because$ |x| $\ge$ a $\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ a or x $\le$ -a and |x| $\le$ a $\Rightarrow$ $-a \leq x \leq a$ ]
$\Rightarrow$ x $\ge$ 2 or x $\le$ -2 or $-1 \leq x \leq 1$
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(2, \infty)$ or $x \in(-\infty,-2)$ or $x \epsilon(-1,1)$
$\Rightarrow$ $x \in(2, \infty) \cup(-\infty,-2) \cup(-1,1)$

Q10. The solution set for: $\left|\frac{2(3-x)}{5}\right|<\frac{3}{5}$
    (A) $(\frac 1 2, \frac 32)$
    (B) $(\frac 14, \frac 34)$
    (C) $(\frac 32, \frac 92)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $(\frac 34, \frac 94)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: $\left|\frac{2(3-x)}{5}\right|<\frac{3}{5}$
$\Rightarrow-\frac{3}{5}<\frac{2(3-x)}{5}<\frac{3}{5}$
$\Rightarrow-\frac{3}{5} \cdot \frac{5}{2}<\frac{2(3-x)}{5} \cdot \frac{5}{2}<\frac{3}{5} \cdot \frac{5}{2}$
$\Rightarrow-\frac{3}{2}<3-x<\frac{3}{2}$
$\Rightarrow-\frac{3}{2}-3<3-x-3<\frac{3}{2}-3$ $[\because|x|<a \Leftrightarrow-a<x<a]$
$\Rightarrow-\frac{9}{2}<-x<\frac{-3}{2}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{9}{2}>x>\frac{3}{2}$
$\Rightarrow x \in\left(\frac{3}{2}, \frac{9}{2}\right)$

Q11. Find all pairs of consecutive even positive integers, both of which are larger than 5, such that their sum is less than 23.
    (A) (8, 6), (6, 4), (10, 6)
    (B) (6, 8),(8, 10), (10, 12)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (4, 6), (6, 8), (8, 10)
    (D) (3, 5), (5, 7), (7, 9)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the consecutive even positive integers be x and x + 2.
By data, x > 5 and x + (x + 2) < 23
Now x + (x + 2) < 23
$\Rightarrow$ 2x + 2 < 23
$\Rightarrow$ 2x < 21
$\Rightarrow$ x < $\frac{21}{2}$ = $10\frac{1}{2}$
So we have the least possible value of x is 6 and the maximum value of x is 10.
Therefore the possible pairs of consecutive even positive integers are (6, 8), (8, 10), (10, 12).

Q12. Solve: 3x + 5 < x - 7, when x is a real number
    (A) x < -6   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x > -6
    (C) x > -12
    (D) x < -12
    Answer: A
    Explanation: 3x + 5 < x - 7
$\Rightarrow$ 3x + 5 - x < x - 7 - x
$\Rightarrow$ 2x + 5 < -7
$\Rightarrow$ 2x + 5 - 5 < -7 - 5
$\Rightarrow$ 2x < -12
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{2x}{2}$ < - $\frac{12}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x < -6

Q13. If x belongs to set of integers, A is the solution set of 2(x - 1) < 3x - 1 and B is the solution set of 4x - 3 $\leq $ 8 + x, find A $\cap$ B
    (A) {0, 1, 2, 3}   <-- CORRECT
    (B) {0, 1, 2}
    (C) {0, 2, 4}
    (D) {1, 2, 3}
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Given 2(x - 1) < 3x - 1 
$\Rightarrow$ 2x - 2 < 3x - 1
$\Rightarrow$ 2x - 2 + 2 < 3x - 1 + 2
$\Rightarrow$ 2x < 3x + 1
$\Rightarrow$ 2x - 3x < 3x + 1 - 3x 
$\Rightarrow$ -x < + 1
$\Rightarrow$ x > -1 but x $\in$ Z
Hence A = {0, 1, 2, 3, 4, ....}
Now 4x - 3 $\leq$ 8 + x
$\Rightarrow$ 4x - 3 + 3 $\leq$ 8 + x + 3
$\Rightarrow$ 4x $\leq$ 11 + x
$\Rightarrow$ 4x - x $\leq$ 11 + x - x
$\Rightarrow$ 3x $\leq$ 11
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{3x}{3}$ $\leq$ $\frac{11}{3}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x $\leq$ $\frac{11}{3}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ x $\leq$ $3\frac{2}{3}$, but x $\in$ Z
Therefore B = {....., -2, -1, 0, 1, 2, 3}
Hence A $\cap$ B = {0, 1, 2, 3}

Q14. The solution set of the inequation: $\frac{2 x-1}{3}-\frac{3 x}{5}+1<0, x \in W$ is:
    (A) x $ \in$ S
    (B) null set   <-- CORRECT
    (C) x $ \in$ N
    (D) x $ \in$ W
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\frac{2 x-1}{3}-\frac{3 x}{5}+1<0$ 
$\Rightarrow 15 \cdot \frac{2 x-1}{3}-15 \cdot \frac{3 x}{5}+15<0$ [Multiply the inequality throughout by the L.C.M]
$\Rightarrow$ 5(2x - 1) -3(3x) + 15 < 0
$\Rightarrow$ 10x - 5 - 9x + 15 < 0
$\Rightarrow$ x + 10 < 0
$\Rightarrow$ x < -10, but given x $\in$ W
Hence the solution set will be null set.

Q15. The solution set of 6x - 1 > 5 is :
    (A) {x : x < 1, x $\in$ N}
    (B) {x : x > 1, x $\in$ R}   <-- CORRECT
    (C) {x : x < 1, x $\in$ W}
    (D) {x : x > 1, x $\in$ N}
    Answer: B
    Explanation: 6x - 1 > 5
$\Rightarrow$ 6x - 1 + 1 > 5 + 1
$\Rightarrow$ 6x > 6
$\Rightarrow$ x > 1
Hence the solution set is {x : x > 1, x $\in$ R}

Linear Inequalities Test 04  (id 630) [PAID]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES
