Q1. If a, b, c, d, e are in G. P., then $\frac e c$ equals
    (A) $\frac b a$
    (B) $\frac c b$
    (C) $\frac db$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac d c$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: If a, b, c, d, e are in G.P
we have $\frac{b}{a}=\frac{c}{b}=\frac{d}{c}=\frac{e}{d}$
$\therefore \frac{c}{b}=\frac{e}{d} \Rightarrow \frac{e}{c}=\frac{d}{b}$

Q2. The product of first n odd terms of a G.P. whose middle term is m is
    (A) ${m^n}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) mn
    (C) m+n
    (D) ${n^m}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let the terms in a GP be a,ar,$a, a r, a r^{2}, a r^{3}, \dots \dots \dots$
Product of odd number of terms ( let number of terms be 'n' , n is odd ) 
$=a \cdot a r \cdot a r^{2} \cdot a r^{3} \dots a r^{n-1}$
$=a^{n} \cdot\left(1 \cdot r \cdot r^{2} \cdot r^{3} \dots r^{n-1}\right)$
$=a^{n}, r^{1+2+3+\dots + n-1}$
$=a^{n} \cdot r^{\frac{(n-1) n}{2}}$ [The sum of first n natural numbers = $\frac{n(n+1)}{2}$]
We have the middle term $=m=a r^{\frac{(n-1)}{2}}$ ......(i)
$\therefore$ Product of odd number of terms = $a^{n} \cdot r^{\frac{n(n-1)}{2}}=\left(a r^{\frac{(n-1)}{2}}\right)^{n}$= $m^{n}$ [using (i)]

Q3. The fourth term of a G. P. is 2, then product of first 7 terms is
    (A) 30
    (B) 128   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 32
    (D) 64
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let a be the first term and r be the common ratio of the G.P
Given T_4 = 2 $\Rightarrow$ ar^3 = 2
Then product of the first 7 terms = $a \cdot a r \cdot a r^{2} \cdot a r^{3} \cdot a r^{4} \cdot a r^{5} \cdot a r^{6}$ = a^7r^21 = (ar^3)^7 = 2^7 = 128

Q4. If three positive numbers a, b, c are in G. P. then log a, log b, log c are in
    (A) A.G.P.
    (B) A.P.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) H.P.
    (D) G.P.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If a, b, c are in G.P. we have $\frac{b}{a}=\frac{c}{b}$ 
So log$\left(\frac{b}{a}\right)$ = log$\left(\frac{c}{b}\right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ log b - log a = log c - log b [$\because$ $\log \left(\frac{a}{b}\right)$ = log a - log b]
$\Rightarrow$ 2log b = log c + log a 
$\Rightarrow$ log a, log b, log c are in A.P.

Q5. The nth term of the sequence 5 + 55 + 555 + …. is
    (A) $5 \times {10^{n - 1}}$
    (B) $3 \times {12^{n - 1}}$
    (C) ${\frac 59}({10^n} - 1)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $5 \times {11^{n - 1}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: 5+55+555+.........
$=\frac{5}{9}\{9+99+999+\ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots .\}$
$=\frac59\left\{[10-1\right]+\left[10^2-1\right]+\left[10^3-1\right]$+........+ [10^n-1] +........}
Hence by inspection we get nth term is $\\\frac59\left[10^n-1\right]$

Q6. The sum of first three terms of a G.P. is to the sum of next three terms is 125 : 27. The common ratio of the G.P. is
    (A) $\frac 14$
    (B) $\frac 12$
    (C) $\frac 3 5$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac 53$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given $\frac{T_{1}+T_{2}+T_{3}}{T_{4}+T_{5}+T_{6}}=\frac{125}{27}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{T_{1}+T_{2}+T_{3}}{T_{1}+T_{2}+T_{3}+T_{4}+T_{5}+T_{6}}=\frac{125}{152}$ [If $\frac{a}{b}=\frac{c}{d}$ then $\frac{a}{a+b}=\frac{c}{c+d}$]
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{S_{3}}{S_{6}}=\frac{125}{152}$ 
We have for a G.P., Sn = $\frac{a\left(r^{n}-1\right)}{r-1}$, r > 1
$\therefore$ $\frac{\frac{a\left(r^{3}-1\right)}{r-1}}{\frac{a\left(r^{6}-1\right)}{r-1}}$ = $\frac{125}{152}$, r - 1 $\ne$ 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{r^{3}-1}{r^{6}-1}=\frac{125}{152}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^6 - 152r^3 - 27 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^6 - 125r^3 - 27r^3 - 27 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^3(r^3 - 1) - 27(r^3 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r^3 - 1)(125r^3 - 27) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^3 = 1 or $\frac{27}{125}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ r = 1, $\frac{3}{5}$ 
Since r - 1 $\ne$ 0, r cannot be 1
$\Rightarrow$ r = $\frac{3}{5}$

Q7. Sum of an infinitely many terms of a G.P. is 3 times the sum of even terms. The common ratio of the G.P. is
    (A) $\frac 32$
    (B) 2
    (C) $\frac 12$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac 14$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Consider the infinite G . P $a, a r, a r^{2}, a r^{3}, \dots \dots \dots \dots, \dots$ with first term a and common ratio r
Then the even terms $a r, a r^{3}, a r^{5}, \ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots \ldots .$ is again an infinite G.P with first term ar and common ratio $r^{2}$
W e have $S_{\infty}=\frac{a}{1-r}$ 
Given $S_{\infty}=3$ . Sum of even terms
$\Rightarrow a+a r+a r^{2}+a r^{3}+$..........$=3 .\left[a r+a r^{3}+a r^{5}+\right.$............]
$\Rightarrow \frac{a}{1-r}=3 \cdot \frac{a r}{1-r^{2}}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{1}{1-r}=3 \cdot \frac{r}{(1-r)(1+r)}$
$\Rightarrow 1(1+r)=3 . r$
$\Rightarrow 2 r=1$$\Rightarrow r=\frac{1}{2}$

Q8. If $\frac{a^n+b^n}{a^{n-1}+b^{n-1}}$ be the arithmetic mean between two distinct positive reals a and b then the value of n is
    (A) $\frac 1 2$
    (B) -$\frac 1 2$
    (C) 1   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have A.M of a and b is $\frac{a+b}{2}$ 
Given $\frac{a^{n}+b^{n}}{a^{n-1}+b^{n-1}}=\frac{a+b}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 2(a^n + b^n) = (a + b)(a^n-1 + b^n-1)
$\Rightarrow$ 2a^n + 2b^n = a^n + ab^n-1 + ba^n-1 + b^n
$\Rightarrow$ a^n + b^n = ab^n-1 + ba^n-1
$\Rightarrow$ a^n - ba^n-1 = ab^n-1 - b^n
$\Rightarrow$ a^n-1(a - b) = b^n-1(a - b)
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{a^{n-1}}{b^{n-1}}$ = 1 = $\left(\frac{a}{b}\right)^{0}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ n - 1 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ n = 1

Q9. If $\frac{a+b x}{a-b x}=\frac{b+c x}{b-c x}=\frac{c+d x}{c-d x}, x \neq 0$ then a, b, c, d are in
    (A) H.P.
    (B) G.P.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) A.P.
    (D) H.M
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let $\frac{a+b x}{a-b x}=\frac{b+c x}{b-c x}=\frac{c+d x}{c-d x}$ = k(say)
Now consider $\frac{a+b x}{a-b x}$ = k
Applying componendo and dividendo, we get
$\frac{a+b x+a-b x}{a+b x-a+b x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{a}{b x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ .....(i)
Now applying componendo and dividendo, on $\frac{b+c x}{b-c x}$ = k we get
$\frac{b+c x+b-c x}{b+c x-b+c x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{b}{c x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ ...(ii)
Again applying componendo and dividendo, on $\frac{c+d x}{c-d x}$ = k we get
$\frac{c+d x+c-d x}{c+d x-c+d x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{c}{d x}=\frac{k-1}{k+1}$ ....(iii)
From equations (i), (ii) and (iii) we get $\frac{a}{b x}=\frac{b}{c x}=\frac{c}{d x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{a}{b}=\frac{b}{c}=\frac{c}{d}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ a, b, c and d are in G.P.

Q10. The A.M. between two positive numbers a and b is twice the G.M. between them. The ratio of the numbers is
    (A) $(2 - 3):\left( {\sqrt 2 + 3} \right)$
    (B) $(\sqrt 3 + 1):\left( {\sqrt 3 - 1} \right)$
    (C) $(2 + \sqrt 3 ):\left( {2 - \sqrt 3 } \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $(2 + 3):\left( {\sqrt 2 - 3} \right)$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given a and b are two positive numbers 
Also given A.M=2.G.M
$\frac{a+b}{2}=2 \sqrt{a b}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{a+b}{2 \sqrt{a b}}=\frac{2}{1}$
Applying componendo dividendo
$\frac{a+b+2 \sqrt{a b}}{a+b-2 \sqrt{a b}}=\frac{2+1}{2-1}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{(\sqrt{a}+\sqrt{b})^{2}}{(\sqrt{a}-\sqrt{b})^{2}}=\frac{3}{1}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{\sqrt{a}+\sqrt{b}}{\sqrt{a}-\sqrt{b}}=\frac{\sqrt{3}}{1}$
Applying componendo dividendo again we get
$\Rightarrow \frac{2 \sqrt{a}}{2 \sqrt{b}}=\frac{\sqrt{3}+1}{\sqrt{3}-1}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{a}{b}=\frac{(\sqrt{3}+1)^{2}}{(\sqrt{3}-1)^{2}}=\frac{4+2 \sqrt{3}}{4+2 \sqrt{3}}=\frac{2(2+\sqrt{3})}{2(2-\sqrt{3})}=\frac{2+\sqrt{3}}{2-\sqrt{3}}$

Q11. If A, G, H denote respectively the A.M., G.M. and H.M. between two unequal positive numbers, then
    (A) A = GH
    (B) A^2 = GH
    (C) G^2 = HA   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A = G^2H
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given the number are a and b, then we have
A.M = A = $\frac{a+b}{2}$, G.M. = G = $\sqrt{a b}$ and H.M = H = $\frac{2ab}{a + b}$ 
Now AH = $\left(\frac{a+b}{2}\right)\left(\frac{2 a b}{a+b}\right)$ = ab = $(\sqrt{a b})^{2}$ = G^2

Q12. The arithmetic, harmonic and geometric means between two +ve numbers are $\frac {144} {15},15$ and 12 but not necessarily in this order, then the H.M. G.M. and A.M. respectively are
    (A) $15,12,\frac {144} {15}$
    (B) $12,,\frac {144} {15},15$
    (C) $12,15,\frac {144} {15}$
    (D) $\frac {144} {15},12,15$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We have H.M < G.M < A.M
Also given their values are $\frac{144}{15}$ = 9, 6, 12, 15
Hence we can say H.M = 9.6, G.M = 12, A.M = 15

Q13. The sum of first eight terms of a G.P. is 82 times the sum of first four terms. The common ratio of the G.P. is
    (A) 5
    (B) 2
    (C) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let d be the common ratio of the G.P.
Given S_8 = 82 S_4 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{S_{8}}{S_{4}}$ = 82
We have S_n = $\frac{a\left(r^{n}-1\right)}{r-1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{\frac{a\left(r^{8}-1\right)}{r-1}}{\frac{a\left(r^{4}-1\right)}{(-1)}}=82, r-1 \neq 0$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{r^{8}-1}{r^{4}-1}$ = 82
$\Rightarrow$ r^8 - 1 - 82r^4 + 82 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r^4)^2 - 82r^4 + 81 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r^4)^2 - 82r^4 - 1r^4 + 81 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^4(r^4 - 1) - 81(r^4 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r^4 - 81)(r^4 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^4 = 81 or r^4 = 1
Since r - 1 $\ne$ 0, r cannot be 1
$\Rightarrow$ r = $\sqrt[4]{81}$ = 3

Q14. The sum of first 10 terms of a G.P. is equal to 244 times the sum of its first five terms. Then the common ratio is
    (A) 7
    (B) 4
    (C) 5
    (D) 3   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let r be the common ratio of the G.P.
Given S_10 = 244 S_5 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{S_{10}}{S_{5}}$ = 244
We have S_n = $\frac{a\left(r^{n}-1\right)}{r-1}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{\frac{a\left(r^{10}-1\right)}{r-1}}{\frac{a\left(r^{5}-1\right)}{r-1}}=244, r-1 \neq 0$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{r^{10}-1}{r^{5}-1}$ = 244
$\Rightarrow$ r^10 - 1 - 244r^5 + 244 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r^5)^2 - 244r^5 + 243 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (r5)^2 - 243r^5 - 1r^5 + 243 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^5(r^5 - 1) - 243(r^5 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^5 = 243 or r^5 = 1
Since r - 1 $\ne$ 0, r cannot be 1
$\Rightarrow$ r = $\sqrt[5]{243}$ = 3

Q15. The product of terms equidistant from the beginning and end in a G.P. (finite) is equal to
    (A) first term
    (B) product of the first and last terms   <-- CORRECT
    (C) last term
    (D) Sum of the first and last terms
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the G.P be a, ar, ar^2, ar^3, ....., ar^n-3, ar^n-2, ar^n-1 with first term a and common ratio r and let the last term l = T_n = ar_n-1 
Now we have T_1T_n = a.ar^n-1 = a^2r^n-1 
T_2.T_n-1 = ar.ar^n-2 = a^2r^n-1
T_3.T_n-2 = ar^2.ar^n-3 = a^2r^n-1 ........
T_m.T_n-(m-1) = ar^m-1. ar^n-m = a^2r^n-1 
Hence we have the product of terms equidistant from the beginning and end = first term. last term

Q1. If x, 2 x + 2, 3 x + 3, … are in G.P., then the fourth term of this sequence is
    (A) 27
    (B) 13.75
    (C) - 27
    (D) - 13.5   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If x, 2x + 2, 3x + 3, .... are in G.P., then we get $\frac{2 x+2}{x}=\frac{3 x+3}{2 x+2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ (2x + 2)^2 = x(3x + 3)
$\Rightarrow$ 4x^2 + 8x + 4 = 3x^2 + 3x
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + 5x + 4 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (x + 4)(x+ 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ x = -4, -1
When x = -4 the sequence is -4, -6, -9.... and then r = $\frac{-6}{-4}=\frac{-9}{-6}=\frac{3}{2}$ 
when x = -1 the sequence is -1, 0, 0, 0 .... and then r = $\frac{0}{-1}$ = 0 (this sequence can be discarded as r = 0)
Hence the fourth term is $-9 \cdot \frac{3}{2}=\frac{-27}{2}$ = -13.5 when r = $\frac{3}{2}$

Q2. If a, b, c are three positive real numbers then (a + b) (b + c) (c + a) is not less than
    (A) 2(a + b + c)
    (B) (a + b + c)
    (C) 6abc
    (D) 8abc   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given the numbers are a and b, then we have
A.M = A = $\frac{a+b}{2}$, G.M. = G = $\sqrt{a b}$ and A.M > G.M
Now we have $\frac{a+b}{2}>\sqrt{a b}$ ...(i)
$\frac{b+c}{2}>\sqrt{b c}$ ....(ii)
$\frac{c+a}{2}>\sqrt{c a}$ ....(iii)
Multiply (i), (ii) and (iii), we get
$\frac{a+b}{2} \cdot \frac{b+c}{2} \cdot \frac{c+a}{2}>\sqrt{a b} \cdot \sqrt{b c} \cdot \sqrt{c a}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ (a + b)(b + c)(c + a) > 8abc

Q3. In an infinite G.P., each term is equal to the sum of all the terms which follow it. The common ratio of this G.P. is
    (A) $\frac 12$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac 13$
    (C) $\frac 14$
    (D) $\frac 23$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let the infinite G.P be $a, a r, a r^{2}, a r^{3}$ ....... with first term a and common ratio r
According to the question $a=a r+a r^{2}+a r^{3}+$....... to $\infty$
$\Rightarrow a=\frac{\bar{a} r}{1-r}$
$\Rightarrow 1-r=r$
$\Rightarrow r=\frac{1}{2}$

Q4. Sum of an infinite G.P. is $\frac 54$ times the sum of all the odd terms. The common ratio of the G.P. is
    (A) 4
    (B) $\frac 1 3$
    (C) $\frac 1 4$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac 2 3$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Consider the infinite G.P a, ar, ar^2, ar^3,.... is a G.P with first term a and common ratio r
Then the odd terms a, ar^2, ar^4,.... is again a G.P with first term a and common ratio r^2 
We have $S_{\infty}=\frac{a}{1-r}$ 
Given $S_{\infty}=\frac{5}{4}$. Sum of odd terms
$\Rightarrow$ a + ar + ar^2 + ar^3 + .... = $\frac{5}{4}$[a + ar^2 + ar^4 + ...]
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{a}{1-r}=\frac{5}{4} \cdot \frac{a}{1-r^{2}}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{1-r}=\frac{5}{4} \cdot \frac{a}{(1-r)(1+r)}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 4(1 + r) = 5
$\Rightarrow$ 4r = 1
$\Rightarrow$ r = $\frac{1}{4}$

Q5. If a, b, c are in G.P., then
    (A) a^2(b + c) = c^2(a + b)
    (B) a^2(b^2 + c^2) = c^2(a^2 + b^2)
    (C) a(b^2 + a^2) = c(b^2 + c^2)
    (D) a(b^2 + c^2) = c(a^2 + b^2)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since a, b, c are in G.P. we get b^2 = ac ....(i)
Consider a(b^2 + c^2)
Now a(b^2 + c^2) = a(ac + c^2) = a^2c + ac^2 = c(a^2 + ac) = c(a^2 + b^2) [using (i)]

Q6. Two positive numbers are in the ratio$\left( {2 + \sqrt 3 } \right):\left( {2 - \sqrt 3 } \right)$. The ratio of their A.M. to G.M. is :
    (A) $\sqrt 3 :2$
    (B) 2 : 1   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\sqrt 3 :1$
    (D) 1 : 2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the two positive numbers be x and y
Now given $\frac{x}{y}=\frac{2+\sqrt{3}}{2-\sqrt{3}}$ 
So let x = $(2+\sqrt{3}) k$ and y = $(2-\sqrt{3}) k$ 
$\therefore$ $\begin{array}{lllll} A . M \ of\ \text {and} \ y \\ \hline G . M \ o f \ x \ \text {and} \ y \end{array}$ = $\frac{\frac{x+y}{2}}{\sqrt{x y}}=\frac{x+y}{2 \sqrt{x y}}=\frac{(2+\sqrt{3}) k+(2-\sqrt{3}) k}{2 \sqrt{(2+\sqrt{3}) k \cdot(2-\sqrt{3}) k}}$ 
= $\frac{4 k}{2 \sqrt{(4-3) k^{2}}}=\frac{4 k}{2 k}=\frac{2}{1}$ [$\because$ (a + b) (a - b) = a^2 - b^2]

Q7. All the terms of a G.P. are squared. The new sequence thus formed is
    (A) G.P.   <-- CORRECT
    (B) H.M
    (C) H.P.
    (D) A.P.
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We have a, ar, ar^2, ar^3, ....., ar^n-1 is a G.P with first term a and common ratio r
Now if we square each term of this we get the sequence a^2, a^2r^2, a^2r^4, a^2r^6...., a^2r^n-1, which is again a G.P with first term a^2 and common ratio r^2

Q8. The least value of n for which 1 + 3 + 3^2 + 3^3 + .... + 3^n-1 > 1000 is
    (A) 6
    (B) 7   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8
    (D) 5
    Answer: B
    Explanation: We have 1, 3, 3^2, 3^3, ...., 3^n-1 is a G.P with first term 1 and common ratio r = 3
Now 1 + 3 + 3^2 + 3^3 + .... + 3^n-1 = S_n = $\frac{a\left(r^{n}-1\right)}{r-1}=\frac{1\left(3^{n}-1\right)}{3-1}$ 
Hence 1 + 3 + 3^2 + 3^3 + ... + 3^n-1 > 100 $\Rightarrow$ $\frac{3^{n}-1}{2}$ > 1000
$\Rightarrow$ 3^n > 2001
But we have 3^6 = 729 and 3^7 = 2187
Therefore least value of n = 7

Q9. The cotangents of $\frac{\pi}{3}, \frac{\pi}{4}$ and $\frac{\pi}{6}$ are in
    (A) A.P.
    (B) H.M
    (C) G.P.   <-- CORRECT
    (D) H.P.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We have $\cot \frac{\pi}{6}=\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}$, $\cot \frac{\pi}{4}=1$ and $\cot \frac{\pi}{3}=\sqrt{3}$ 
Clearly $\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}, 1, \sqrt{3}$ are terms of a G.P. with first term $\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}$ and common ratio r = $\sqrt{3}$

Q10. If one A.M. A and two geometric means B and C be inserted between two numbers, then ${B^3} + {C^3}$ is equal to
    (A) 3 ABC
    (B) $\frac {2\;BC} {A}$
    (C) 2 ABC   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ABC
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let the 2 numbers be x and y.
Since A is the A.M between the numbers x and y, we get A = $\frac{x+y}{2}$ ...(i)
Since B and C are the geometric means between x and y, we get x = x, B = xr and C = xr^2, y = xr^3 where r is the common ratio of the G.
Now $\frac{B^{3}+C^{3}}{B C}=\frac{B^{2}}{C}+\frac{C^{2}}{B}$ = $\frac{(x r)^{2}}{x r^{2}}+\frac{\left(x r^{2}\right)^{2}}{x r}$ = x + xr^3 = x + y = 2A from equation (i)
Hence we get B^3 + C^3 = 2ABC

Q11. In a G.P. the ratio of the sum of first three terms to the sum of first six terms is 125 : 152. The common ratio of the G.P. is
    (A) 3.5
    (B) $\frac {3}{5}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 5.3
    (D) $\frac 53$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given $\frac{S_{3}}{S_{6}}=\frac{125}{152}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{\frac{a\left(r^{3}-1\right)}{r-1}}{\frac{a\left(r^{6}-1\right)}{r-1}}=\frac{125}{152}, r-1 \neq 0$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{r^{3}-1}{r^{6}-1}=\frac{125}{152}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 152r^3 - 15^2 = 125r^6 - 125
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^6 - 152r^3 + 27 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^6 - 125r^3 - 27r^3 + 27 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 125r^3(r^3 - 1) - 27(r^3 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ (125r^3 - 27)(r^3 - 1) = 0
$\Rightarrow$ r^3 = $\frac{27}{125}$ or r^3 = 1
Since r - 1 $\ne$ 0, r cannot be 1
$\Rightarrow$ r = $\frac{3}{5}$

Q12. In a G.P. (m + n)^th and (m – n)^th terms are respectively p and q. Its m^th term is
    (A) pq
    (B) $\frac {p + q} {2}$
    (C) p-q
    (D) $\sqrt {p\;q} $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let a be the first term and r be the common ratio of the G.P
Then since T_n = a^n-1, we get
T_m+n = p $\Rightarrow$ ar^m+n-1 = p ....(i)
T_m-n = q $\Rightarrow$ ar^m-n-1 = q ...(ii)
Now dividing equation (i) by (ii)
$\frac { ar^{ m+n-1 } }{ ar^{ m-n-1 } } =\frac { p }{ q } \Rightarrow$ r^(m + n - 1) - (m - n - 1) = $\frac pq$
$\Rightarrow$ $r2n = \frac { p }{ q }$
Taking square root on both sides we get r^n = $\sqrt { \frac { p }{ q } }$ ....(iii)
Substituting equation (iii) in (i), we get 
$a.\sqrt { \frac { p }{ q } } .r^{ m-1 }$ = p
$\Rightarrow a.r^{ m-1 }=p.\sqrt { \frac { q }{ p } } =\sqrt { pq } $

Q13. If a, b, c are in A. P., a, mb, c are in G.P., then a, m^2b, c are in
    (A) G.P.
    (B) H.P.   <-- CORRECT
    (C) H.M
    (D) A.P.
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If the numbers a, b, c are in A.P. we have b = $\frac{a+c}{2}$ ....(i)
Since a, mb, c are in G.P. we get (mb)^2 = ac ....(ii)
Now m^2b = $\frac{2(m b)^{2}}{2 b}=\frac{2 a c}{a+c}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ a, m^2b, c are in H.P.

Q14. The next term of the sequence $\frac{1}{4}, \frac{1}{36}, \frac{1}{144}$,
    (A) $\frac {1} {576}$
    (B) $\frac {1} {1296}$
    (C) $\frac {1} {169}$
    (D) $\frac {1} {400}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: By inspection we get a_n = $\frac{1}{n^{2} \cdot(n+1)^{2}}$, as
a_1 = $\frac{1}{1^{2} \cdot(1+1)^{2}}= \frac{1}{ 4}$ 
a_2 = $\frac{1}{2^{2} \cdot(2+1)^{2}}= \frac{1}{ 36}$ 
and a_3 = $\frac{1}{3^{2} \cdot(3+1)^{2}}=\frac{1}{144}$ 
$\therefore$ a_4 = $\frac{1}{4^{2} \cdot(4+1)^{2}}= \frac{1}{400}$

Q15. If the sum of first n natural numbers is one-fifth of the sum of their squares, then n equals
    (A) 7   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 6
    (C) 5
    (D) 8
    Answer: A
    Explanation: According to question,
The sum of n natural no. = $\frac{1}{5}$ times of sum of their squares
So, 
$\frac{n(n+1)}{2}=\frac{1}{5} \frac{n(n+1)(2 n+1)}{6}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ 15 = 2n+ 1
$\Rightarrow$ n = 7

Straight Lines Test 01  (id 647) [FREE]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Straight Lines
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The point which divides the joint of ( 1, 2 ) and ( 3,4 ) externally in the ratio 1 : 1 .
    (A) lies in ${{\rm{3}}^{{\rm{rd}}}}$ quadrant
    (B) lies in the ${{\rm{2}}^{{\rm{nd}}}}$ quadrant
    (C) cannot be found   <-- CORRECT
    (D) lies in the ${{\rm{1}}^{{\rm{st}}}}$ quadrant
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The point which divides the line in the ratio m:n externally is given by x =$m(x_2) -n(x_1)\over m - n$
Substituting the values we get,
x = $ 1(3) - 1(1)\over 1-1$ which is undefined.

Q2. The distance of the point (x, y) from the origin is
    (A) x
    (B) $\sqrt {{x^2} + {y^2}} $   <-- CORRECT
    (C) x + y
    (D) x - y
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Distance between two points is given by $\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 +(y_2-y_1)^2}$ 
Therefore the distance from the origin to the point (x, y) is $\sqrt{(x-0)^2 +(y-0)^2}$ = $\sqrt{x^2 +y^2}$

Q3. The distance of the point ( x , y ) from Y axis is
    (A) ${\text{|y|}}$
    (B) y
    (C) ${\text{|x|}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The abscissa or the x co-ordiate of a point is the distance from the y- axis. Hence the distance is x

Q4. Slope of a line is not defined if the line is
    (A) parallel to the line x – y
    (B) parallel to X axis
    (C) parallel to Y axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) parallel to the line x + y
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Vertical lines have undefined slopes. Hence a line which is parallel to Y-axis has undefined slopes.

Q5. The distance of the point ($\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $) from X axis is
    (A) $| \alpha |$
    (B) $\alpha $
    (C) $| \beta |$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) none of these.
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The distance of a point from X axis is its y coordinate.
Hence the distance of the point ($\alpha , \beta$) from X axis is |$\beta$|

Q6. The line through the points (a, b) and (- a, - b) passes through the point
    (A) (a^2, ab)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (1, 1)
    (C) (3a, - 2b)
    (D) (2a, - 3b)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Equation of a line passing through (x_1, y_1) and (x_2, y_2) is given by
$y-y_1 \over y_2-y_1$=$x - x_1\over x_2-x_1$ 
Substituting the given values we get,
$y-b\over -b-b$^ =^ $x-a \over -a-a$ 
That is $y-b \over -2b $ = $x-a \over -2a$ 
On cross multiplying and rearranging we get,
bx - ay = 0
If this passes through the given point (a^2, ab) then
b(a^2) - a(ab) = 0

Q7. Projection (the foot of perpendicular) from (x, y) on the x-axis is
    (A) (x, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (0, - y)
    (C) (-x, 0)
    (D) (0, y)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let L be the foot of the perpendicular from the X-axis. Therefore its y coordinate is zero.
Therefore the coordinates of the point L is (x, 0).

Q8. The image of the point ($\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $) with respect to the line x + y = 0 is
    (A) (- $\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }} - {\rm{ }}\alpha $)
    (B) ($\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $)
    (C) ($\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\alpha $)
    (D) (- $\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\alpha $)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The equation of the line which is perpendicular to the given line x + y = 0 is x - y = 0
The point of intersection of these two lines is (0, 0) which is the origin
This point of intersection is the midpoint of the given point ($\alpha,\beta$) and its image, say (a, b)
Therefore $\alpha +a\over 2$ 
This implies a = $-\alpha$ 
Similarly $\beta+b\over 2$ = 0
This implies b = $-\beta$ 
Therefore $(-\alpha, -\beta)$ is the image.

Q9. The distance between the lines 5x – 12y + 65 = 0 and 5x – 12y – 39 = 0
    (A) - 2
    (B) 8   <-- CORRECT
    (C) - 8
    (D) 2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: To find the distance between two parallel lines given by the equations $A x+B y+C_1=0$ and $A x+B y+C_2=0$, we can use the formula:
$ \text { Distance }=\frac{\left|C_2-C_1\right|}{\sqrt{A^2+B^2}} $
For the lines $5 x-12 y+65=0$ and $5 x-12 y-39=0$ : - Here, $A=5, B=-12, C_1=65$, and $C_2=-39$. Now, we calculate the distance:
$ \text { Distance }=\frac{|-39-65|}{\sqrt{5^2+(-12)^2}}=\frac{|-104|}{\sqrt{25+144}}=\frac{104}{\sqrt{169}}=\frac{104}{13}=8 $

Q10. The image of the point ($\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $) with respect to the line x = y is
    (A) (- $\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }} - {\rm{ }}\alpha $)
    (B) (- $\alpha {\rm{ }}, - {\rm{ }}\beta $)
    (C) ($\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\alpha $)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ($\alpha {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\beta $)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The image point of ($\alpha, \beta$) with respect x = y is ($\beta,\alpha$)

Q11. The equation y - y_1 = m(x - x_1), m $\in$ R represents all lines through the point (x_1, y_1) except the line
    (A) parallel to the line x + y = 0
    (B) parallel to the line x – y = 0
    (C) parallel to X axis
    (D) parallel to Y axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The vertical lines which are parallel to Y-axis have undefined slopes. Hence the slope of the line 'm' will be undefined.
Therefore the above equation of the line will represent all lines through (x_1, y_1) except the line parallel to Y-axis.

Q12. Slope of any line parallel to X axis is
    (A) -1
    (B) 2
    (C) 1
    (D) 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since the angle made with x-axis is zero since tan $\theta$ is the slope. Then tan $\theta$ = 0
Hence the slope of the line parallel to the X-axis is zero.

Q13. The distance between the parallel lines 3x + 4y + 13 = 0 and 3x + 4y - 13 = 0 is
    (A) $\frac{26}{5}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{26}{3}$
    (C) $\frac{26}{4}$
    (D) 26
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Distance between parallel lines is given by $|C_1-C_2| \over \sqrt {A^2+B^2} $ 
Now substituting the values we get, $|13-(-13)|\over \sqrt{3^2+4^2}$ = $26\over 5$

Q14. The straight lines x + y = 0, 3x - y – 4 = 0, x + 3y – 4 = 0 form a triangle which is
    (A) isosceles
    (B) equilateral
    (C) scalene
    (D) right angled   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The lines formed by these lines is a right-angled, triangle.
Two lines are perpendicular to each other if the product of their slopes is -1.
Slope of the lines 3x - y – 4 = 0, x + 3y – 4 = 0 are 3 and $\frac{-1}{3}$ respectively.
The product of these slopes is -1
Hence the lines 3x - y – 4 = 0, x + 3y – 4 = 0 are perpendicular to each other.
Therefore the triangle formed by these lines is a right-angled triangle.

Q15. The lines 2x – 3y = 5 and 6x – 9y – 7 = 0 are
    (A) coincident
    (B) Incident
    (C) parallel   <-- CORRECT
    (D) perpendicular
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given lines are parallel lines condition for the line to be parallel is $a_1\over a_2$= $b_1\over b_2$ $\ne $$C_1\over C_2$ 
Substituting the values,
$2\over 6$ =$-3\over -9$$\ne$$5\over 7$ 
Hence they are parallel lines.

Straight Lines Test 02  (id 648) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Straight Lines

Q1. The equation of the line which passes through the point (1, - 2) and cuts off equal intercepts from the axis is
    (A) x - y - 1 = 0
    (B) x - y - 2 = 0
    (C) x + y + 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x + y = 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let the equation of the line which has equal intercepts be 
$x\over a$ + $y\over a$ = 1
Substituting the values for x and y
1 - 2 = a
Therefore a = -1
Hence the equation of the line is x + y + 1 = 0

Q2. If a line is drawn through the origin and parallel to the line x - 2y + 5 = 0, its equation is
    (A) x = 2y   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2x + y = 0
    (C) x – 2y + 5 = 0
    (D) x – 2y – 5 = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: If the line is parallel to the given line x - 2y + 5 = 0, then the required line will have the same slope.
Hence the equaion of the given line is x - 2y + k = 0
Since it passes through the origin,
0 + 0 + k = 0
Therefore k = 0
Hence the equation of the required line is x - 2y = 0 or x = 2y

Q3. The line passing through (1, 1) and parallel to the line 2x – 3y + 5 = 0 is
    (A) 3x + 2y = 5
    (B) 2x – 3y + 1= 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2x + 3y = 5
    (D) 3x – 2y = 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The required line is parallel to the given line, hence it has same slope.
Therefore the equation of the required line is 2x - 3y + k = 0
Since it passes through (1, 1)
2(1) - 3(1) + k = 0
Therefore k = 1
Hence the equation of the required line is 2x - 3y + 1 = 0

Q4. The equation of the line which passes through the point (2, -3) and cuts off equal intercepts from the axis is
    (A) x – y – 2 = 0
    (B) x – y = 1
    (C) x + y + 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x + y = 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The equation of the line which cuts equal intercepts is x + y = a 
Since it passes through (2, -3), 2 - 3 = a
Hence a = -1
Hence the equation of the required line is x + y +1 = 0

Q5. The straight lines x + y - 4 = 0, 3x + y – 4 = 0, x - 3y – 4 = 0 form a triangle which is
    (A) equilateral
    (B) Acute angled triangle
    (C) right angled triangle   <-- CORRECT
    (D) obtuse angled triangle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The triangle formed by these lines is a right-angled triangle.
If the lines are perpendicular to each other, then the product of their slopes is -1
The slope of lines 3x + y – 4 = 0, x - 3y – 4 = 0 are -3 and $\frac{1}{3}$ respectively.
The product of the slopes is -1.
Hence these two lines are perpendicular to each other.
This infers that the triangle formed by these lines is a right angled triangle.

Q6. The distance between the parallel lines 4x + 3y + 11 = 0 and 8x + 6y = 15 is
    (A) $\frac{7}{10}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{5}{2}$
    (C) $\frac{7}{2}$
    (D) 4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Distance between two parallel lines is given by $|c_1-c_2|\over \sqrt{A^2+B^2}$ 
c_1 = 2 $\times$ 11 = 22 and c_2 = 15 and A = 8 and B = 6
Now substituting the values we get
$|22 - 15|\over\sqrt{36+64}$ = $\frac{7}{10}$

Q7. The line which passes through the point ( 0 , 1 ) and perpendicular to the line x – 2y + 11 = 0 is
    (A) 2x + y – 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2x – y + 1 = 0
    (C) 2x – y - 3 = 0
    (D) 2x – y + 3 = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The line which is perpendicular to the given line is 2x + y + k = 0
Since it passes through (0,1)
2(0) + 1 + k = 0
This implies k = -1
Hence the equation of the required line is 2x + y - 1 = 0

Q8. The perpendicular distance of the origin from the line 3x + 4y + 1 = 0 is
    (A) $\frac{1}{2}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{5}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{1}{4}$
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The perpendicular distance from the origin to the line is given by $Ax_1 +By_1+C\over \sqrt{A^2+B^2}$ 
For the given line c = 1, A = 3 and B = 4 and since it passes through the origin,
Substituting the values we get,
$1\over \sqrt{9+16}$ = $\frac{1}{5}$

Q9. The acute angle between the lines x – y = 0 and y = 0 is
    (A) 75^o
    (B) 30^o
    (C) 60^o
    (D) 45^o   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Slope of the line x - y = 0 is 1. This implies the tan$\theta$ = 1 Hence, the angle made by the line with X-axis is 45^o
The angle made by the line y = 0 with the Y-axis is 90^o. Therefore the acute angle between the lines is 45^o.

Q10. The vertices of a triangle are (0, 3), (-3, 0) and (3, 0). The orthocenter of the triangle is
    (A) (3, 0)
    (B) (-3, 0)
    (C) (0, 3)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (0, -3)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: From the given points it is clear that these points form a right-angled isosceles triangle.
The orthocentre of all right angle lies on its right-angle vertex.
Here the right angle vertex is (0, 3)
Hence the orthocentre is (0, 3)

Q11. The lines x + ( k - 1)y + 1 = 0 and 2x + k^2y - 1 = 0 are at right angles if
    (A) k > 1
    (B) k = 1
    (C) k < 1
    (D) k = - 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If the lines are at right angles to each other, then the product of their slopes = -1. Slope of any line = -(coefficient of x/coeffiecient of y)
Therefore the slope of line 1 = -$\frac{1}{k-1}$
The slope of line 2 = $\frac{-2}{k^2}$
Therefore $-1 \over (k-1)$ $\times$ $-2 \over k^2$ = - 1
That is k^2 (k - 1) = -2
i.e; k^3 - k^2 + 2 = 0
On factorizing we get (k + 1)(k^2 - 2k - 2) = 0
This imlpies k + 1 is a factor, hence k = -1
Hence they are at right angles if k = -1

Q12. A line is equally inclined to the axis and the length of perpendicular from the origin upon the line is $\sqrt 2 $. A possible equation of the line is
    (A) x + y = 2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) y = $\sqrt 2 $ x + 2
    (C) y = x + $\sqrt 2 $
    (D) y = x + 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Since the line is equally inclined, the slope of the line should be -1, because it makes 135^o in the positive direction of the X-axis.
This implies the equation of the line is y = -x + c 
i.e; x + y - c = 0
distance of the line from the origin is given as $\sqrt 2$ 
Therefore $\sqrt 2$ = $|c|\over \sqrt{1^2+1^2}$ 
This implies c = 2
Hence, the equation of the line is x + y = 2

Q13. The lines y = mx, y + 2x = 0, y = 2x + $\lambda $ and y = - mx + $\lambda $ form a rhombus if m =
    (A) 2
    (B) - 1
    (C) -2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Rhombus is a parallelogram in which the opposite sides are equal and parallel.
Therefore the lines y = mx and y = -2x are parallel, similarly y = 2x + $\lambda$ and y = -mx + $\lambda$ are parallel.
If two lines are equal, then their slopes are equal.
This implies m = -2

Q14. Two points (a, 0) and (0, b) are joined by a straight line. Another point on this line is
    (A) (-a, 2b)
    (B) (a, -2b)
    (C) (-3a, 2b)
    (D) (3a, - 2b)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The slope of the line joining the points (a, 0) and (0, b) is [$\frac{[b-0]}{[0-a]}$ = -($\frac{b}{a}$)
Hence the equation of the line is y = (-$\frac{b}{a}$)x + b
i.e; ay = -bx + ab
Substituting the x coordinate 3a in the place of x in the above equation we get y = -2b
Hence (3a, -2b) is another point on the line.

Q15. The coordinates of the foot of perpendicular from (0, 0) upon the line x + y = 2 are
    (A) (1, 2)
    (B) (1, 1)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (-1, 2)
    (D) (1, -2)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation of the line perpendicular to the given line is x - y + k = 0
Since it passes through the origin, 
0 - 0 + k = 0
Therefore, k = 0
Hence the equation of the line is x - y = 0
On solving these two equations we get x = 1 and y = 1
The point of intersection of these two lines is (1, 1)
Hence the coordinates of the foot of the perpendicular is (1, 1)

Straight Lines Test 03  (id 649) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Straight Lines
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The area of the triangle whose sides are along the lines x = 0, y = 0 and 4x + 5y = 20 is
    (A) 20 sq.units
    (B) 10 sq.units   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{1}{10}$ sq.units
    (D) $\frac{1}{20}$ sq.units
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation 4x + 5y = 20 can be written as $x \over 5$ + $y \over4$ = 1
This implies the intercepts cut by this line on the X and Y axes are 5 and 4 respectively.
Hence the area of the triangle is $\frac{1}{2}$[5 $\times$ 4] = 10 square units.

Q2. A line is drawn through the points (3, 4) and (5, 6). If the is extended to a point whose ordinate is – 1, then the abscissa of that point is
    (A) - 2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 0
    (C) -1
    (D) 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The slope of the given line is $y_2 - y_1 \over x_2-x_1$ = $6-4 \over 5 -3$ = 1
Therefore $4-(-1) \over 3-x$ = 1
That is 4 + 1 = 3 - x
Therefore x = -2

Q3. The line x + y – 6 = 0 is the right bisector of the segment [PQ]. If P is the point (4, 3), then the point Q is
    (A) (3, 3)
    (B) (3, 4)
    (C) (3, 2)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (4, 4)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Equation of the line which is perpendicular to the given line x + y = 6 is x - y + k = 0
Since it passes through the point (4, 3)
4 - 3 + k = 0
Therefore k = -1
Hence the equation of the line segment PQ is x - y - 1 = 0
On solving these two lines we get x = $\frac{7}{2}$ and y = $\frac{5}{2}$
This point of intersection is the midpoint of the line segment PQ.
That is $4+x \over 2$ = $\frac{7}{2}$ Hence x = 3
Similarly $3+y \over 2$ = $\frac{5}{2}$. Hence y = 2
Hence the coordinates of the point Q is (3, 2).

Q4. The acute angle between the lines ax + by + c = 0 and (a + b)x = (a – b)y , a $ \ne $b , is
    (A) 30^o
    (B) 60^o
    (C) 15^o
    (D) 45^o   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The slope of the first line is -($\frac{a}{b}$) and slope of the second line is $a+b \over a-b$ 
Angle between the lines is $tan\theta$ = $|m_2 - m_1|\over 1+ m_1m_2$ 
Let m_1 = -($\frac{a}{b}$) and m_2 = $a+b \over a-b$ 
Hence $tan \theta$ =[ $(-a/b) - (a+b)/a-b)\over1 +(-a/b)(a+b)/(a-b)$]
On simplifying we get, 
tan $ \theta$ = 1
This implies $\theta$ = 45^o

Q5. The lines x + 2y – 3 = 0, 2x + y – 3 = 0 and the line l are concurrent. If the line I passes through the origin, then its equation is
    (A) x – y = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x + y = 0
    (C) x - 2y = 0
    (D) x + 2y = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Equation of a line passing through the intersection of two lies is given by ax_1 + by_1 +c_1 + k(ax_2 + by_2 + c_2) = 0
Hence x + 2y - 3 + k(2x + y - 3) = 0
Since it passes through (0, 0)
-3 -3k = 0
This implies k = -1
Sustituting for k we get,
x + 2y - 3 +(-1)(2x + y - 3) = 0
-x + y = 0 or x - y = 0

Q6. The triangle formed by the lines x + y = 1, 2x + 3y – 6 = 0 and 4x – y + 4 = 0 lies in
    (A) 3^rd quadrant
    (B) 1^st quadrant
    (C) 4^th quadrant
    (D) 2^nd quadrant   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: On solving line 1 and line 2 we get x = -3 and y = 4. Hence the point of intersection is (-3, 4)
On solving line 2 and line 3 we get x = ($\frac{-3}{7}$) and y = $\frac{16}{7}$. Hence the point of intersection is ($\frac{-3}{7}$, $\frac{16}{7}$)
On solving line 3 and line 1 we get x = $\frac{-3}{7}$ and y = $\frac{-8}{7}$. Hence the point of intersection is ($\frac{-3}{7}$, $\frac{-8}{7}$)
All the above points lie in the second quadrant. Hence the triangle formed by these lines also lie in the second quadrant.

Q7. The area of triangle formed by the lines y = x, y = 2x and y = 3x + 4 is
    (A) 7
    (B) 8
    (C) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 9
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Area of the triangle formed by the coordinates (x_1, y_1), (x_2, y_2) and (x_3, y_3) is given by
$1\over 2$[x_1(y_2 - y_3) + x_2(y_3 - y_1) + x_3(y_1 - y_2)]
On solving the lines 1 and 2, the point of intersection is (0, 0)
On solving the lines 2 and 3, the point of intersection is (4, 8)
On solving the line 3 and 1 , the point of intersection is (-2, -2)
Now substituting the values to find the area of the triangle,
Area = $1\over 2$| [0 + 4(-2 - 0) + (-2)(0 - 8)] |
= 4 sq units

Q8. If the points representing the complex numbers - 4 +3i, 2 – 3i and 0 + pi are collinear, then the value of p is
    (A) 1
    (B) 2
    (C) - 2
    (D) - 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let us take the coordinates as (-4, 3), (2, -3) and (0, p).
If the points are collienear the $1\over 2$|x_1(y_2 - y_3) + x_2(y_3 - y_1) + x_3(y_1 - y_2)| = 0
Now substituting the values |-4(-3 - p) +2(p - 3) + 0(3 + 3)|= 0
12 + 4p + 2p - 6 + 0 = 0
6p +6 = 0
6p = -6
Therefore p = -1

Q9. The lines lx + my + n = 0, mx + ny + l = 0 and nx + ly + m = 0 are concurrent if
    (A) l + m + n = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) l – m – n = 0
    (C) l + m – n = 0
    (D) I – m + n = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The required condition for concurrency is a_3(b_1c_2 - b_2c_1) + b_3(c_1a_2 - c_2a_1) + c_3(a_1b_2 - a_2b_1) = 0
Here a_1 = l, a_2 = m, a_3 = n and b_1 = m, b_2 = n, b_3 = l and c_1 = n, c_2 = l and c_3 = m
Substituting the values we get
n(ml - n^2) + l(nm - l^2) + m(ln - m^2) = 0
This implies l^3 + m^3 + n^3 - 3lmn = 0
That is (l + m+ n)(l^2 + m^2 + n^2 - lm - mn - nl) = 0
This implies l + m + n = 0

Q10. The equations of the lines through (-1, -1) and making angles of 45^o with the line x + y = 0 are
    (A) x + 1 = 0, y + 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x – 1 = 0, y – x = 0
    (C) x - 1 = 0, y - 1 = 0
    (D) x + y = 0, y + 1 = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The lines x + 1 = 0 and y + 1 = 0 are perpendicular to each other.
The slope of the line x + y = 0 is -1
Hence the angle made by this line with respect to X-axis is 45^o
In other words, the angle made by this line with x + 1 = 0 is 45^o
Clearly the other line with which it can make 45^o is y + 1 = 0

Q11. Given the 4 lines with equations x + 2y – 3 = 0, 2x + 3y – 4 = 0, 3x + 4y – 5 = 0, 4x + 5y – 6 = 0, then these lines are
    (A) the sides of a quadrilateral
    (B) sides of a Rhombus
    (C) sides of a parallelogram
    (D) concurrent   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The lines are concurrent
On solving the lies 1 and 2 we get the point of intersection as (-1, 2)
Similarly on solving lines 2 and 3, the point of intersection is (-1, 2)
Similarly solving lines 3 and 4, the point of intersection is (-1, 2)
On solving lines 1 and 4 the point of intersection is (-1, 2)
Since the point of intersection is the same for all the lines, the lines are concurrent.

Q12. The locus of the equation xy = 0 is
    (A) a straight line
    (B) A parabola
    (C) a pair of perpendicular lines   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a hyperbola
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The equation of the pair of straight lines passing through the origin is given by ax^2 + 2hxy + by^2 = 0
The condition for perpendicularity between the pair of lines is a + b = 0
Hence the locus of the pair of these perpendicular straight lines should be xy = 0

Q13. The locus of the inequation xy $≥$ 0 is
    (A) a pair of straight lines
    (B) a parallel line
    (C) a straight line
    (D) the set of all points either in the 1st quadrant or in the 3rd quadrant including the points on coordinate axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It is the set of all points either in the 1st quadrant or in the 3rd quadrant including the points on coordiate axis. This is because the inequality $\ge$ indicates that the points belong either to 1st or 3rd quadrant.

Q14. The acute angle between the lines y = 2x and y = - 2x is
    (A) greater than 60^o
    (B) 90^o
    (C) 60^o
    (D) less than 60^o   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The angle between two straight lines is given by $|m_1-m_2|\over 1+m_1m_2$ 
Here m_1 = 2 and m_2 = -2
Sustituting the values we get,
tan $\theta$ = $2-(-2)\over 1+2.(-2)$ 
= $\frac{4}{5}$ < 60^0

Q15. The image of the point (-1, 2) in the origin is
    (A) (-1, -2)
    (B) (1, 2)
    (C) (1, -2)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (2, - 1)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: When a point M which is in the 2nd quadrant is reflected in the origin, its image is formed in the 4th quadrant whose coordinates are (x, -y)
Hence, the image of the point (-1, 2) is (1, -2)

Straight Lines Test 04  (id 650) [PAID]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. The orthogonal projection of the point (2, - 3) on the line x + y = 0 is
    (A) (-2, -3)
    (B) (2, -3)
    (C) (2, 3)
    (D) ($\frac{5}{2}$, $\frac{-5}{2}$)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Equation of the line which is perpendicular to the given line is x - y + k = 0
Since this line passes through (2, -3)
2-(-3) + k = 0
This implies k = -5
Hence the equation og the line is x - y = 5
On solving the lines x + y = 0 and x - y = 5, we get the point of intersection as x = $\frac{5}{2}$ and y = $\frac{-5}{2}$
Hence ($\frac{5}{2}$, $\frac{-5}{2}$) is the coordinates of orthogonal projection.

Q2. Three points A, B and C are collinear if the area of triangle ABC is
    (A) greater than zero
    (B) less than zero
    (C) not equal to zero
    (D) zero   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Only non-collinear points can form a triangle. Hence if the three points are collinear a triangle cannot be formed, hence the area of the triangle is zero

Q3. The lines 8x + 4y = 1, 8x + 4y = 5, 4x + 8y = 3, 4x + 8y = 7 form a
    (A) Square
    (B) Rectangle
    (C) Trapezium
    (D) Rhombus   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: On solving the equations 8x + 4y = 1 and 4x + 8y = 3, we get the point of intersection as ($\frac{-1}{2}$, $\frac{5}{12}$)
On solving the equations 8x + 4y = 5 and 4x + 8y = 7, we get the point of intersection as ($\frac{1}{4}$, $\frac{3}{4}$)
On solving the equations 8x + 4y = 1 and 4x + 8y = 7, we get the point of intersection as ($\frac{-5}{12}$, $\frac{13}{12}$)
On solving the equations 8x + 4y = 5 and 4x + 8y = 3, we the point of intersection as ($\frac{7}{12}$, $\frac{1}{12}$)
Let the points A(($\frac{-1}{2}$, $\frac{5}{12}$), B($\frac{7}{12}$, $\frac{1}{12}$) C($\frac{1}{4}$, $\frac{3}{4}$) and D($\frac{-5}{12}$, $\frac{13}{12}$) be the vertices of the quadrilateral
Since the slopes of the opposite sides are equal the quadrilateral is a parallelogram
The slope of the diagonal AC is $5/12 - 3/4\over -1/2 - 1/4$ = 1
The slope of the diagonal BD is $1/2 - 13/12\over 7/12 - (-5/12)$ = -1
Since the product of the slopes is -1, the diagonals are perpendicular to each other.
Hence the parallelogram is a rhombus.

Q4. The number of points on X-axis which are at a distance of c units (c < 3) from (2, 3) is
    (A) 1
    (B) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3
    (D) 2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let (x, 0) be the point.
Then, by distance formula we have
(x - 2)^2 + 3^2 = c^2
x^2 - 4x + 4 + 9 - c^2 = 0
x^2 - 4x + 13 - c^2 = 0
x will be real if the b^2 - 4ac $\ge$0
i.e; 16 - 4(13 - c^2) $\ge$ 0
i.e; c^2 - 9 $\ge$ 0
i.e; |c| $\ge$ 3
Hence there is no point.

Q5. If (x, y) are the coordinates of point in the plane, then $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} 3&4&2 \\ 5&8&2 \\ x&y&2 \end{array}} \right| $ = 0 represents
    (A) a circle
    (B) a straight line parallel to y axis
    (C) a straight line   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a straight line parallel to x axis
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The given determinant can be written as 2$\begin{vmatrix} 3 & 4 & 1\\ 5 & 8 & 1\\ x & y & 1 \end{vmatrix}$ = 0
On expansion we get 
2[3(8 - y) - 4(5 - x) + 1(5y - 8x)]
On simplifying the equation 2(-4x + 2y + 4) = 0 represents a striaght line.

Q6. The equations of the lines through (1, 1) and making angles of 45^o with the line x + y = 0
    (A) x – 1 = 0, x – y = 0
    (B) x – y = 0, y – 1 = 0
    (C) x + y = 0, y – 1 = 0
    (D) x – 1 = 0, y – 1 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If the lines make equal angles of 45^o with the given line, x + y = 0.
Then these lines must be perpendicular with each other.
This is possible only when the two lines are parallel to X-axis and Y-axis.
That is the equations should be x = a constant and y = a constant.
Since it passes through (1, 1)
The equations should be x = 1 or x - 1 = 0 and y = 1 or y - 1 = 0

Q7. The number of lines that are parallel to 2x + 6y – 7 = 0 and have an intercept 10 units between the coordinate axis is :
    (A) 4
    (B) 1
    (C) 3
    (D) 2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The slope of the given line 2x + 6y = 7 is $\frac{-1}{3}$
Hence the line which is parallel to the above line is 
y = ($\frac{-1}{3}$)x + c
That is the y-intercept is (0, c) and the x-intercept is (3c, 0)
Using the distance formula
d^2 = (0 - 3c)^2 + (3c - 0)^2
= 10c^2
Since the distance is given as 10, then
100 = 10c^2
Therefore c = $ \pm$10
Since two values are possible, two lines can be drawn.

Q8. The line (p + 2q)x + (p – 3q)y = p - q for different values of p and q passes through the fixed point
    (A) ($\frac{2}{5}$, $\frac{2}{5}$)
    (B) ($\frac{3}{5}$, $\frac{5}{2}$)
    (C) ($\frac{3}{5}$, $\frac{3}{5}$)
    (D) ($\frac{2}{5}$, $\frac{3}{5}$)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Expanding the given equation
px + 2qx + py - 3qy = p - q
px + py + 2qx - 3qy = p - q
p(x + y) - q(- 2x + 3y) = p - q
Equating the coeffiecients of like terms
x + y = 1 and - 2x + 3y = 1
On solving both the equations we get,
x = $\frac{2}{5}$ and y = $\frac{3}{5}$
Hence the line passes through the fixed point ($\frac{2}{5}$, $\frac{3}{5}$)

Q9. The area of the quadrilateral formed by the lines |x| + |y| = 1 is
    (A) 4
    (B) 2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 8
    (D) 10
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Equations of the lines are
x $\ge$ 0, y $\ge$ 0, then x + y = 1
x $ \le$ 0, y $\le$ 0, then x + y = -1
x $\ge$ 0, y $\le$ 0, then x - y = 2
x $\le$ 0, y $\ge$ 0, then x - y = -2
Clearly these lines form a square, whose coordinates are (1, 1), (1, -1),(-1, -1), (-1, 1)
Hence its area is 4 $\times$ [$\frac{1}{2}$]1 $\times$ 1 = 2 sq units

Q10. If a , b , c are in A . P. then straight line ax + by + c = 0 will always pass through a fixed point whose coordinates are
    (A) ( -1 ,2 )
    (B) ( 1 , - 2 )   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ( - 1 , - 2 )
    (D) ( 1 , 2 )
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since a,b,c are in A.P,
a+c = 2b
This implies a-2b+c = 0
This implies the the family of lines is concurrent at (1,2)

Q11. The line segment joining the points (1, 2) and (-2, 1) is divided by the line 3x + 4y = 7 in the ratio
    (A) 4 : 9   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 3 : 4
    (C) 4 : 3
    (D) 9 : 4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let the line divide in the ratio k:1
By applying section formula $k.x_2 -1.x_1\over k+1$, $k.y_2-1.y_1\over k+1$
Substituting the values
$-2k+1\over k+1$, $k+2\over k+1$
This given line 3x + 4y = 7 passes through this point.
Hence, 3($-2k+1\over k+1$) + 4($k+2\over k+1$ )= 7
On simplifying, we get,
k = $\frac {4}{9}$
Hence the ratio is 4 : 9

Q12. A line L passes through the points (1, 1) and (2, 0) and another line M which is perpendicular to L passes through the point (1/2, 0). The area of the triangle formed by these lines with y axis is :
    (A) 25/10
    (B) 25/16   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 25/4
    (D) 25/8
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation of the line joining the two points (x_1, y_1) and (x_2, y_2) is
$y - y_1 \over y_2 - y_1$ = $x-x_1\over x_2 - x_1$
The given points are (1, 1) and (2, 0)
On substituting the values we get
$y-1\over 0-1$ = $x-1\over 2-1 $
On simplifying we get,
x + y - 2 = 0
The line which is perpendicular to this line is x - y + k = 0
Since it passes through (1/2, 0)
(1/2) - 0 = k
This implies k = -1/2
Hence the equation of this line is x - y - 1/2 = 0
On solving these twolines we get the point of intersection as (5/4, 3/4)
The point which line x + y - 2 = 0 cuts the Y axis is (0, 2) and the point which the line x - y - 1/2 = 0 cuts the Y axis is (0, -1/2)
Hend e the area of the triangle = [1/2] x [5/4] x [5/4] = 25/16 squnits

Q13. The medians AD and BE of a triangle with vertices A ( 0 , b ) , B ( 0, 0 ) and C ( a , 0 )are perpendicular to each other if
    (A) $a = \sqrt { - 2} b$
    (B) $a = \pm \sqrt 2 b$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $b = \sqrt { - 2} a$
    (D) $b = \pm \sqrt 2 a$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let D be the midpoint of BC. Hence its midpoint is ($0+a\over2$,0) = ($a\over2$,0)
Let E be the midpoint of AC. Hence its midpoint is ($0+a\over2$,$0+b\over2$) = ($a\over2$,$b\over2$)
Slope of the median AD is $b-0\over (a/2)-0$ = -$2b\over a$
Sope of BE = $(a/2)-0\over(b/2)-0$= $b\over a$
If BE and AD are perpendicular to each other then their product is -1
i.e;- $2b\over a$ x $b\over a$ = -1
This implies 2b^2 = a^2
a = $\pm\sqrt2$b

Q14. The straight lines x + y = 0, 3x + y – 4 = 0, x + 3y – 4 = 0 form a triangle which is
    (A) isosceles   <-- CORRECT
    (B) right angled
    (C) equilateral
    (D) Scalene
    Answer: A
    Explanation: On solving lines 1 and 2 we get the point of intersection as (-2, 2)
On solving the lines 2 and 3 we get, the point of intersection as (2, -2)
On solving lines 3 and 1 we get the point of intersection as (1, 1)
Now using distance formula we get AB = $\sqrt{(2-(-2))^2+(-2-2)^2}$ = $\sqrt 8$ 
Similarly, BC = $\sqrt{(1-2)^2+(1-(-2))^2}$ = $\sqrt{10}$ 
Similarly, AC = $\sqrt{(-2-1)^2+(2-1)^2}$= $\sqrt {10}$ 
Since AB = AC, it is an isosceles triangle.

Q15. The line which is parallel to X-axis and crosses the curve y = $\sqrt x $ at an angle of 45^o is:
    (A) y = $\frac{3}{2}$
    (B) y = $\frac{1}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) y = 1
    (D) y = $\frac 14$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation of the line which is a tangent to the curve y = $\sqrt x$ is
y = mx + a/m
Since it makes and angle of 45^o, m = 1
y^2 = x implies a = $\frac{1}{4}$
Hence the equation of the tangent is y = x + $\frac 14$
That is the y-intercept is $\sqrt \frac 14$ = $\frac{1}{2} $
Hence the equation of the line is y = $\frac{1}{2} $

Straight Lines Test 05  (id 651) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Straight Lines
Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. Two opposite vertices of a rectangle are (1, 3), (5, 1). If the equation of a diagonal of this rectangle is y = 2x + c, then the value of c is
    (A) 2
    (B) 1
    (C) -9
    (D) - 4   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Slope of the line joining the given points (1, 3) and (5, 1) is $1-3\over 5-1$ = $\frac{-1}{2}$
Hence the line having slope $\frac{-1}{2}$ is y = [$\frac{-1}{2}$]x + c
If the diagonal is y = 2x + c, then c = -4

Q2. The sum of all the two-digit numbers is
    (A) 4895
    (B) 4315
    (C) 4605
    (D) 4905   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The two digit numbers forms on A.P with a = 10, a_n = 99 and d = 1
Now a_n = a + (n - 1)d $\Rightarrow$ 99 = 10 + (n - 1) $\Rightarrow$ n = 99 - 9 = 90
We have S_n = $\frac {n}{2}$[2a + (n - 1)d]
$\Rightarrow$ S_90 = $\frac {n}{2}$[20 + (90 - 1)1]
$\Rightarrow$ S_90 = $\frac {90}{2}$ $\times$ 109 = 4905

Q3. The points (- a, -b), (0, 0), (a, b) and (a^2, ab) are
    (A) vertices of a square
    (B) collinear   <-- CORRECT
    (C) vertices of a parallelogram
    (D) vertices of a rectangle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Consider the points (a, b), (0, 0), (-a, -b)
It is clear that (0, 0) is the midpoint of (a, b) and (-a, -b)
This implies that these three points are collinear
Now consider the points,
(a, b), (a^2, ab) and (-a, -b)
If three points are collinear then the area of the triangle formed by these points is zero.
That is $1\over 2$[x_1(y_2 - y_3) + x_2(y_3 - y_1) + x_3(y_1 - y_2)]= 0
Substituting the values
$1\over 2$[a(a + b) + a^2(-b - b) + (-a)(b - ab)]
On expanding and simplifying we get the value to be zero.
Hence these points are collinear.

Q4. The distance between the lines 3x + 4y = 9 and 6x + 8y = 15 is
    (A) $\frac{2}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{7}{10}$
    (C) $\frac{3}{10}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{3}{2}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Distance between two parallel lies is given by $|c_1-c_2|\over \sqrt{A^2+B^2}$ 
The given lines are parallel where c_1 = 9 and c_2 = $\frac{15}{2}$
Sustituting the values 
d = $|9-15/2|\over \sqrt{9+16}$ = $\frac{3}{10}$

Q5. The locus of a point, whose abscissa and ordinate are always equal is
    (A) x + y = 1
    (B) x + y - 1 = 0
    (C) x + y + 1 = 0
    (D) x – y = 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The abscissa is equal to the ordinate implies x = y
Hence, the locus is x - y = 0

Q6. The ortho centre of the triangle formed by lines xy = 0 and x + y = 1 is :
    (A) ($\frac{1}{3}$, $\frac{1}{3}$)
    (B) (0, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ($\frac{1}{4}$, $\frac{1}{4}$)
    (D) ($\frac{1}{2}$, $\frac{1}{2}$)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given xy = 0 and x + y = 1, indicates that the straight line passes through (1, 0) and (0, 1). Hence it is a right-angled triangle whose vertex is the origin. Therefore the orthocenter is also at the origin (0, 0), this is one of the properties of right-angled triangle whose vertex is the origin.

Q7. The straight-line 3x + y = 9 divides the line segment joining the points (1, 3) and (2, 7) in the ratio
    (A) 5 : 4
    (B) 4 : 2
    (C) 3 : 4   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4 : 5
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let the point be (x, y) and the ratio it divides (1, 3) and (2, 7) be k : 1
By section formula, x = $2k+1\over k+1$, y = $7k+3\over k+1$ 
his point also lies on the given line so it would satisfy the equation 3x + y - 9 = 0
3(2k + 1) + (7k + 3) - 9(k + 1) = 0
k = $\frac{3}{4}$
Hence the ratio is ratio = 3 : 4

Q8. In a $\Delta ABC,$ if A is the point (1, 2) and equations of the median through B and C are respectively x + y = 5 and x = 4, then B is
    (A) (-2, 7)
    (B) (1, 4)
    (C) (4, 1)
    (D) (7, - 2)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let F be the midpoint on AC
Hence the coordinate of F is $\frac{x_1 + 1}{2}$ and $\frac{5-x_1 + 2}{2}$
This point lies on x = 4
Therefore $\frac{x_1 + 1}{2}$ = 4
Therefore x_1 = 7 
Therefore y = 5 - 7 = -2
Hence the coordinates of B is (7, -2)

Q9. The ratio of the ${{\rm{7}}^{{\rm{th}}}}$ to the (n - 1)th mean between 1 and 31, when n arithmetic means are inserted between them, is 5 : 9. The value of n is
    (A) 12
    (B) 13
    (C) 14   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 15
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let A_1, A_2, A_3, A_4 ..., A_n be the n arithmetic means inserted between 1 and 31.
The we have 1, A_1, A_2, A_3, A_4 ..., A_n, 31 is an A.P with a = 1, T_n = 31 and number of terms = n + 2
Now, T_n = 31 $\Rightarrow$ 1 + [(n + 2) - 1]d = 31
$\Rightarrow$ d = $\frac{30}{n+1}$
Hence we get T_7 = a + 7d = 1 + 7$\left[\frac{30}{n+1}\right]$ ...(i)
And T_n - 1 = a(n - 1) + d = 1 + (n - 1)$\left[\frac{30}{n+1}\right]$ ...(ii)
Given $\frac{T_{7}}{T_{n-1}}=\frac{5}{9}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{1+7\left[\frac{30}{n+1}\right]}{1+(n-1)\left[\frac{30}{n+1}\right]}=\frac{5}{9}$
$\Rightarrow \frac{\frac{n+1+210}{n+1}}{\frac{31 n-29}{n+1}}=\frac{5}{9}$
$\Rightarrow$ 9n + 1899 = 155n - 145
$\Rightarrow$ 2044 = 146 n
$\Rightarrow$ n = $\frac{2044}{146}$ = 14

Q10. The point on the axis of y which is equidistant from (- 1, 2) and (3, 4) is
    (A) (4, 0)
    (B) (0, 4)
    (C) (5, 0)
    (D) (0, 5)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let (0, y) be the point on Y-axis which is equidistant from the points (-1, 2) and (3, 4)
By applying the distance formula,
(0 + 1)^2 + (y - 2)^2 = (3 - 0)^2 + (4 - y)^2
on simplifying we get
4y = 20
Therefore y = 5
Hence the point on the y-axis is (0, 5)

Q11. Given the three straight lines with equations 5x + 4y = 0, x + 2y – 10 = 0 and 2x + y + 5 = 0, then these lines are
    (A) the sides of a right angled triangle
    (B) the sides of an equilateral triangle
    (C) the sides of an isosceles triangle
    (D) concurrent   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The lines are said to be concurrent $\begin{vmatrix} 5 & 4 & 0\\ 1 & 2 & -10\\ 2 & 1 & 5\\ \end{vmatrix} $ = 0
On expanding we get 
5(10 + 10) -4(5 + 20) + 0 = 0
Hence the lines are concurrent.

Q12. A line passes through (2,2) and is perpendicular to the line 3x+y=3, then its y intercept is
    (A) 1/3
    (B) 2/3
    (C) 4/3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The line which is perpendicular to the given line is x-3y+k=0
This passes through the point (2,2)
Substituting the values,
2-3(2)+k=0
k = 4
Hence the equation of the line is x-3y+4=0
This can be written as $x\over-4$+$y\over4/3$ = 1
Hence the y intercept is 4/3

Q13. The angle between the two straight lines 6y^2 - xy - x^2 + 30y + 36 = 0 is
    (A) 60^o
    (B) 30^o
    (C) 50^o
    (D) 45^o   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Consider the equation -x^2 + xy + 6y^2 = 0 or x^2 - xy - 6y^2 = 0
On factorizing we get,
(x - 3y)(x + 2y) = 0
Hence, the equation of the pair of straight lines is given by 
x - 3y + l = 0 and x + 2y + m = 0
Hence, the slope of these lines are $\frac{1}{3}$ and $\frac{-1}{2}$ respectively.
The angle between the straight lines is given by,
$tan \theta$ = $m_1 -m_2\over 1+m_1m_2$ = $1/3 - (-1/2)\over 1+(1/3)(-1/2)$ = 1
Hence, the angle is 45^o.

Q14. Area of a triangle is 5 sq. units. Its two vertices are (2, 1) and (3, - 2). Third vertex is on the line y = x + 3. The coordinates of that vertex are
    (A) ($\frac{8}{3}$, $\frac{5}{3}$)
    (B) (8, 14)
    (C) ($\frac{7}{2}$, $\frac{13}{2}$)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ($\frac{8}{5}$, $\frac{6}{5}$)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Area of a triangle whose vertices are (x_1, y_1), (x_2, y_2) and (x_3, y_3) is
$1\over 2$[x_1(y_2 - y_3) + x_2(y_3 - y_1) + x_3(y_1 - y_2)
The given veritces are (x, y), (2, 1), (3, -2) and area is 5 sq units
Substituting the values we get
5 = $1\over 2$[(x(1 + 2) + 2(-2 - y) + 3(y - 1)]
That is 10 = 3x + y - 7
or 3x + y = 17
The third vertex passes lies on the line y = x + 3
On solving the equations we get,
x = $\frac{7}{2}$ and y = $\frac{13}{2}$
Hence, the third vertex is ($\frac{7}{2}$, $\frac{13}{2}$)

Q15. The foot of the perpendicular from (2, 3) on the line 3x + 4y – 6 = 0 is
    (A) $(\frac {14} {25}, \frac {27} {25})$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $(\frac {14} {25}, - \frac {27} {25})$
    (C) $( - \frac {14} {25}, - \frac {27} {25})$
    (D) $( - \frac {14} {25}, \frac {29} {25})$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The equation of the line perpendicular to the given line 3x + 4y = 6 is 4x - 3y + k = 0
Since this line passes through (2, 3)
4(2) - 3(3) + k = 0
Therefore k = 1
Therefore the line which is perpendicular to the given line is 4x - 3y + 1 = 0
On solving both the equations we get, x = $\frac{14}{25}$ and y = $\frac{27}{25}$
Hence the foot of the perpendicular is ($\frac{14}{25}$, $\frac{27}{25}$)

CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Conic Sections

Q1. If the line 2x – y + $\lambda $ = 0 is a diameter of the circle x^2 + y^2 + 6x - 6y + 5 = 0 then $\lambda $ =
    (A) 3
    (B) 6
    (C) 9   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 12
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Equation of circle is x^2 + y^2 + 6x - 6y + 5 = 0 
x^2 + 6x + y^2 - 6y = -5
Applying completing the square method
(x + 3)^2 + (y - 3)^2 = $(\sqrt{13})^{2}$ 
Comparing the above equation with (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = (r)^2 we get center as (-3, 3) and radius as $\sqrt{13}$
As the centre of the circle lies on diameter, it will satisfy the equation of diameter, so on putting (-3, 3) in the equation of diameter we get 
2(-3) - (3) + $\lambda$ = 0
$\Rightarrow$ -6 - 3 - $\lambda$ = 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\lambda$ = 9

Q2. Length of common chord of the circles x^2 + y^2 + 2x + 6y = 0 and x^2 + y^2 - 4x - 2y - 6 = 0 is
    (A) $2\sqrt {106} $
    (B) $\frac 15\sqrt {106} $
    (C) $\frac {2}{5}\sqrt {106} $   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\sqrt {106} $
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 + 2x + 6y = 0
x^2 + 2x + y^2 + 6y = 0
Applying the completing the square
(x + 1)^2 + (y + 3)^2 = $(\sqrt{10})^{2}$
Comparing the above equation with (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2, we get its center as (-1, -3) and radius (r_1) =$\sqrt{10}$ 
x^2 + y^2 - 4x - 2y - 6 = 0
(x - 2)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = $(\sqrt{11})^{2}$
Comparing the above equation with (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2 we get its center as (2, 1) and radius (r_2) =$\sqrt{11}$ 
So distance(d) between the centers is ​$\sqrt{(2+1)^2+(1+3)^2}$​ = 5 units
After applying the general formula of the length of common chord as ${\sqrt \frac {(d^2-(r_1-r_2)^2)((r_1+r_2)^2-d^2)} {d}}$ and putting the values of r_1, r_2 and d we get length as ${\frac 25}\sqrt {106} $.

Q3. The circles x^2 + y^2 + 6x + 6y = 0 and x^2 + y^2 - 12x - 12y = 0
    (A) cut orthogonally
    (B) intersect in two points
    (C) touch each other externally   <-- CORRECT
    (D) touch each other internally
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Circle touches externally if distance between the centers is equal to the sum of the radii.
x^2 + y^2 + 6x + 6y = 0
x^2 + 6x + y^2 + 6y = 0
After applying completing the square, we get
(x + 3)^2 + (y + 3)^2 = $(3 \sqrt{2})^{2}$ 
So the center is (-3, -3) and radius is $ 3\sqrt{2}$ 
x^2 + y^2 - 12x - 12y = 0
x^2 - 12x + y^2 - 12y = 0
After applying completing the square
(x - 6)^2 + (y - 6)^2 = $(6 \sqrt{2})^{2}$ 
So the center is (6, 6) and radius is $6\sqrt{2}$ 
Distance between centres ​$\sqrt{(6+3)^2+(6+3)^2}=9\sqrt{2}$​ and sum of radii ($3\sqrt {2}+6\sqrt {2} =9\sqrt{2}$ ) are equal.
Hence the circle touches externally.

Q4. The equation x^2 + y^2 = 0 represents
    (A) an equilateral hyperbola
    (B) a degenerate circle   <-- CORRECT
    (C) pairs of straight line
    (D) an ellipse
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The above circle can be written as (x - 0)^2 + (y - 0)^2 = (0)^2 
Here the center is (0, 0) and radius is also 0 units.
So it is a degenerate circle as a degenerate circle is a circle( a point) where the radius is zero units.

Q5. The equation (x^2 + y^2) + 5x - 7y - 2 = 0 represents
    (A) an empty set
    (B) a circle   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a degenerate circle
    (D) a pair of straight lines
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The general equation of the circle is x^2 + y^2 - 2gh - 2fy + c = 0. Since the given equations satisfy the general equation, it represents the equation of the circle.

Q6. Circumcentre of the triangle, whose vertices are (0, 0), (6, 0) and (0, 4) is
    (A) (0, 3)
    (B) (3, 0)
    (C) (3, 2)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (2, 0)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Circumcentre of a right-angled triangle ABC right angled at A is $b+c\over2$ as circumcentre of right-angled triangle lies on the mid point of the hypotenuse.
So mid point of BC = ($6+0\over2$,$0+4\over2$) i.e.(3, 2)

Q7. If (x - a)^2 + (y - b)^2 = c^2 represents a circle, then
    (A) b = 0
    (B) a = b = 0
    (C) a = 0
    (D) c $ \ne $ 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: (x - a)^2 + (y - b)^2 = c^2 here (a, b) is center and c is the radius and radius cannot be zero because if radius is zero it will become a point or degenerate circle so c $ \ne $ 0.

Q8. The length of the chord joining the point ( 4 cos $\theta $, 4 sin $\theta $) and 4 ( cos($\theta $+${60^o}$), 4 sin($\theta $ + ${60^o}$)) of the circle ${x^2} + {y^2} = 16$ is
    (A) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) 8
    (D) 16
    Answer: A
    Explanation: using distance formulae $\sqrt{(x_2-x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}$$ =\sqrt{[(4cos\theta - 4cos(\theta + 60)^2 + (4sin\theta - 4sin(\theta+60)^2]}$
on simplifying we get, $\sqrt{16 + 16 -32.-(1/2)}$$$ = 4

Q9. Two perpendicular tangents to the circle ${x^2} + {y^2} = {r^2}$ meet at P. The locus of P is
    (A) ${x^2} + {y^2} = 4\;{r^2}$
    (B) x + y = r
    (C) ${x^2} + {y^2} = \frac {r^2}{2}$
    (D) ${x^2} + {y^2} = 2\;{r^2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: locus of P is a circle with centre at origin and radius $\sqrt{2r^2}$. This is known as the director circle of the circle ${x^2} + {y^2} = {r^2}$

Q10. The number of tangents to the circle x^2 + y^2 - 8x - 6y + 9 = 0, which pass through the point (3, - 2), is
    (A) 2   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 1
    (C) 0
    (D) 3
    Answer: A
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 - 8x - 6y + 9 = 0
After completing the square, we get
(x - 4)^2 + (y - 3)^2 = (4)^2 
So the center is (4, 3) and radius is 4.
Distance between the center and the given point $\sqrt{(4-3)^2+(3+2)^2}=\sqrt{26}$ which is greater than 4.
Hence point lies outside the circle.
Since point lies outside of the circle there will be 2 tangents since two tangents can be drawn from external point to a circle.

Q11. The value of k, such that the equation 2x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x + 8y + k = 0 represents a point circle, is
    (A) $ -\frac {25} {2}$
    (B) 0
    (C) $\frac {25} {2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 25
    Answer: C
    Explanation: ​2x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x + 8y + k = 0​
x^2 - 3x + y^2 + 4y = $\frac{-k}{2}$ 
(x - 1.5)^2 + (y + 2)^2 = $\frac{-k}{2}+\frac{9}{4}+4$ 
Which gives radius = $\sqrt{\frac{-k}{2}+\frac{9}{4}+4}$ 
For a point circle radius should be zero.
Hence $\frac{-k}{2}+\frac{9}{4}+4$ = 0
Solving which we get k = $\frac {25} {2}$

Q12. The equation $a{x^2} + b{y^2} + 2hxy + 2gx + 2fy + c = 0$ represents a circle only if
    (A) a = b $ \ne $ 0, h = 0
    (B) a = b , h = 0
    (C) a = b $ \ne $ 0, h = 0, g^2 + f^2 - c > 0
    (D) a = b $\neq$ 0,h = 0, g^2 + f^2 - ac > 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Recalling the general form of a circle as
 It is a quadratic equation in both x and y.
 Coefficient of $x^2 $
 = Coefficient of $y^2 $ .
 There is no term containing xy i.e., the coefficient of xy is zero.
 radius is $\mathrm{\frac{1}{a}\sqrt{g^{2} + f^{2} - ca}}$ 
To satisfy (i) and (ii) condition we have $a = b \ne 0$ 
To satisfy (iii) condition we have $h = 0$
To satisfy (iv) and as we cant have a negative sign in root so g^2 + f^2 - ac > 0

Q13. x^2 + y^2 - 6x + 8y - 11 = 0 is a circle. The points (0, 0) and (1, 8) lie
    (A) both outside the circle
    (B) one outside the circle and one inside   <-- CORRECT
    (C) both inside the circle
    (D) one on the circle and the other outside
    Answer: B
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 - 6x + 8y - 11 = 0
x^2 - 6x + y^2 + 8y = 11
(x - 3)^2 + (y + 4)^2 = (6)^2
So the center is (3, -4) and radius is 6 units.
Distance between center and (0, 0) is $\sqrt{3-0)^2+(-4-0)^2}$ = 5 units which is less than the radius so it lies inside the circle.
Whereas the distance between center and (1, 8) is $\sqrt{(3-1)^2 +(8-(-4))^2}$ = $\sqrt{148}$ which is greater than the radius so it lies outside the circle

Q14. The length of tangent from the point (2, -3) to the circle 2x^2 + 2y^2 = 1 is
    (A) $\frac {5} {\sqrt 2 }$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) - 5
    (C) 5
    (D) $ - \frac {5} {\sqrt 2 }$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: 2x^2 + 2y^2 = 1
Applying completing the square method, we get
(x - 0)^2 + (y - 0)^2 = $ \frac{1}{2}$
So it has center (0, 0) and radius $\frac {1}{\sqrt{2}} $ 
Let O = (0, 0) be the center, A = (2, -3) be the external point and B be the point of contact of tangent and circle.
OAB forms a triangle with angle OBA = 90° (as The angle between the tangent and radius is 90°) and distance OA =${\sqrt{13}} $ units (using distance formula) and OB = $\frac {1}{\sqrt{2}} $ units(radius)
Length of tangent = AB
Using Pythagoras theorem,
OA^2 = OB^2 + AB^2
$\Rightarrow$ AB^2 = OA^2 - OB^2
Putting the values of OA and OB = AB^2 = 13 - $\frac 12$ = $\frac {25}{2}$
Therefore AB = $\frac{5}{\sqrt{2}} $

Q15. Which one of the following lines is farthest from the centre of the circle x^2 + y^2 = 10?
    (A) 3x + 4y – 15 = 0
    (B) x + y = 1
    (C) x + $ \sqrt 3 \;y $ + 7 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 12x + 5y + 26 = 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 = 10
After completing the square, we get
(x - 0)^2 + (y - 0)^2 = $(\sqrt{10})^{2}$ 
So center is (0, 0) and equation of given line is $x + \sqrt 3 \;y + 7 = 0$ 
By applying formula of the distance of a point from a given line i.e.,$Ax_1+By_1+C\over{\sqrt{A^2+B^2}}$ where(x_1, y_1) are the coordinates of point and A and B are coefficient of x,y in given line so d = $7\over{2}$ which is greatest.

Conic Sections Test 02  (id 653) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Conic Sections
