Q1. Which of the following lines is a normal to the circle (x - 1)^2 + (y - 2)^2 = 10
    (A) 2x + y = 3
    (B) x + y = 3   <-- CORRECT
    (C) x + 2y = 10
    (D) (x – 1) + (y – 2) = 10
    Answer: B
    Explanation: (x - 1)^2 + (y - 2)^2 = 10
Comparing the above equation with (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2 we get center as (1, 2) putting (1, 2) in L.H.S of above line, we get 1 + 2 = 3 = R.H.S
$\Rightarrow$ It satisfies the equation of line or the line passes through center and the line passing through the centre is normal.

Q2. A circle with its centre on the line y = x + 1 is drawn to pass through the origin and touch the line y = x + 2. The centre of the circle is
    (A) $\left( {{\frac 12},{\frac 12}} \right)$
    (B) (-1, 2)
    (C) $\left( { - {\frac 12},{\frac 12}} \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (-1, 0)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2 be the equation of circle with (h, k) as the center and r be the radius.
As the center lies on the line y = x + 1
$\Rightarrow$ k = h + 1 or k = 1 + h ...(i)
Circle passes through origin so (0, 0) will satisfy the equation of line so putting (0, 0) in the equation of circle we get (h)^2 + (k)^2 = r^2 .....(ii)
putting k from (i) into (ii), we get
h^2 + (h + 1)^2 = r^2 
2h^2 + 2h + 1 = r^2 ....(iii)
and as the circle touches the line y = x + 2 so radius should be equal to the distance from the center to this line.
$\Rightarrow$ r =$\frac {h-k+2}{\sqrt 2}$ 
putting value ok k from (i) in above equation, we get
r = $\frac {h-(h+1)+2}{\sqrt{2}}$ 
r = $\frac {1}{\sqrt{2}}$ 
putting the value of r in (iii)
2h^2 + 2h + 1 = $\frac{1}{2}$ 
2h^2 + 4h + 1 = 0
2h^2 + 2h + 2h + 1 = 0
(2h + 1)(2h = 1) = 0 which gives h = $\frac{-1}{2}$ putting h in (i) we get k = $\frac{1}{2}$ 
Hence center is $(\frac{-1}{2},\frac{1}{2})$

Q3. Four distinct points $(2\lambda ,3\lambda )$, (1, 0), (0, 1) and (0, 0) lie on a circle for
    (A) only one value of $\lambda $
    (B) $\lambda $ < 0
    (C) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 0 $<$ $\lambda $$<$1
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Because the equation of circle will be x^2 + y^2 - x - y = 0 which is a quadratic equation and by putting the given fourth point we will get two different values of $\lambda$. 
Proof: let equation of cirle be (x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2 
As (1, 0) (0, 1) and (0, 0) lie on circle, we get
(1 - h)^2 + k^2 = r^2 ....(i)
h^2 + (1 - k)^2 = r^2 ....(ii)
h^2 + k^2 = r^2 ....(iii)
Comparing (i) and (iii) , we get h =$\frac{1}{2}$ 
Comparing (ii) and (iii) we get k =$\frac{1}{2}$ 
putting the value of h and k in (iii) we get $r^2=\frac{1}{4}$ 
Hence we get the equation of circle as (2x - 1 )^2 + (2y - 1)^2 = 1 
Now putting $(2\lambda ,3\lambda )$in above circle, we get
$(4\lambda-1)^2+(6\lambda-1)^2=1$ 
Which is quadratic and will give 2 values of $\lambda$

Q4. The locus of the point of intersection of the lines x cos $\alpha $ + y sin $\alpha = a$ and x sin $\alpha $ - y cos $\alpha $ = b is
    (A) an ellipse
    (B) a straight line
    (C) a circle   <-- CORRECT
    (D) A parabola
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Solving the above two equations we get,
x = $a\cos \alpha - b\sin \alpha$ .....(i) 
y = $ a\sin \alpha - b\cos \alpha$ .....(ii)
Squaring both sides of (i) and (ii) and adding both the equation we get x^2 + y^2 = a^2 + b^2.
Which represents the locus of circle as
 it is a quadratic equation
 coeff of x^2 = coeff of y^2
 there is no term involving xy.

Q5. The line y = mx + c is a normal to the circle x^2 + y^2 + 2gx + 2fy + c = 0, if
    (A) mg $ \ne $ c + f
    (B) c $\ne$ 0
    (C) c = 0
    (D) mg = c + f   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 + 2gx = 2fy + c = 0 has center (-g, -f)
As normal passes through the center so center will satisfy the equation of normal put y = -f and x = -g in equation of the line y = mx + c
-f = m(-g) + c
Which gives mg = f + c.

Q6. The line 3x – 4y = 0
    (A) is a normal to the circle x^2 + y^2 = 25   <-- CORRECT
    (B) is a tangent to the circle x^2 + y^2 = 25
    (C) does not pass through the origin
    (D) does not meet the circle x^2 + y^2 = 25
    Answer: A
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 = 25
After completing the square, we get
(x - 0)^2 + (y - 0)^2 = 5^2 
So the center is (0, 0) and the radius is 5 units.
As the normal should pass through the centre of the circle, the center should satisfy the equation of normal.
So 3x – 4y = 0 is the equation of normal as (0, 0) satisfy this equation.

Q7. The equations x = a cos $\theta $ + b sin $\theta $ , and $y = a\sin \theta - b\cos \theta $ , 0 $ \le $ $\theta $ $ \le $ 2 $\pi $ represent
    (A) a parabola
    (B) a circle   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) an ellipse
    Answer: B
    Explanation: x = a cos $\theta $ + b sin $\theta $ , and $y = a\sin \theta - b\cos \theta $ 
Putting the value of x and y in x^2 + y^2 
$ (a\cos \theta + b\sin \theta)^2+( a\sin \theta - b\cos \theta)^2 $ we get a^2+b^2
$\Rightarrow$ x^2 + y^2 = a^2 + b^2
Which is quadratic in nature, coefficient of x^2 = coefficient of y^2 and no term involving xy
Hence its locus represents a circle.

Q8. If the lines 3x - 4y + 4 = 0 and 6x - 8y - 7 = 0 are tangents to the circle then the radius of the circle is
    (A) $\frac{3}{4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{2}{3}$
    (C) $\frac{4}{3}$
    (D) $\frac{3}{2}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The given lines are parallel. Hence the tangents are parallel tangents. Distance between these lines is equal to the diameter
D = $|8 - (-7)|\over \sqrt{36+64}$ = $\frac{3}{2}$ 
Therefore, the radius is $\frac{3}{4}$

Q9. A circle passes through (0, 0) ( a, 0), (0, b). The coordinates of its centre are
    (A) (- a, - b)
    (B) (a, b)
    (C) $\left( \frac a 2, \frac b2 \right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (b, a)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Because line joining the points (a, 0) and (0, b) will be diameter and it's mid-point will be centre of the circle.
Or
let the equation of circle be $(x-h)^2+(y-k)^2=r^2$ 
as circle passes through (0, 0), (a, 0) and (0, b), they will satisfy the above equation
putting the points in above equation we get
$h^2+k^2=r^2$ ...(i)
$(a-h)^2+k^2=r^2$ ...(ii)
$h^2+(b-k)^2=r^2$ ...(iii)
Solving (i) and (ii), we get h = $\frac a2$
whereas solving (i) and (iii) we get k = $\frac b2$
hence its center is $\left( \frac a2, \frac b2 \right)$

Q10. The focus of the parabola x^2 - 8x + 2y + 7 = 0 is
    (A) (4, 4)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\left( {0, -\frac {1}{2}} \right)$
    (C) $\left( {4,\frac{9}{2}} \right)$
    (D) $\left( { - 4, - \frac{9}{2}} \right)$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: x^2 - 8x + 2y + 7 = 0
x^2 - 8x = -2y - 7
After completing the square we get,
(x - 4)^2 = -2y + 9
(x - 4)^2 = $-4 \frac{1}{2}\left(y-\frac{9}{2}\right)$ 
Comparing the above equation with x^2 = -4ay focus is (0, -a)
Putting x co-ordinate = 0 we get x - 4 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ x = 4
and y co-ordinate = -a we get $(y -\frac{ 9}{2})=-\frac{1}{2} $ 
$\Rightarrow$ y = 4
Hence (4, 4) is the focus.

Q11. The radius of the circle passing through the foci of the ellipse $\frac{x^2}{16}+\frac{y^2}{9}$ = 1 and having its centre at (0, 3) is
    (A) 3
    (B) 4   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\sqrt {12} $
    (D) $\frac 7 2$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\frac{x^2}{16}+\frac{y^2}{9}$ = 1
Comparing with the standard equation we get a = 4 and b = 3 we get c =$\sqrt{16-9}$ = $\sqrt{7}$ 
So focus is $(\sqrt{7},0)$ and the given centre is (0, 3).
Using distance formulae. we get radius = 4 units

Q12. The line y = c is a tangent to the parabola x^2 = y - 1 if c is equal to
    (A) c = 1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a
    (C) 0
    (D) 2a
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Putting the value y = c into parabola, we get
x^2 = c - 1
or x^2 - (c - 1) = 0
Here discriminat =$\sqrt{4c-4}$ 
Line y = c is tangent when the discriminant is equal to 0.
Putting discriminant = 0 we get c = 1.
(0, c) will be a point on the parabola.

Q13. The area of the circle centred at (1,2) and passing through (4,6) is
    (A) $5\pi$ sq units
    (B) $10\pi$ sq units
    (C) $15\pi$ sq units
    (D) $25\pi$ sq units   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given centre = (1,2)
Therefore radius = $\sqrt{(4-1)^2 + (6 - 2)^2}$ = 5 units
Area of the circle is $\pi r^2$ = $25\pi$ sq units

Q14. The locus of a variable point whose distance from the point (2, 0) is $\frac {2}{ 3}$ times its distance from the line x = $\frac 9 2$ is
    (A) a parabola
    (B) a circle
    (C) an ellipse   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a hyperbola
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let the point be (x, y)
Hence (x - 2)^2 + (y - 0)^2 = $\frac{2}{3} \frac{(x-9 / 2)}{\sqrt{1}^2}$ 
(x - 2)^2 + y^2 = $\frac 2 3$(x - $\frac{9}{2}$)
On simplifying we get the equation of an ellipse

Q15. The equation of a circle with origin as centre and passing through the vertices of an equilateral triangle whose median is of length 3a is [Hint: Centroid of the triangle coincides with the centre of the circle and the radius of the circle is $\frac{2}{3}$ of the length of the median]
    (A) $x ^ { 2 } + y ^ { 2 } = 16 a ^ { 2 }$
    (B) $x ^ { 2 } + y ^ { 2 } = a ^ { 2 }$
    (C) $x ^ { 2 } + y ^ { 2 } = 9 a ^ { 2 }$
    (D) $x ^ { 2 } + y ^ { 2 } = 4 a ^ { 2 }$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $x ^ { 2 } + y ^ { 2 } = 4 a ^ { 2 }$

Conic Sections Test 03  (id 654) [PAID]
CBSE > Class 11 > Mathematics > Conic Sections

Q1. A and B are two distinct points, Locus of a point P satisfying |PA| + | PB| = 2k, a constant is
    (A) nothing can be said as we will not get any specific equation as k is not specified   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the line segment [AB]
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) an ellipse
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Since the value of k is not specified, we cannot get a specific equation.

Q2. The eccentricity of the hyperbola x^2 - y^2 = 9 is
    (A) $\sqrt 2 $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) More than 1
    (C) 1
    (D) less than 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: x^2 - y^2 = 9
above equation can be written as,
$\frac{x^2}{(3)^2} -\frac {y^2}{(3)^2} $ = 1
Comparing it with the standard equation we get a = 3 and b = 3
As c =$\sqrt{a^2+b^2}$ 
We get c = 3 $\sqrt 2 $ and as e = $\frac{c}{a}$ 
We get e = $\sqrt 2 $

Q3. The locus of the point of intersection of the lines $a x \sec \theta+b y \tan \theta=a$ and $a x \tan \theta+b y \sec \theta=b$ where $\theta$ is a parameter and
$a \neq b$ is $a(a n)$
    (A) A hyperbola   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a parabola
    (C) an ellipse
    (D) a straight line
    Answer: A
    Explanation: A hyperbola

Q4. The line y = mx + c, touches the parabola y^2 = 4ax if
    (A) c = am^2
    (B) $c = \frac{a}{{{m^2}}},m \ne 0$
    (C) c = am
    (D) $c = \frac{a}{m},m \ne 0$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: y = mx + c ......(i)
y^2 = 4ax ....(ii)
Putting the value of y from (i) in (ii), we get
(mx + c)^2 = 4ax
$\Rightarrow$ (mx)^2 + x(2mc - 4a) + c^2 = 0
Here discriminant =$\sqrt{(2mc-4a)^2-4m^2c^2}$ = $\sqrt{16a^2-16amc}$ 
When discriminant > 0 line touches parabola at two points, when discriminant < 0 lines do not touch parabola and when discriminant = 0 line touches parabola at one point and we know that tangent is a line that touches the curve at exactly one point.
So putting discriminate = 0 and solving
we get $c = \frac{a}{m},m \ne 0$ 
On putting the value of y from line in the parabola and solving for equal roots.

Q5. The equations x = at^2, y = 4at; t $\in$ R represent
    (A) an ellipse
    (B) a circle
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) a parabola   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: y = 4at
Squaring both sides, we get
y^2 = 16a^2t^2 
Putting the value of at^2 i.e. at^2 = $\frac{y^{2}}{16 a}$ in x = at^2 we get,
16ax = y^2 
or y^2 = 4(4a)x
Which is nothing but equation of parabola.

Q6. $x=\frac{e^t+e^{-t}}{2}, y=\frac{e^t-e^{-t}}{2} ; t \in R$ represents
    (A) a parabola
    (B) a hyperbola   <-- CORRECT
    (C) an ellipse
    (D) a circle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $x=\frac{e^t+e^{-t}}{2}, y=\frac{e^t-e^{-t}}{2} ; t \in R$ 
Squaring both sides of both the equation, we get
$$x^2 = $\frac {(e^t + e^-t)^2}{ 4}$ and y^2 = $\frac {(e^t - e^-t)^2}{4}$ 
Subtracting one equation from another we get
x^2 - y^2 = 1 which is nothing but equation of hyperbola.

Q7. The vertex of the parabola y^2 = 4a(x - a) is
    (A) (0, a)
    (B) (0, 0)
    (C) (a, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    (D) (a, a)
    Answer: C
    Explanation: y^2 = 4a(x - a)
Let Y = y and X = x - a
For standard parbola Y^2 = 4aX the vertex is (0, 0)
So put X = 0 and Y = 0.
i.e. put x - a = 0 and y = 0
So vertex is (a, 0)

Q8. The two parabolas x^2 = 4y and y^2 = 4x meet in two distinct points. One of these is the origin and the other is
    (A) (1, 1)
    (B) (3 ,3)
    (C) (2, 2)
    (D) (4, 4)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given, equations of the parabola are x^2 = 4y and y^2 = 4x ... (i)
$\therefore$ $\left(\frac{x^{2}}{4}\right)^{2}$ = 4x
$\Rightarrow$ x^4 - 64x = 0
$\Rightarrow$ x = 0, x = 4
On putting the values of x in Eq. (i), we get y = 0 and y = 4, −4
($\because$ y = −4 does not satisfy the equation x^2 = 4y)
Thus, the points of intersection are (0, 0) and (4, 4).
Hence, the point other than origin is (4, 4).

Q9. The equation of the directrix of the parabola x^2 = -4ay is
    (A) y – a = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x + a = 0
    (C) y + a = 0
    (D) x – a = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: From the equation, we infer that the parabola is open downward.
Hence the directrix passes through the point (0, a) and will be parallel to the X-axis. 
Hence the equation of the directrix is y = a or y - a = 0

Q10. The eccentricity e of a parabola is
    (A) Less than 1
    (B) More than 1
    (C) Zero
    (D) Equal to 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Eccentricity of a parabola is 1.

Q11. The ellipse = $\frac{x^2}{a^2}+\frac{y^2}{b^2}$ = 1, b^2 = a^2 is a
    (A) vertical ellipse
    (B) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) horizontal ellipse
    Answer: B
    Explanation: If a^2 = b^2, then the equation becomes x^2 + y^2 = a^2 which represents the equation of a circle.

Q12. The equations x = a cos $\theta $ , y = b sin $\theta $, 0 $≤$ $\theta $ <${\rm{2}}\pi $ , a $ \ne $ b, represent
    (A) a parabola
    (B) a circle
    (C) an ellipse   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a hyperbola
    Answer: C
    Explanation: parametric form of ellipse.

Q13. The graph of the function f(x) = $\frac 1 x$ i.e. the curve y = $\frac 1 x$ is
    (A) a parabola
    (B) an ellipse
    (C) a hyperbola   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a circle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: It is called rectangular hyperbola.

Q14. The line y = c touches the parabola y^2 = 4ax when
    (A) c > 0
    (B) c = 0
    (C) c < 0
    (D) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: When y = c, then it implies slope = 0. Hence the line should be parallel to the X-axis.
Therefore the line y = c, when m = 0.

Q15. The parabolas x^2 = 4y and y^2 = 4x intersect
    (A) on the line x + y = 0
    (B) in a unique point
    (C) on the line x - y = 0
    (D) on the line y = x   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Point of intersection is (0, 0) and (4, 4). This implies y = x. Hence, it intersects the line y = x.

Q1. The length of the common chord of the parabolas y^2 = x and x^2 = y is
    (A) $\sqrt 2 $   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $2\sqrt 2 $
    (C) 1
    (D) $4\sqrt 2 $
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Point of intersection is (0, 0) and (1, 1). Hence by using the distance formula
$\sqrt{(1^2-0)^2 + (1^2 + 0)^2}$ = $\sqrt2$

Q2. The number of points on X-axis which are at a distance c units (c < 3) from (2, 3) is
    (A) 3
    (B) 1
    (C) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The shortest distance from x-axis to the point is 3.

Q3. The eccentricity of the conic 9x^2 - 16y^2 = 144 is
    (A) $\sqrt 7 $
    (B) $\frac{5}{4}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{4}{3}$
    (D) $\frac{4}{5}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given 9x^2 - 16y^2 = 144
Dividing throughout by 144 we get,
$\frac{x^2}{16} $ - $\frac{y^2}{9}$ = 1
This implies a^2 = 16 and b^2 = 9
e = $\sqrt \frac{a^2 + b^2}{a}$ = $\frac{5}{4}$

Q4. The eccentricity of 3x^2 + 4y^2 = 24 is
    (A) $\frac{7}{4}$
    (B) $\sqrt\frac {7}{4} $
    (C) $\frac{1}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{1}{4}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Given equation is 3x^2 + 4y^2 = 24
Dividing throught by 24 we get,
$\frac{x^2}{8}$ + $\frac{y^2}{6}$ = 1
This implies a^2 = 8 and b^2 = 6
e = $\frac{\sqrt{a^2 - b^2}}{a}$ = $\frac{1}{2}$

Q5. The angle between the tangents drawn from the origin to the circle = (x - 7)^2 + (y + 1)^2 = 25 is
    (A) $\frac{\pi}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{\pi}{8}$
    (C) $\frac{\pi}{6}$
    (D) $\frac{\pi}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let tangent from origin be y = mx
Using the condition of tangency, we get
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{7 m+1}{\sqrt{m^{2}+1}}$ = 5
(7m + 1)^2 = 25(m^2 + 1)
$\Rightarrow$ 24m^2 + 14m - 24 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 12m^2 + 7m - 12 = 0
$\Rightarrow$ 12m^2 + 16m - 9m - 12 = 0
(4m - 3)(3m - 4)
$\therefore$ m = $\frac{3}{4}$ and m = -$\frac{4}{3}$ 
The angle between tangents = $\frac{\pi}{2}$

Q6. The line y = mx + 1 is a tangent to the parabola ${y^2} = 4x$ if m =
    (A) 1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 2
    (C) 3
    (D) 4
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The condition for a line to be a tangent to the parabola is y = mx +$a\over m$
From the given equation of the parabola we infer that a = 1 and from the equation of the line c = 1
Therefore m = a/c = 1

Q7. The equation x^2 - 7xy + 12y^2 = 0 represents a
    (A) pair of parallel straight lines
    (B) circle
    (C) pair of non-perpendicular intersecting straight lines   <-- CORRECT
    (D) pair of perpendicular straight lines
    Answer: C
    Explanation: On factorizing the given equation we get x - 4y = 0 and x - 3y = 0, which represents a pair of intersecting straight lines. Since the product of their slopes is not equal to -1, they are non-perpendicular.

Q8. The equation y^2 - x^2 + 2x - 1 = 0 represents
    (A) an ellipse
    (B) a pair of straight lines   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a parabola
    (D) a circle
    Answer: B
    Explanation: On factorizing the given equation we get y + x - 1 = 0 and y - x + 1 = 0, which clearly represents a pair of straight lines which are intersecting.

Q9. The length of latus rectum of an ellipse is one-third of its major axis. Its eccentricity would be
    (A) $\frac{2}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{ {\sqrt 3 }}$
    (C) $\frac{1}{{\sqrt 2 }}$
    (D) $\sqrt \frac{2}{3} $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\frac{2b^2}{a^2}$ = $\frac{2a}{3}$
Hence $\frac{b^2}{a^2}$ = $\frac{1}{3}$. Hence, e^2 = 1 - $\frac{b^2}{a^2}$= 1 - ($\frac{1}{3}$) = $\frac{2}{3}$ 
Therefore, e = $\sqrt\frac{2}{3}$

Q10. Three normals to the parabola y^2 = x are drawn through a point (c, 0) then
    (A) c = $\frac{3}{4}$
    (B) c > $\frac{1}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) c = $\frac{1}{2}$
    (D) c = $\frac{1}{4}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation of the normal to a parabola y^2 = 4ax is
y = mx - 2am - am^3
Hence the equation of the normal to the given parabola y^2 = x is 
mx - $\frac{m}{2}$ - $\frac{m^3}{4}$ 
Since it passes through (c, 0)
mc - $\frac{m}{2}$ - $\frac{m^3}{4}$ = 0
on solving we get 
m = 0 or m^2 = 4(c - $\frac{1}{2}$)
If m = 0 then the equation of the normal is y = 0
If m^2 $\ge$0, then 4(c - $\frac{1}{2}$) $\ge$0
Hence c - $\frac{1}{2}$ $\ge$0 or c > $\frac{1}{2}$

Q11. S and T are the foci of an ellipse and B is an end of the minor axis. If STB is an equilateral triangle, the eccentricity of the ellipse is
    (A) $\frac{2}{3}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{3}$
    (C) $\frac{1}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\frac{1}{4}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: s = (ae, 0) and T = (-ae, 0) and B = (0, b)
Since it is an equilateral triangle, ST^2 = TB^2
This implies 4a^2e^2 = a^2e^2 + b^2
3a^2e^2 = b^2 
3a^2e^2 = a^2(1 - e^2)
3e^2 = 1 - e^2
Therefore e = $\frac{1}{2}$

Q12. The centre of a circle passing through the points (0, 0), (1, 0) and touching the circle ${x^2} + {y^2} = 9$ is
    (A) $\left(\frac{1}{2}, \frac{1}{2}\right)$
    (B) $\left(\frac{1}{2},-\sqrt{2}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\left(\frac{1}{2}, \sqrt{2}\right)$
    (D) $\left(\frac{1}{2}, \frac{3}{2}\right)$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since the circle passes through (0, 0) the equation reduces to
c = 0 ....(1)
Since it passes through (1, 0),
1 + 2g + c = 0
This implies g = -1/2
Since the circle touches the circle x^2 + y^2 = 9, their radii should be equal
2$\sqrt{g^2 + f^2 + c}$ = 3
Substituting the values and simplifying we get f = $\pm\sqrt 2$
Hence the centre is $\left(\frac{1}{2},-\sqrt{2}\right)$

Q13. The number of tangents to the circle x^2 + y^2 - 2x + 4y = 0 through the point (-1, 2) is
    (A) 1
    (B) 2   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3
    (D) 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The given equation of the circle can be written as (x - 1)^2 - 1 + (y + 2)^2 - 4 = 0
(x - 1)^2 + (y + 2)^2 = 5
This implies the radius is $\sqrt 5$ and the centre is (1, -2)
The given point is (-1, 2)
The distance between the centre of the circle and the given point is
$\sqrt{(-1-1)^2 + (2+2)^2}$ = $\sqrt 20$ 
Since this is greater than the radius, the point lies outside the circle. Hence two tangents can be drawn.

Q14. The slope of the tangent at the point (a, a) of the circle ${x^2} + {y^2} = {a^2}$ is
    (A) -1   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -2
    (C) 0
    (D) depends upon h
    Answer: A
    Explanation: the equation of the tangent is x+y=a. Hence its slope is -1

Q15. The equation of the normal to the parabola y^2 = 8x having slope 1 is
    (A) x – y – 6 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) x – y + 6 = 0
    (C) x + y + 6 = 0
    (D) x + y – 6 = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: slope form of normal is y = mx - 2am - am^3
For the given parabola a = 2 and m = 1
therefore y = x - 4 - 2 
i.e; x - y - 6 = 0

Q1. The equation of the tangent to the conic x^2 - y^2 - 8x + 2y + 11 = 0 at (2, 1) is
    (A) 2x + 1 = 0
    (B) x + 2 = 0
    (C) x – 2 = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x + y + 1 = 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Differentiating the given equation w.r.t x, we get,
2x - 2y$dy\over dx$ - 8 + 2 $dy\over dx$ = 0
$dy\over dx$(1 - y) = x - 4
Therefore, $dy\over dx$ = $x-4\over 1-y $ 
Therefore, $dy\over dx$(2,1)_ is not defined
 The equation of the tangent at (x_1, y_1) is y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)
Therefore, the equation of the tangent is x - 2 = 0

Q2. In an ellipse the distance between its foci is 6 and its minor axis is 8; the eccentricity of the ellipse is
    (A) $\frac{2}{5}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{{\sqrt {52} }}$
    (C) $\frac{1}{2}$
    (D) $\frac{3}{5}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Here c = 3, b = 4, from relation a^2 = b^2 + c^2 we get a = 5.
e = $\frac{c}{a}$ = $\frac{3}{5}$

Q3. If the major axis of an ellipse is three times the minor axis, then its eccentricity is equal to
    (A) $\frac{1}{{\sqrt 3 }}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{{\sqrt 2 }}$
    (C) $\frac{1}{3}$
    (D) $\frac{2\sqrt 2 }{3}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\frac{2\sqrt 2 }{3}$
Length of the major axis = 2b
Length of the minor axis = 2a
According to question, the major axis of the ellipse is three times the minor axis.
i.e. 2b = 3(2a)
$\Rightarrow$ 2b = 6a
$\Rightarrow$ a = $\frac {2b} {6}$
$\Rightarrow$ a = $\frac {b} {3}$, b = 3a
Here, a > b, so the major and the minor axes of the ellipse are along the x - axis and they y - axis, respectively
Now, e $=\sqrt{1-\frac{a^{2}}{b^{2}}}$
$\Rightarrow e=\sqrt{1-\frac{\frac{b^{2}}{9}}{b^{2}}}$
$\Rightarrow e=\sqrt{1-\frac{1}{9}}$
$\Rightarrow e=\sqrt{\frac{8}{9}}$
$\Rightarrow e=\frac{2 \sqrt{2}}{3}$

Q4. At what point on the parabola y^2 = 4x the normal makes equal angles with the axes?
    (A) (9, 6)
    (B) (4, -4)
    (C) (4, 4)
    (D) (1, - 2)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: If the normal has slope - 1 then the tangent, that is perpendicular to the normal, will have slope = + 1 
Hence its equation is y = x + k
Hence the point of intersection between the parabola and the normal is 
(x + k)^2 = 4x
i.e; x^2 + 2kx - 4x + k^2 = 0
For discriminant value to be zero (b^2 - 4ac) = 0
(2k - 1)^2 - 4k^2 = 0
on solving this we get k = 1
Therefore the equaiton is x^2 - 2x + 1 = 0
This implies x = 1 and y = $\pm$2

Q5. The number of common tangents to the circles x^2 + y^2 - x = 0, x^2 + y^2 + x = 0 is
    (A) 1
    (B) 2
    (C) 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The equation of the circles can be written as (x - $1\over 2$)^2 + y^2 = $1\over 4$ and (x + $1\over 2$)^2 + y^2 = $1\over 4$ 
Hence their radii is $1\over 2$ and the centres is ($1\over 2$, 0) and ($-1\over 2$,0)
Distance between their centres is 1 and sum of the radii is also 1, hence the circles touch externally.
Therefore number of tangents that can be drawn is 3.

Q6. The locus of a point which moves so that its distance from a fixed point, called focus, bears a constant ratio, which is less than unity, to its distance from a fixed line, called the directrix is called
    (A) an ellipse   <-- CORRECT
    (B) a circle
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) a parabola
    Answer: A
    Explanation: For an ellipse e < 1

Q7. The axis of the parabola 9y^2 - 16x - 12y - 57 = 0 is
    (A) x + 3y = 3
    (B) y = 3
    (C) 3y = 2   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 2x = 3
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The equation can be written as y^2 - $12\over 9$y - $16\over 9$x - $57\over 9$ = 0
This can be written in the normal form as 
(y - $2\over 3$)^2 = $16x\over 9$ + $61\over 9$ 
y - $2\over 3$ = 0 
Therefore, y = $2\over 3$
or 3y = 2

Q8. Consider a circle with its centre lying on the focus of the parabola y^2 = 2 px such that it touches the directrix of the parabola, then a point of intersection of the circle and the parabola is
    (A) $\left(\frac{p}{2},-p\right)$
    (B) $\left(-\frac{p}{2}, p\right)$
    (C) $\left(-\frac{p}{2},-p\right)$
    (D) $\left(\frac{p}{2}, p\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Centre of circle = ($\frac{p}{2}$, 0), radius = p.
Hence the equation of the circle is (x - $\frac{p}{2}$)^2 + y^2 = p^2. Since y = p,
i.e; (x - $\frac{p}{2}$)^2 + p^2 = p^2
This imlpies x = $\frac{p}{2}$
Hence the point of intersection is ($\frac{p}{2}$, p)

Q9. The straight line 3x + 4y = 20 and the circle x^2 + y^2 = 16
    (A) intersect in two distinct points
    (B) intersect in three distinct points
    (C) touch each other   <-- CORRECT
    (D) neither touch nor intersect in two points
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Distance from the origin to the line is equal to the radius.
$\ 0+ 0 + 20\over \sqrt{3^2 + 4^2}$ = 4. The radius of the circle is 4.
Hence the line and circle touch each other.

Q10. The equation x^2 + 3y^2 - 9x + 2y + 1 = 0 represents
    (A) a circle
    (B) an ellipse   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a hyperbola
    (D) a parabola
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The given equation can be written of the form 
(x - $\frac{9}{2}$)^2 + 3(y + $\frac{1}{3}$)^2 - $81\over 4$ - $1\over 3$ + 1 = 0, i.e; (x - $\frac{9}{2}$)^2 + 3(y + $\frac{1}{3}$)^2 = 235
That is $(x-9/2)^2\over 235$ + 3$(y+2/3)^2\over 235$ = 1
This is an equation of an ellipse.

Q11. A bridge is in the shape of a semi-ellipse. It is 400 meters long and has a maximum height of 10 metres at the middle points. The height of the bridge at a point distant 80 meters from one end is
    (A) 2 metres
    (B) 8 metres   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\sqrt {91} $ metres
    (D) 4 metres
    Answer: B
    Explanation: a = 200, b = 10, 
Put x = 200 - 80 = 120.
Substituting in the equation of the ellipese $x^2\over 200^2$ + $y^2\over 10^2$= 1
y^2 = $\frac{256}{16}$
therefore y = 8

Q12. The radius of the circle 3x (x – 2) + 3y(y + 1) = 4 is
    (A) 2
    (B) 3
    (C) $\sqrt{\frac{31}{12}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $\sqrt{\frac{15}{4}}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The general form of the given circle is x^2 + y^2 - 2x + y - $\frac{4}{3}$ = 0
Hence g = 1, f = $\frac{-1}{2}$ and c = $\frac{-4}{3}$
Radius = $\sqrt{g^2 + f^2 -c}$ 
Substituting the values we get,
Radius = $\sqrt{1 +\frac{1}{4}+\frac{4}{3}}$ = $\sqrt\frac{31}{12}$

Q13. If the angle between the lines joining the foci of an ellipse to an extremity of a minor axis is 90^o, then the eccentricity of the ellipse is
    (A) $\frac{1}{ 4}$
    (B) $\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{1}{8}$
    (D) $\frac{1}{{\sqrt 3 }}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The triangle formed is a right-angled triangle.
Let us consider STS' as the triangle right angled at T.
The coordinates of S is (ae, 0), S' (-ae, 0) and T(0, b)
By applying Pythagoras theorem
ST^2 + S'T^2 = SS'^2
i.e; (a^2e^2 + b^2) + (a^2e^2 + b^2) = 2 a^2e^2
on simplifying we get
e^2 = $\frac{1}{2}$ or e = $\frac{1}{\sqrt2}$

Q14. The vertex of the parabola y^2 = 4a(x + a) is
    (A) (0, a)
    (B) (0, 0)
    (C) (a, 0)
    (D) (- a, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let the equation y = Y and (x + a) = X
Then the equation of the parabola can be written as
Y^2 = 4aX, whose vertex is (0, 0)
Therefore, x + a = 0 and y = 0., implies x = -a and y = 0
Hence, the vertex of the given parabola is (-a, 0).

Q15. If 3x + y = 0 is a tangent to the circle which has its center at the point (2, - 1), then the equation of the other tangent to the circle from the origin is
    (A) 3x - y = 0
    (B) x - 3y = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) x + 2y = 0
    (D) x + 3y = 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The other tangent will be perpendicular to the given tangent 3x + y = 0
Therefore its equation is x - 3y + k = 0
Since it passes through the origin, k = 0
Hence the equation of the other tangent is x - 3y = 0

Q1. The distance of the point (3, 4, 5) from X-axis is
    (A) 5
    (B) $\sqrt {34} $
    (C) 3
    (D) $\sqrt {41} $   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The distance of the point (3, 4, 5) from X-axis is: let L be the foot of the perpendicular from the point (3, 4, 5) to X-axis, then coordinate of L will be (3, 0, 0) because on X-axis y and z coordinate are zero then the distance of the point (3, 4, 5) from X-axis i.e. from L (3, 0, 0) is given by $\sqrt {{{(3 - 3)}^2} + {{(4 - 0)}^2} + {{(5 - 0)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt {41} $

Q2. The direction cosines of X -axis are
    (A) $<$ 0 , 1 , 1 $>$
    (B) $<$ 0 , 1 , 0 $>$
    (C) $<$ 0 , 0 , 1 $>$
    (D) $<$ 1 , 0 , 0 $>$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: As we know that if a lines makes angles a , b and c with X-axis , Y-axis and Z-axis respectively then direction cosines are given by < cos a , cos b ,cos c >
In our case line is X-axis itself which we know makes angle of 0$^ \circ $ , 90$^ \circ $ , 90$^ \circ $ with X-axis , Y-axis and Z-axis respectively then direction cosine will be
<cos 0$^ \circ $ , cos 90$^ \circ $, cos 90$^ \circ $>
= < 1, 0, 0 >

Q3. The medians of a triangle are concurrent at the point called
    (A) orthocentre
    (B) incentre
    (C) centroid   <-- CORRECT
    (D) circumcentre
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The centroid is the point of concurrency of the medians of the triangle. It is a point of the centre of gravity of the triangle.

Q4. The direction cosines of any normal to the XY plane are
    (A) $<$ 0 , 1 , 0 $>$
    (B) $<$ 1 , 0 , 0 $>$
    (C) $<$ 0 , 0 , 1 $>$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) $<$ 1 , 1 , 0 $>$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Concept used - Parellel lines have same direction cosines
Explanation We know Z axis is perpendicular to XY plane and direction cosines of Z axis are <0,0,1>
and as any normal to XY plane will be parallel to Z axis and parellel lines have same direction cosines so answer is <0,0,1>

Q5. How many lines through the origin make equal angles with the coordinate axes ?
    (A) 1
    (B) 4
    (C) 2
    (D) 8   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $since \ \alpha = \beta =\ \gamma$
$cos^2\alpha +cos^2\beta+cos^2\gamma=1\\ hence \ 3 cos^2\alpha=1\\ hence \ cos \alpha=\frac{1}{\sqrt3}\\ \ cos \beta=\frac{1}{\sqrt3}\\\ cos \gamma=\frac{1}{\sqrt3} dcs \ of \ lines \ will \ be\ \\(\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt3},\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt3},\pm \frac{1}{\sqrt3}) $
hence the lines will be 8

Q6. the numbers 3, 4 , 5 can be
    (A) direction numbers of a line in space   <-- CORRECT
    (B) direction cosines of a line in space
    (C) coordinates of a point in the plane x + y – z = 0
    (D) coordinates of a point on the line y = 4 , z = 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: the numbers 3, 4 , 5 can be direction ratio of any line these not satisfying any other option

Q7. If the directions cosines of a line are k,k,k, then
    (A) 0 $<$ k $<$ 1
    (B) k $>$ 0
    (C) k = 1
    (D) $k = \frac{1}{{\sqrt {3} }}$ or $k = - \frac{1}{{\sqrt 3 }}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: We know that if l, m, n are direction cosines of a lines then l^2 +m^2 +n^2= 1
so, k^2 + k^2 +k^2 = 1
3 k^2 = 1
k^2 = $\frac{1}{3}$
taking squareroot on both sides , we have $k = \frac{1}{{\sqrt {3} }}$ or $k = - \frac{1}{{\sqrt 3 }}$

Q8. The lines, which do not lie in the same plane, are called?
    (A) intersecting
    (B) coincident
    (C) skew lines   <-- CORRECT
    (D) parallel
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Lines which lie in the same plane can be parallel, coincident or intersecting.
Skew lines are those lines which lie in different planes and never meet to each other.

Q9. The radius of the sphere through the points (4, 3, 0), (0, 4, 3), (0, 5, 0) and (4, 0, 3) is
    (A) 5   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $\frac{5}{7}$
    (C) 7
    (D) $\frac{7}{5}$
    Answer: A
    Explanation: We know that general equation of sphere is x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 2gx + 2fy + 2hz + c = 0
Since sphere passing through the points (4, 3, 0), (0, 4, 3), (0, 5, 0) and (4, 0, 3) so putting these values one by one in given equation, we get
16 + 9 + 8g + 6f + c = 0 $\Rightarrow$ 8g + 6f + c = -25 ......(i)
16 + 9 + 8f + 6h + c = 0 $\Rightarrow$ 8f + 6h + c = -25 ......(ii)
25 + 10f + c = 0 ......(iii)
16 + 9 + 8g + 6h + c = 0 $\Rightarrow$ 8g + 6h + c = -25 ......(iv)
By (ii) - (iv) we have f = g
Using this in (i) we have 16f +c = -25 .....(v)
Now solving (iii) and (v) we get f = 0 
Using value of f we have g = 0, h = 0, c = -25
Now radius =$\sqrt {{{( - g)}^2} + ( - f) + {{( - h)}^2} - c} $ = $\sqrt {25} $ = 5

Q10. The points (4, 7, 8), (2, 3, 4), (-1, -2, 1) and (1, 2, 5) are the vertices of a
    (A) rectangle
    (B) parallelogram   <-- CORRECT
    (C) square
    (D) rhombus
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The vertices of a quadrilateral are A( 4, 7, 8), B(2, 3, 4) ,C (- 1, -2, 1) and D(1, 2, 5) 
AB =$\sqrt {{{(4 - 2)}^2} + {{(7 - 3)}^2} + {{(8 - 4)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt{4+16+16}$ = $\sqrt{36}$ = 6 
BC =$\sqrt {{{(2 + 1)}^2} + {{(3 + 2)}^2} + {{(4 - 1)}^2}}$ = $\sqrt{9+25+9}$ = $\sqrt{43}$ 
CD =$\sqrt {{{(1 + 1)}^2} + {{(2 + 2)}^2} + {{(5 - 1)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt{4+16+16}$ = $\sqrt{36}$ = 6
DA = $\sqrt {{{(4 - 1)}^2} + {{(7 - 2)}^2} + {{(8 - 5)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt{9+25+9}$ = $\sqrt{43}$ 
Here opposite sides of quadrilateral ABCD are equal, so it may be parallelogram or rectangle
Now , diagonal AC =$\sqrt {{{(4 + 1)}^2} + {{(7 +2)}^2} + {{(8 -1)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt{25+81+49}$ = $\sqrt{155}$ 
BD = $\sqrt {{{(2 - 1)}^2} + {{(3 - 2)}^2} + {{(4 - 5)}^2}}$ = $\sqrt{1+1+1}$ = $\sqrt{3}$ 
Here the length of diagonals AC and BD are different so ABCD is a parallelogram.

Q11. The equation xy = 0 in three dimensional space represents
    (A) a pair of straight lines
    (B) a pair of planes at right angles   <-- CORRECT
    (C) a plane
    (D) a pair of parallel lines
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since xy = 0 implies x = 0 or y = 0.i.e YZ plane or XZ plane. Hence it represents a pair of planes at right angles.

Q12. The graph of the equation x^2 + y^2 = 0 in the three dimensional space is
    (A) X - axis
    (B) XY – plane
    (C) Y - axis
    (D) Z - axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: x^2 + y^2 = 0 $\Rightarrow $ x = 0 and y = 0 represents a point (0, 0) in space in 2D. In 3D the collection of all these points forms Z-axis.

Q13. In three dimensional space, locus of the equation x^2 + z^2 = 0 is
    (A) empty set
    (B) a degenerate circle
    (C) y - axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a degenerate sphere
    Answer: C
    Explanation: x^2 + z^2 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ x = 0 and z = 0 it will represent a point in 2d and in 3d the collection of all these point will form Y axis.

Q14. The distance of the point (x, y, z) from the XY–plane is
    (A) y
    (B) |z|   <-- CORRECT
    (C) z
    (D) x
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let L be the foot of a perpendicular segment from point P (x, y, z) on the XY plane.
Now since L is the foot of perpendicular on XY plane so z coordinate will be zero so the point L will be (x, y, 0)
Then the distance between these two will be $\sqrt {{{(x - x)}^2} + {{(y - y)}^2} + {{(z - 0)}^2}} $ = $\sqrt {{z^2}} $ = |z|

Q15. The angle between the lines x = 1, y = 2 and y = - 1, z = 0 is
    (A) 0^o
    (B) 90^o   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 30^o
    (D) 60^o
    Answer: B
    Explanation: x = 1, y = 2 represents XY plane and y = - 1, z = 0 represents YZ plane. Since XY perpendicular to YZ. Hence angle is 90 degrees.

Q1. The lines having drs as a_1a_2 + b_1b_2 + c_1c_2 = 0 are
    (A) perpendicular   <-- CORRECT
    (B) coincident
    (C) parallel
    (D) skew
    Answer: A
    Explanation: cos $\theta$ = $\frac{a_{1} a_{2}+b_{1} b_{2}+c_{1} c_{2}}{\sqrt{a_{1}^{2}+b_{1}^{2}+c_{1}^{2}} \sqrt{a_{2}^{2}+b_{2}^{2}+c_{2}^{2}}}$ 
but a_1a_2 + b_1b_2 + c_1c_2 = 0
Hence cos $\theta$ = 0
$\theta$ = 90^o
Hence lines are perpendicular.

Q2. The line x = 1, y = 2 is
    (A) parallel to Y – axis
    (B) parallel to X – axis
    (C) lies in a plane parallel to XY – plane
    (D) parallel to Z – axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since z coordinate is zero it is parallel to Z axis.

Q3. The equation (x – 1)(x – 2) = 0 represents, in three dimensional space, a
    (A) sphere
    (B) pair of parallel planes   <-- CORRECT
    (C) pair of straight lines
    (D) an empty set
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation (x - 1) (x - 2) = 0 represents, in three dimensional space, a pair of parallel planes.
(x - 1) (x - 2) = 0 $\Rightarrow$ (x - 1) = 0, (x - 2) = 0
x = 1 and x = 2 
According to the equation ax + by + cz = d and by the formula $\frac{{a_1}}{{a_2}} = \frac{{b_1}}{{b_2}} = \frac{{c_1}}{{c_2}}$ we have both the planes represent pair of parallel planes.

Q4. A point (x, y, z) moves parallel to X- axis. Which of the three variables x, y, z remain fixed?
    (A) x
    (B) z and x
    (C) y and z   <-- CORRECT
    (D) x and y
    Answer: C
    Explanation: A point (x, y, z) moves parallel to X-axis then value of x will vary and remaining will be fixed.

Q5. A point (x, y, z) moves parallel to XY - plane. Which of the three variables x, y, z remain fixed?
    (A) x
    (B) x and y
    (C) y
    (D) z   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: A point (x, y, z) moves parallel to XY - plane then x and y-coordinate will vary and z will fixed.

Q6. The plane x = 0 divides the join of (- 2, 3, 4) and (1, -2, 3) in the ratio
    (A) 1: 2
    (B) 3 : 2
    (C) 4 : 3
    (D) 2 : 1   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Given:
Place: x = 0 and two points (−2, 3, 4) and (1, −2, 3)
Let say a point (x, y, z) in x = 0 place
So, x = $\frac{m+n(-2)}{m+n}=\frac{m-2 n}{m+n}$ 
0 = $\frac{m-2 n}{m+n}$ $\Rightarrow$ m = 2n
So, $\frac{m}{n}=\frac{2}{1} \Rightarrow$ 2 : 1

Q7. The direction cosines of the line joining (1, - 1, 1) and (-1, 1, 1) are
    (A) < 1, - 1, 1 >
    (B) < 2, - 2, 0 >
    (C) $<\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}},-\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}, 0>$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) < 1, -1, 0 >
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The direction ratio of the line joining (x_1, y_1, z_1) and (x_2, y_2, z_2) = < x_1 - x_2, y_1 - y_2, z_1 - z_2 >
The direction ratio of the line joining (1, -1, 1) and (-1, 1, 1) = < 1 + 1, -1 - 1, 1 - 1 > = < 2, -2, 0 >
The direction cosines of the line = <$\frac{{ 2}}{{\sqrt {{{( - 2)}^2} + {{(2)}^2} + {{(0)}^2}} }},\frac{-2}{{\sqrt {{{( -2)}^2} + {{(2)}^2} + {{(0)}^2}} }},\frac{0}{{\sqrt {{{( - 2)}^2} + {{(2)}^2} + {{(0)}^2}} }}$ > = $ < \frac{{ 2}}{{\sqrt 8 }},\frac{-2}{{\sqrt 8 }},\frac{0}{{\sqrt 8 }} > $ = $ < \frac{{ 2}}{{2\sqrt 2 }},\frac{-2}{{2\sqrt 2 }},\frac{0}{{2\sqrt 2 }} > $=$ < \frac{{ 1}}{{\sqrt 2 }},\frac{-1}{{\sqrt 2 }},0 > $

Q8. The line $\frac{x-x_1}{0}=\frac{y-y_1}{1}=\frac{z-z_1}{2}$ is
    (A) at right angles to plane YOZ
    (B) is perpendicular to Y-axis
    (C) is parallel to Y-axis
    (D) at right angles to x –axis   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since the drs i.e. a = 0. Hence, the line is perpendicular to the x-axis.

Q9. The line x = x_1, y = y_1 is
    (A) parallel to z axis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) parallel to y axis
    (C) parallel to x axis
    (D) perpendicular to y axis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The line x = x_1, y = y_1 is parallel to Z-axis as here value of x and y is fixed. Here whatever be the value of z, x and y will be fixed So it represents a plane parallel to Z-axis.

Q10. Skew lines are
    (A) parallel lines
    (B) intersecting lines
    (C) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (D) coplanar lines
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Skew lines are those lines which lie in different planes and never meet.

Q11. The locus of the equation xy + yz = 0 is
    (A) a pair of straight lines
    (B) a pair of curvy lines
    (C) a pair of perpendicular planes   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a pair of parallel planes
    Answer: C
    Explanation: xy represents the plane through origin and perpendicular to z-axis. Similarly yz represents the plane through origin and perpendicular to x-axis. Hence it represents pair of perpendicular lines.

Q12. The number of spheres of a given radius r and touching the coordinate axes(3D) is
    (A) 4
    (B) 8   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 10
    (D) 6
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Each octant will have one sphere of radius r touching axes. So there are 8 such spheres.

Q13. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i}$ represents
    (A) the Z axis
    (B) the X axis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the Y axis
    (D) the YOZ plane
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i}$ represents X- axis
 $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i}$ 
$\vec r = \ x \widehat {i} +\ y \widehat {j}+\ z \widehat {k}$ = $\lambda \ \widehat {i} +\ 0 \widehat {j}+\ 0 \widehat {k}$ 
x = $\lambda$, y = 0, z = 0 this is a general point on X-axis. So given equation represent X axis.

Q14. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i} + \mu \widehat {j} $ represents
    (A) the plane z = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (B) the Z axis
    (C) the Y axis
    (D) the X aixs
    Answer: A
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i} + \mu \widehat {j} $ represents the plane z = 0 as the equation can be written as $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i} + \mu \widehat {j} +\ 0 \widehat {k} $ 
In this z-coordinate is zero. So, this represents XY plane i.e. the plane Z = 0

Q15. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {k} $ represents
    (A) the Y axis
    (B) the X axis
    (C) the Z axis   <-- CORRECT
    (D) origin
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {k} $ can be represented in the form $\vec r = \ 0 \widehat {i} +\ 0\widehat {j}+\lambda \widehat {k}$. Here x, y coordinate are 0 and z is any real number. It represents a general point on Z-axis 
So, it represent Z-axis.

Q1. The distance between the planes $\vec r.\hat n = {p_{1}}and$ $\vec r.( - \hat n) = {p_{2}}is$
    (A) $\left| {{p_1} - {p_2}} \right|$
    (B) ${p_2} - {p_1}$
    (C) ${p_2}*{p_1}$
    (D) ${p_1} + {p_2}$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: P_1 is distance of first plane from origion in the direction of normal vector and P_2 is distance of second plane from origion opposite to normal vector. So distance between planes is $P_1-\left(-P_2\right)\;=\;P_1+P_2$

Q2. The point equidistant from the points (0, 0, 0), (1, 0, 0), (0, 2, 0) and (0, 0, 3) is
    (A) (1, 2, 3)
    (B) ($\frac{1}{2}$, 1, $\frac{3}{2}$)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) ($\frac{-1}{2}$, -1, $\frac{-3}{2}$)
    (D) (-1, -2, 3)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let the point equidistant from the points (0, 0, 0), (1, 0, 0), (0, 2, 0) and (0, 0, 3) is (x, y, z)
Then according to the given condition and distance formula between two points we have 
$\sqrt{(x-0)^{2}+(y-0)^{2}+(z-0)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{(x-1)^{2}+(y-0)^{2}+(z-0)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{(x-0)^{2}+(y-2)^{2}+(z-0)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{(x-0)^{2}+(y-0)^{2}+(z-3)^{2}}$ 
$\sqrt {{x^2} + {y^2} + {z^2}} $ = $\sqrt{(x-1)^{2}+y^{2}+z^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{x^{2}+(y-2)^{2}+z^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{x^{2}+y^{2}+(z-3)^{2}}$ 
Taking ist two expressions and solving them we get x^2 = (x - 1)^2 $\Rightarrow$ x^2 = x^2 - 2x + 1 $\Rightarrow$ -2x + 1 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ x = $\frac{1}{2}$ 
Similarly by taking i^st and 3^rd we get y = 1 and by taking ist and 4th we get z = $\frac{3}{2}$ 
So the required point is ($\frac{1}{2}$, 1, $\frac{3}{2}$)

Q3. The plane x + y = 0 is
    (A) passes through z – axis   <-- CORRECT
    (B) parallel to z – axis
    (C) intersecting to z – axis
    (D) perpendicular to z – axis
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Co-ordinates of any point on z-axis are (0, 0, z)
$\therefore$ The plane x + y = 0 will pass through z-axis if (0, 0, z) satisfies x + y = 0 ....(i)
Now L.H.S of (i) = x + y
For (0, 0, z), L.H.S of (i) = 0 + 0 = 0 = R.H.S of (i)
Hence the result.

Q4. The points ( 1 , 1 , 0 ) , ( 0 , 1 , 1 ) , ( 1 , 0 , 1 ) , and ( 2/3 , 2/3 , 2/3 ) are
    (A) the vertices of a parallelogram
    (B) coplanar   <-- CORRECT
    (C) non coplanar
    (D) the angle of a parallelogram
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\vec{a}=1 \hat{i}+1 \hat{j}+0 \hat{k}), \vec{b}=(0 \hat{i}+1 \hat{j}+1 \hat{k}), \vec{c}=((\hat{i}+0 \hat{j}+1 \hat{k}), \vec{d}=(2 / 3 \hat{i}+2 / 3 \hat{j}+2 / 3 \hat{k})$
$\overrightarrow{A B}=-\overrightarrow{1 i}+0 \hat{j}+1 \hat{k}, \overrightarrow{A C}=-0 \hat{i}+-1 \hat{j}+1 \hat{k}, \overrightarrow{A D}=-1 / 3 \hat{i}+-1 / 3 \hat{j}+2 / 3 \hat{k}$
$\text { Consider }\left|\begin{array}{ccc}{-1} & {0} & {1} \\ {0} & {-1} & {1} \\ {-1 / 3} & {-1 / 3} & {2 / 3}\end{array}\right|=-1(-1 / 3)+1(-1 / 3)$
=0 
Hence points are coplanar

Q5. The lines $\frac{x-1}{2}=\frac{y-2}{3}=\frac{z-3}{4}$ and $\frac{x-1}{3}=\frac{y-2}{4}=\frac{z-3}{5}$ are
    (A) perpendicular
    (B) parallel
    (C) intersecting   <-- CORRECT
    (D) skew
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Here (a_1, b_1, c_1) = (2, 3, 4)
and, (a_2, b_2, c_2) = (3, 4, 5)
Consider $\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {x_2 - x_1}&{y_2 - y_1}&{z_2 - z_1} \\ {a_1}&{b_1}&{c_1} \\ {a_2}&{b_2}&{c_2} \end{array}} \right|$ 
We get
$\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} 0&0&0 \\ 2&3&4 \\ 3&4&5 \end{array}} \right|$ = 0
Since the shortest distance is zero hence the lines are intersecting.

Q6. The lines l_1 and l_2 intersect. The shortest distance between them is
    (A) positive
    (B) zero   <-- CORRECT
    (C) negative
    (D) infinity
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since the lines intersect. Hence they have a common point in them. Hence the distance will be zero.

Q7. Volume of a tetrahedron is kX area of one face X length of the perpendicular from the opposite vertex upon it, where k is
    (A) it is $\frac{1}{4}$
    (B) it is $\frac{1}{6}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) it is $\frac{1}{2}$
    (D) it is $\frac{1}{3}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Volume of tetrahedron = $\frac{1}{6}[\bar a \bar b \bar c]$ where a, b, c are co-terminus edges of the tetrahedron. a $\times$ b is area of one face and c is the perpendicular from the opposite vertex.

Q8. A, B, C and D are four points in spaces such that AB = BC = CD = DA. Then ABCD is a
    (A) skew quadrilateral
    (B) rectangle
    (C) rhombus
    (D) nothing can be said   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: It can be square or rhombus(all sides are equal). Angle property must be mentioned.

Q9. The foot of the perpendicular from ($\alpha {\rm{ }},\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\gamma $) on Y-axis is
    (A) (0, 0, 0)
    (B) (0, $\gamma$, 0)
    (C) (0, $\alpha$, 0)
    (D) (0, $\beta $, 0)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let P($\alpha {\rm{ }},\beta {\rm{ }},{\rm{ }}\gamma $) be the point and Q (0,b,0) be any point on Y-axis.
Direction of PQ = ($\alpha,\beta-b,\gamma)$ 
Direction of y-axis (0, b, 0)
Since PQ perpendicular to y-axis. Hence a_1a_2 + b_1b_2 + c_1c_2 = 0
0 + b($\beta$ - b) + 0 = 0
b($\beta$ - b) = 0
$\beta$ = b
Hence the foot of perpendicular will be $(0,\beta,0)$

Q10. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \hat j$ represents
    (A) the Z axis
    (B) the Y axis   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the plane y = 0
    (D) the X axis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \hat j$ $\Rightarrow$$ \ x \hat i +\ y \hat j+\ z \hat k$ = $\lambda \hat j$ $\Rightarrow$ x = 0, y = $\lambda$, z = 0 which represent Y-axis.

Q11. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i} + \mu \widehat {k} $ represents
    (A) the Y axis
    (B) the X axis
    (C) the Z axis
    (D) the plane y = 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {i} + \mu \widehat {k} $ $\Rightarrow$$\ x \widehat {i} +\ y \widehat {i}+ \ z \widehat {k} $ =$ \lambda \widehat {i} +\ 0 \widehat {j} + \mu \widehat {k} $ $\Rightarrow$ x = $\lambda$, y = 0, z = $\mu$ which represent generally XY plane i.e the plane y = 0.

Q12. The centre of the sphere, which passes through (a, 0, 0), (0, b, 0) (0, 0, c ) and (0, 0, 0) is where abc $ \ne $ 0
    (A) ($\frac{a}{2}$, $\frac{b}{2}$, $\frac{c}{2}$)   <-- CORRECT
    (B) (0, 0, $\frac{c}{2}$)
    (C) ($\frac{a}{2}$, 0, 0)
    (D) (0, $\frac{b}{2}$, 0)
    Answer: A
    Explanation: General equation of the sphere is x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 2gx + 2fy + 2hz + d = 0......(i)
Since (i) passes through the point (0, 0, 0) using this in (i) we get d = 0
Similarly (i) passes through (a, 0, 0), (0, b, 0) (0, 0, c) using these values in (i)
a^2 + 2ag = 0 $\Rightarrow$ a(a + 2g) = 0
b^2 + 2bf = 0 $\Rightarrow$ b(b + 2f) = 0
c^2 + 2ch = 0 $\Rightarrow$ c(c + 2h) = 0
But as abc $\ne $ 0 So, a $\ne $ 0, b $\ne $ 0, c $\ne $ 0
So from above equations we have a = - 2g, b = - 2f, c = -2h centre is (-f, -g, -h) = ($\frac{a}{2}$, $\frac{b}{2}$, $\frac{c}{2}$)

Q13. The equations of y axis are
    (A) x = 0, y = 0
    (B) x = 0, z = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) y = 0, z = 0
    (D) x = 0, y = 0, z = 0
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since on Y-axis x and z coordinate are 0.
So, Equations of Y-axis are x = 0 and z = 0

Q14. The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {j} + \mu \widehat {k} $ represents
    (A) the Y axis
    (B) the plane x = 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) the Z axis
    (D) the X axis
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The equation $\vec r = \lambda \widehat {j} + \mu \widehat {k} $ $\Rightarrow$$ \ x \widehat {i} +\ y\widehat {j}+ \ z \widehat {k} =\ 0 \widehat {i}+ \lambda \widehat {j} + \mu \widehat {k} $ $\Rightarrow$ x = 0, y = $\lambda$, z = $\mu$ which represent generally YZ plane i.e. X = 0 plane.

Q15. Distance between two parallel planes 2x+y+2z=8 and 4x+2y+4z+5=0 is
    (A) $\frac {9}{2}$
    (B) $\frac {7}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac{5}{2}$
    (D) $\frac {3}{2}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Given planes are 
2x+2y+2z-8=0
and 2x+y+2z+$\frac{5}{2}$=0
Distance between planes =$\frac {|c_1-c_2|}{\sqrt {a^2+b^2+c^2}}\\ $.
$=|\frac {-8-\frac{5}{2}}{\sqrt {2^2+1^2+2^2}}|\\ =\frac{ \frac{21}{2}}{3}=\frac {7}{2}$

3D Geometry Test 04  (id 660) [PAID]

Questions: 15 | Answers: YES

Q1. There is one and only one sphere through
    (A) 3 points not lie in the same line
    (B) 4 points not in the same plane   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 4 points not lie in the same straight line
    (D) 4 points lie in the same straight line
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Yes, it is true because if we assume 2 spheres or more than that they will coincide.

Q2. Three planes x + y = 0, y + z = 0 and x + z = 0
    (A) meet in a line
    (B) meet taken two at a time in parallel lines
    (C) meet taken three at a time in parallel lines
    (D) meet in a unique point   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: x + y = 0 .....(1)
y + z = 0 .....(2)
x + z = 0 ......(3)
Subtracting 1 and 2 we get x - z = 0 .......(4)
Adding 3 and 4 we get x = 0, y = 0 and z = 0

Q3. The centre of the sphere through the points ( 0 , 3 , 4 ) , ( 0 , 5 , 0 ) , ( 4 , 0 , 3 ) and ( - 3 , 4 , 0 ) is
    (A) ( 0 , 2 , 3 )
    (B) ( 0 , 2 , -3 )
    (C) (- 4 , 3 , 0 )
    (D) ( 0 , 0 , 0 )   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let the equation of the required sphere be 
$\mathrm{x}^{2}+\mathrm{y}^{2}+\mathrm{z}^{2}+2 \mathrm{ux}+2 \mathrm{vy}+2 \mathrm{wz}+\mathrm{d}=0$ ...........(1)
since it passes through (0,3,4),(0,5,0),(4,0,3) and (-3,4,0) therefore
$0^{2}+3^{2}+4^{2}+2 u(0)+2 v(3)+2 w(4)+d=0$
$4^{2}+0^{2}+3^{2}+2 u(4)+2 v(0)+2 w(3)+d=0$
$(-3)^{2}+4^{2}+0^{2}+2 u(-3)+2 v(4)+2 w(0)+d=0$
$\Rightarrow 6 v+8 w+25+d=0 \ldots \ldots \ldots .(2)$
$\Rightarrow 8 u+6 w+25+d=0 \ldots \ldots \ldots(3)$
$\Rightarrow-6 u+8 v+25+d=0 \ldots \ldots \ldots .(4)$
$\Rightarrow 10 \mathrm{v}+25+\mathrm{d}=0 \ldots \ldots \ldots \text { (5) }$
Subtracting (5) from (2),(3),(4) respectively, we get 
$\Rightarrow-4 \mathrm{v}+8 \mathrm{w}=0 \ldots \ldots .(6)$
$\Rightarrow 8 u+6 w-10 v=0............(7)$
$\Rightarrow-6 u-2 v=0 \ldots \ldots .(8)$
Solving these, we get, u=v=w=0
$\therefore$ Centre of sphere (-u,-v,-w)=(0,0,0)

Q4. The points A ( 0 , 0 , 0 ) , B ( 1 , $\sqrt 3 $ , 0 ) , C ( 2 , 0 , 0 ) and D ( 1 , 0 , $\sqrt 3 $) are the vertices of
    (A) rhombus
    (B) square
    (C) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (D) parallelogram
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Direction ratios of AB are $(1-0, \sqrt{3}-0,0-0) \text { i.e }(1, \sqrt{3}, 0)$
Direction ratios of BC are$(1-0, \sqrt{3}-0,0-0) \text { i.e }(1,-\sqrt{3}, 0)$
Direction ratios of CD are $(-1-0,0-0, \sqrt{3}-0) \text { i.e }(-1,0, \sqrt{3})$
Direction ratios of CD are $(-1-0,0-0,-\sqrt{3}-0) \text { i.e }(-1,0, \sqrt{3})$
If ABCD is a parallelogram, then
$\mathrm{AB} \| \mathrm{CD} \text { and } \mathrm{AD} \| \mathrm{BC}$
Now,$\frac{1}{-1} \neq \frac{\sqrt{3}}{0} \neq \frac{0}{\sqrt{3}}$ $\left[\because\frac{{\mathbf a}_1}{{\mathbf a}_2}\neq\frac{\mathbf b1}{{\mathbf b}_2}\neq\frac{{\mathbf c}_1}{{\mathbf c}_2}\right]$
$\therefore$ AB is not parallel to CD
Similarly $\frac{-1}{1} \neq \frac{0}{\sqrt{-3}} \neq \frac{-\sqrt{3}}{0}$
$\Rightarrow$ AD and BC are not parallel 
$\therefore$ ABCD is not a parallelogram and hence it is not a square or rhombus

Q5. The points A (0, 2, 0), B ($\sqrt 3 $, 1, 0), and $\mathrm{C}\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}, 1, \frac{2 \sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$ are the vertices of
    (A) an equilateral triangle   <-- CORRECT
    (B) an isosceles triangle
    (C) Right angle triangle
    (D) a scalene triangle
    Answer: A
    Explanation: To check which type of triangle these points form we need to check the distance between the two points
AB=$\sqrt{(\sqrt 3)^2+1+0}$ = 2
BC = $\sqrt{\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}-\sqrt{3}\right)^2+\left(\frac{2 \sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{3}}\right)^2}$ = 2,
Similarly AC = 2 by distance formula between two points.
Since all sides are same so the triangle is equilateral.

Q6. The locus of a first degree equation in x, y, z is a
    (A) sphere
    (B) plane   <-- CORRECT
    (C) Circle
    (D) straight line
    Answer: B
    Explanation: First-degree equation in x, y, z can be written in the form Ax + By + Cz + d = 0. Which represents a plane Where A, B and C are the direction ratios of normal to the plane.

Q7. Area of $\Delta ABC$ whose vertices A (-1, 2, 3), B(1, 1, 1) and C (2, - 1, 3) is
    (A) 4.5   <-- CORRECT
    (B) 9
    (C) 6
    (D) 0
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Formula is $\frac{1}{2}|\vec AB \times\vec AC| $ where $\vec AB$ has coordinates = P.V. of B - P.V of A = 2, -1, -2 and $\vec AC$ has coordinates = 3, -3, 0 
Area of triangle ABC = $\frac{1}{2}\left|\begin{array}{ccc} i & j & k \\ 2 & -1 & 2 \\ 3 & -3 & 0 \end{array}\right|$ = $\frac{1}{2}|6 i+6 j+3 k|$
= $\frac{1}{2} \times 9$ 
= 4.5

Q8. Perpendicular distance of the point (3, 4, 5) from the y-axis is,
    (A) 5
    (B) $\sqrt{41}$
    (C) $\sqrt{34}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 4
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Distance of $(\alpha, \beta, \gamma)$ from y-axis is given by d = $\sqrt{\alpha^{2}+\gamma^{2}}$ 
$\therefore$$$ Distance (d) of (3, 4, 5) from y-axis is 
d = $\sqrt{3^{2}+5^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{9+25}$ = $\sqrt{34}$

Q9. G is the centroid of triangle ABC . If P.V. of the points G , A , B , C are respectively , $3\hat i + 7\hat j + \hat k,2\hat i + \hat j + \hat k,x\hat i + 3\hat j + \hat k,and4\hat i + y\hat j + \hat k,then\left( {x,y} \right) = $
    (A) ( 3 , 3)
    (B) ( 17 , 3 )
    (C) ( 7 , 17 )
    (D) ( 3 , 17 )   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\vec{g}=\frac{\vec{a}+ \vec{b}+ \vec{c}}{3}$ centroid formula
$3(3 \hat{i}+7 \hat{j}+\hat{k})$=$2 \hat{i}+\hat{j}+\hat{k}+x \hat{i}+3 \hat{j}+\hat{k}+4 \hat{i}+y \hat{j}+\hat{k}$
$9 \hat{i}+21 \hat{j}+3 \hat{k}$=$(6+x) \hat{i}+(4+y) \hat{j}+3 \hat{k}$
9=6+x and 21=4+y
x=3 and y=17

Q10. If the four points (3, -2, -1), (2, 3, -4), (-1, 1, 2) and (4, 5, $\lambda $) are coplanar then $\lambda $ is equal to
    (A) $\frac{-17}{146}$
    (B) $\frac{-146}{17}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 0
    (D) $\frac{-13}{146}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since A(3, -2, -1), B(2, 3, -4), C(-1, 1, 2) and D(4, 5, $\lambda $) are coplanar
$\overrightarrow {AB} = - 1\hat i + 5\hat j - 3\hat k$ 
$\overrightarrow {AC} = - 4\hat i + 3\hat j + 3\hat k$ 
$\overrightarrow {AD} = 1\hat i + 7\hat j + (\lambda + 1)\hat k$ 
Hence $[\overrightarrow {AB} \;\overrightarrow {AC} \;\overrightarrow {AD} ] = 0\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} { - 1}&5&{ - 3} \\ { - 4}&3&3 \\ 1&7&{\lambda + 1} \end{array}} \right| $ = 0
-1(3$\lambda$ + 3 - 21) - 5(-4$\lambda$ - 4 - 4) - 3(-28 - 3) = 0
$\lambda$ = $\frac{-146}{17}$

Q11. The number of spheres of a given radius which touch the coordinate planes is
    (A) 1
    (B) 8   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 2
    (D) 4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: There are 8 quadrants in 3D, so for a given radius, there will be 8 possible spheres touching all the 3 coordinate planes.

Q12. The plane XOZ divides the join of (1, -1, 5) and (2, 3, 4) in the ratio k : 1, then the value of k is
    (A) -3
    (B) $\frac{1}{3}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 3
    (D) $\frac{-1}{3}$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Since XOZ plane is given y coordinate must be zero 
$\frac{k \times 3 + 1 \times (-1)}{k + 1}$=0
3k -1 = 0
k = $\frac{1}{3}$

Q13. A line AB in three-dimensional space makes angles 45° and 120° with the positive X-axis and the positive Y-axis, respectively. lf AB makes an acute angle $\theta$ with the positive X-axis, then $\theta$ is equal to
    (A) 45°
    (B) 75^o
    (C) 60°   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 90°
    Answer: C
    Explanation: We know that,
cos^2 45^o + cos^2 120^o + cos^2 $\theta$ = 0
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{2}+\frac{1}{4}+\cos ^{2} \theta$ = 1
$\Rightarrow$ cos^2 $\theta$ = $\frac{1}{4}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ cos $\theta$ = $\pm \frac{1}{2}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\theta$ = 60^o or 120^o 
Since $\theta$ is acute, therefore $\theta$ = 60^o

Q14. The coordinates of the foot of the perpendicular from the point A (1, 1, 1), on the line joining the points B (1, 4, 6) and C (5, 4, 4) are
    (A) (-4, 5, 3)
    (B) (4, 5, 3)
    (C) (-3, 0, 4)
    (D) (3, 4, 5)   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Equation of line BC
$\frac{{x - 1}}{4} = \frac{{y - 4}}{0} = \frac{{z - 6}}{{ - 2}} = \lambda $ 
Hence x = 4$\lambda$ + 1, y = 4 and z = -2$\lambda$ + 6
Let M (x, y, z) be any point on line BC
Since AM Perpendicular to BC
Direction of AM = (4$\lambda$ + 1 - 1, 0, -2$\lambda$ + 6 - 1)4(4$\lambda$) + 0 - 2(-2$\lambda$ + 5) = 0
$20\lambda $ = 10
$\lambda = \frac{1}{2}$ 
Hence M (x, y, z) = ($\frac{4 \times 1}{2+1}$ ,4, $\frac{-2 \times 1}{2+6}$)
M = (3,4,5)

Q15. The points (1, 2, 3), (-1, -1, -1) and (3, 5, 7) are the vertices of
    (A) an equilateral triangle
    (B) an isosceles triangle
    (C) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    (D) a right triangle
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let A = (1, 2, 3), B = (-1, -1, -1) and C = (3, 5, 7)
By distance formula between two points (x_1, y_1, z_1) and (x_2, y_2, z_2) = $\sqrt {{{(x_1 - x_2)}^2} + {{(y_1 - y_2)}^2} + {{(z_1 - z_2)}^2}} $ 
We get AB = $\sqrt {29} $ , BC = $\sqrt {116} $ = 2$\sqrt {29} $ 
AC =$\sqrt {29} $ 
As we know the triangle is possible only if the sum of any two sides is greater than 3rd but in our case, this condition is not holding so the triangle is not possible, these are collinear points.

Q1. A line making angles ${45^0}and{60^0}$ with the positive directions of the axis of x and y makes with the positive direction of Z axis , an angle of
    (A) ${60^0}$
    (B) ${45^0}$
    (C) ${60^0}or120{^0}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ${120^0}$
    Answer: C
    Explanation: cos^2$\alpha$+ cos^2$\beta$ + cos^2$\gamma$ =1
$\alpha =45 , \beta =60$
put the values in above equation 
($ {1/ \sqrt{2}}$)^2 +( 1/2)^2+ cos^2$\gamma$ =1
cos$\gamma = \pm 1/2$

Q2. The coordinates of the point which divides the line segment joining the points ( 5 , 4, 2 ) and ( - 1 , - 2 , 4 ) in the ratio 2 : 3 externally is
    (A) none of these
    (B) ( 13/5 , 8/5 , 14/5 )
    (C) ( 17/5 , 16/5 , - 2/5 )
    (D) ( 17 , 16 , -2 )   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: ( 17 , 16 , -2 )

Q3. The angle between a line with direction ratios 2 : 2 : 1 and a line joining (3, 1, 4) to (7, 2, 12)
    (A) tan^-1 $( - \frac{3}{2})$
    (B) cos^-1 $(\frac{3}{2})$
    (C) tan^-1 $( - \frac{2}{ 3})$
    (D) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{2}{3}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The angle between a line with direction ratios 2 : 2 : 1 and a line joining (3, 1, 4) to (7, 2, 12)
Direction ratios of the line joining the points A(3, 1, 4), B(7, 2, 12) is <x2-x1 , y2-y1, z2-z1> = < 7-3 , 2-1 , 12-4> = <4 ,1 ,8>
Now as the angle between two lines having direction ratios <a1,b1,c1> and <a2,b2,c2> is given by
$\operatorname{Cos}^{-1} \frac{a 1 a 2+b 1 b 2+c 1 c 2}{\sqrt{a 1^2+b 1^2+c 1^2} \sqrt{a 2^2+b 2^2+c 2^2}}$
Using the vuales we have
$\cos ^{-1} \frac{2 \times 4+2 \times 1+1 \times 8}{\sqrt{2^2+2^2+1^2} \sqrt{4^2+1^2+8^2}}$
$=\cos ^{-1} \frac{18}{27}=\cos ^{-1} \frac{2}{3}$

Q4. Lines OA, OB are drawn from 0 with direction cosines proportional to <1, - 2, - 1> and <3, - 2, 3> respectively. The direction ratios of the normal to the plane AOB are
    (A) <- 4, - 3, 2>
    (B) <4, 3, 2>
    (C) <-4, 3, 2>
    (D) <4, 3, -2>   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let the direction ratios of normal to plane be a, b, c.
The line in the plane with drs 1, -2, -1 and 3, -2, 3 must be perpendicular to normal 
Then a_1a_2 + b_1b_2 + c_1c_2 = 0
Thus a - 2b - c = 0
3a - 2b + 3c = 0
Solving by cross multiplication a = -8k, b = -6k, c = 4k
Direction of normal will be 4, 3, -2.

Q5. The projections of a vector on the three coordinate axes are 6, -3 and 2, respectively. The direction cosines of the vector are
    (A) $-\frac {6}{7},-\frac{3}{7},\frac{2}{7}$
    (B) $\frac{6}{7},-\frac{3}{7},\frac{2}{7}$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 6, -3, 2
    (D) -6, 3, -2
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Projection of vector on coordinate axes are 
x_2 - x_1, y_2 - y_1, z_2 - z_1
$\Rightarrow$ x_2 - x_1 = 6, y_2 - y_1 = -3, z_2 - z_1 = 2
Now, $\sqrt{\left(x_{2}-x_{1}\right)^{2}+\left(y_{2}-y_{1}\right)^{2}+\left(z_{2}-z_{1}\right)^{2}}$ = $\sqrt{36+9+4}$ = 7
So, the direction cosines of the vector are $\frac{6}{7},-\frac{3}{7}, \frac{2}{7}$

Q6. The points A (5, - 1, 1), B (7, - 4, 7), C(1, - 6, 10) and D (- 1, - 3, 4) are the vertices of
    (A) Trapezium
    (B) rectangle
    (C) rhombus   <-- CORRECT
    (D) square
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Distance between AB = 7, BC = 7, CD = 7 and DA = 7
Whereas distance between AC and BD is not equal.

Q7. If the projections of $\overrightarrow {PQ} $ on OX, OY, OZ are respectively 1, 2, 3 and 4, then the magnitude of $\overrightarrow {PQ} $ is
    (A) 169
    (B) 13   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 144
    (D) 19
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let $\overrightarrow {PQ} = x\hat i + y\hat j + z\hat k$ 
Since $OX = \hat iOY = \hat jOZ = \hat k$ 
Projection of PQ on OX = $\frac{{\overrightarrow {PQ} .\overrightarrow {OX} }}{{|OX|}}$ 
12 = $\frac{x}{1}$ 
x = 12
Similarly
Projection of PQ on OY = $ \frac{{\overrightarrow {PQ} .\overrightarrow {OY} }}{{|OY|}}$ 
3 = $\frac{y}{1}$ 
y = 3
Similarly
Projection of PQ on OZ = $\frac{{\overrightarrow {PQ} .\overrightarrow {OZ} }}{{|OZ|}}$ 
4 = $\frac{z}{1}$ 
z = 4
Hence $\overrightarrow {PQ} = 12\hat i + 3\hat j + 4\hat k$ 
$\left| {PQ} \right| = \sqrt {{{12}^2} + {3^2} + {4^2}} = 13$

Q8. The centre of sphere passing through four points (0, 0, 0), (0, 2, 0), (1, 0, 0) and (0, 0, 4) is
    (A) ($\frac{1}{2}$, 1, -2)
    (B) ($\frac{1}{2}$, 1, 2)   <-- CORRECT
    (C) (1, $\frac{1}{2}$, 2)
    (D) ($\frac{-1}{2}$, 1, 2)
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Equation of sphere is given by x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 2ux + 2vy + 2wz + d = 0
Since sphere passing through four points (0, 0, 0), (0, 2, 0), (1, 0, 0) and (0, 0, 4)
Substituting in the given equation we get d =0
4 + 4v = 0
v = -1
1 + 2u = 0
u = $\frac{-1}{2}$
16 + 8w = 0
w = -2
Centre of sphere (-u, -v, -w) = ($\frac{1}{2}$, 1, 2)

Q9. The ratio in which the line joining (2, 4, 5) (3, 5, -4) is divided by the YZ – plane is
    (A) 4 : - 3
    (B) 2 : 3
    (C) - 2 : 3   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 3 : 2
    Answer: C
    Explanation: The ratio in which the line joining (2, 4, 5) (3, 5, - 4) is divided by the YZ – plane is the point in YZ plane will be P(0, y, z) let it divides the line joining points A(2, 4, 5) and B(3, 5, - 4) in the ratio k : 1 
Then X coordinate of point P will be given by $3k+2 \over k+1$ which is equal to zero. 
i.e. $3k+2 \over k+1$= 0 $\Rightarrow$ 3k + 2 = 0 $\Rightarrow$ k = $\frac{-2}{3}$ 
So, YZ plane divides in -2 : 3

Q10. The area of the triangle whose vertices are (1, 2, 3), (2, 5, -1), (-1, 1, 2) is ________ sq. units.
    (A) 150
    (B) 145
    (C) $\frac{\sqrt{155}}{2}$   <-- CORRECT
    (D) 165
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Let $\vec a = (1\hat i + 2\hat j + 3\hat k)$, $\vec{b}=(2 \hat{i}+5 \hat{j}-1 \hat{k})$, $\vec{c}=(-1 \hat{i}+1 \hat{j}+2 \hat{k})$ 
Area of triangle = $\frac{1}{2}[\vec a*\vec b + \vec b*\vec c + \vec c*\vec a]$ 
= $ \frac{1}{2}\left[ {\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {\hat i}&{\hat j}&{\hat k} \\ 1&2&3 \\ 2&5&{ - 1} \end{array}} \right|} \right] + \left[ {\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {\hat i}&{\hat j}&{\hat k} \\ 2&5&{ - 1} \\ { - 1}&1&2 \end{array}} \right|} \right] + \left[ {\left| {\begin{array}{*{20}{c}} {\hat i}&{\hat j}&{\hat k} \\ { - 1}&1&2 \\ 1&2&3 \end{array}} \right|} \right]$ 
= $ \frac{1}{2}[ - 17\hat i + 7\hat j + 1\hat k + 11\hat i - 3\hat j + 7\hat k - 1\hat i + 5\hat j - 3\hat k]$ 
= $ \frac{1}{2}[ - 7\hat i + 9\hat j + 5\hat k]$ 
Area = $ \frac{1}{2}\sqrt {49 + 81 + 25} $ 
Area = $\frac{\sqrt{155}}{2}$

Q11. The direction ratios of a normal to the plane through ( 1 , 0 , 0 ) , ( 0 , 1 , 0 ) , which makes an angle of $\frac \pi 4$ with the plane x + y = 3
    (A) $ < 1,1,\sqrt 2 >$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) $ < 1,\sqrt 2 ,1 > $
    (C) $< \sqrt 2 ,1,1 > $
    (D) <1, 1, 2>
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Equation of plane through (1, 0, 0), (0, 1, 0) be ax + by + cx + d = 0
Let $\overrightarrow n = (a,b,c)$ unit vector normal to the plane
$\sqrt {{a^2} + {b^2} + {c^2}} = 1$
Equation of plane gives a + d = 0 and b + d = 0
solving we get a - b = 0 ....(1).
plane makes angles $\frac \pi 4$ with x + y = 3
$\cos {45^o} = \frac{{a(1) + b(1) + c(1)}}{{1*\sqrt 2 }}$
a + b = 1 ...(2)
solving (1) and (2) we get
a = b = $\frac 12$
Hence $\sqrt {{a^2} + {b^2} + {c^2}} = 1$
$c = \frac {1}{\sqrt 2 }$
drs of normal $(\frac 12, \frac 12, \frac {1}{\sqrt 2 })$
drs of normal $(1,1,\sqrt 2 )$

Q12. A tetrahedron has vertices at O (0, 0, 0), A (1, 2, 1), B (2, 1, 3) and C (-1, 1, 2), then the angle between the faces OAB and ABC will be
    (A) 90^o
    (B) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{19}{35}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 30^o
    (D) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{17}{31}\right)$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: Let n_1 and n_2 be the normals to the plane OAB and ABC
$\overrightarrow n_1=\overrightarrow {OA}\times\overrightarrow {OB}=\left |\begin {array}{ccc} \hat i & \hat j & \hat k\\1 & 2 & 1\\ 2 & 1 & 3\end {array}\right |$ 
n_1 = (5, -1, -3)
$\overrightarrow n_2=\overrightarrow {AB}\times\overrightarrow {AC}=\left |\begin {array}{ccc} \hat i & \hat j & \hat k\\1 & -2 & 2\\- 2 & -1 & 1\end {array}\right |$ 
n_2 = (1, -5, -3)
$cos\theta=\large\frac{\overrightarrow n_1.\overrightarrow n_2}{|\overrightarrow n_1||\overrightarrow n_2|} $ 
= $\large\frac{5+5+9}{\sqrt {35}.\sqrt {35}}\\$ 
= $\frac{19}{35}$ 
$\theta =cos^{-1}(\frac{19}{35})$

Q13. The equation of any plane parallel to y – axis
    (A) x = d
    (B) y = d
    (C) ax + cz + d = 0, a^2 + c^2 $ \ne$ 0   <-- CORRECT
    (D) ax + cz = 0, a^2 + c^2 $\ne$ 0
    Answer: C
    Explanation: Since the plane ax + by + cz + d = 0 is parallel to y axis hence b = 0.
Hence ax + cz + d = 0.

Q14. An angle between two diagonals of a cube is
    (A) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{1}{\sqrt{2}}\right)$
    (B) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{8}{5}\right)$
    (C) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{9}{5}\right)$
    (D) cos^-1 $\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Let a be the length of the cube and one corner D(0,0,0) as the origin.the diagonals will have co-ordinates as follows:
A(a,0,0) G(0,a,a) ie diagonal AG and diagonal DF where F(a,a,a)
$cos\theta=\frac{a X -a+a Xa+a X a}{ \sqrt {-a^2+a^2+a^2}\sqrt {a^2+a^2+a^2}}$
$cos \theta =\frac{-a^2+a^2+a^2}{\sqrt {3a^2}\sqrt {3a^2}}$
cos^-1 = $\left(\frac{1}{3}\right)$

Q15. The points P (0, 0, 0), Q (2, 0, 0), R (1, $\sqrt 3 $, 0) and S$\left(1, \frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}, \frac{2 \sqrt{2}}{\sqrt{3}}\right)$ lie
    (A) in a plane at right angles to Z – axis
    (B) in XOY plane
    (C) in a line
    (D) none of these   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: The equation of plane passing through (0, 0, 0) is a(x - 0) + b(y - 0) + c(z - 0) = 0
ax + by + cz = 0. If it passes through Q (2, 0, 0), R (1, $\sqrt 3 $, 0) then we get
2a = 0; a +$\sqrt 3$ b = 0 i.e. we get a = 0 and b = 0
Now if we put co-ordinates of S it does not satisfy the equation.
Hence points are not coplanar.

Q1. $\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0} \frac{\log (1+a x)-\log (1+b x)}{x}$ is equal to
    (A) a – b   <-- CORRECT
    (B) log a + log b
    (C) log a – log b
    (D) a + b
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0} \frac{\log (1+a x)}{x}-\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0} \frac{log (1 + bx)}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0}\frac{\log (1+a x)}{x} \cdot \frac{a}{a}-\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0} \frac{\log (1+b x)}{x} \cdot \frac{b}{b}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ a - b

Q2. If $f(x)=\left|4 x-x^2-3\right|$ when $x €[0,4]$, then, which of the following is correct?
    (A) $x=2$ is the global maximum
    (B) $x=0$ is the global maximum
    (C) $x=1$ is the global maximum
    (D) $x=3$ is the global maximum   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Clearly, $x=1,3$ are the points of global minimum (as the values being equal).
And, $x=0,4$ are the points of global maximum (as the values being equal).
And, $x=2$, is the point of local maximum (as the values being equal).
Thus, $x=3$ is the global maximum.

Q3. Let f(x) = x sin$\frac 1 x$, x $ \ne $ 0, then the value of the function at x = 0, so that f is continuous at x = 0, is
    (A) $% MathType!Translator!2!1!LaTeX.tdl!LaTeX 2.09 and later! % MathType!MTEF!2!1!+- % feaagGart1ev2aaatCvAUfeBSjuyZL2yd9gzLbvyNv2CaerbuLwBLn % hiov2DGi1BTfMBaeXatLxBI9gBaerbd9wDYLwzYbItLDharqqtubsr % 4rNCHbGeaGqiVu0Je9sqqrpepC0xbbL8F4rqqrFfpeea0xe9Lq-Jc9 % vqaqpepm0xbba9pwe9Q8fs0-yqaqpepae9pg0FirpepeKkFr0xfr-x % fr-xb9adbaqaaeGaciGaaiaabeqaamaabaabaaqcfayaaiabgkziUk % abg6HiLcaa!39D7! \[ \to \infty \]% MathType!End!2!1! $$\sqrt{2}$
    (B) 1
    (C) -1
    (D) 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Here, if we directly put x = 0, f(0) = 0 $\times$ sin ($\frac{1}{0}$) = 0.
At L.H.L, put x = 0 - h$% MathType!Translator!2!1!LaTeX.tdl!LaTeX 2.09 and later! % MathType!MTEF!2!1!+- % feaagGart1ev2aaatCvAUfeBSjuyZL2yd9gzLbvyNv2CaerbuLwBLn % hiov2DGi1BTfMBaeXatLxBI9gBaerbd9wDYLwzYbItLDharqqtubsr % 4rNCHbGeaGqiVu0Je9sqqrpepC0xbbL8F4rqqrFfpeea0xe9Lq-Jc9 % vqaqpepm0xbba9pwe9Q8fs0-yqaqpepae9pg0FirpepeKkFr0xfr-x % fr-xb9adbaqaaeGaciGaaiaabeqaamaabaabaaqcfayaamaaxababa % GaciiBaiaacMgacaGGTbaabaGaamiAaiabgkziUkaaicdaaeqaaaaa % !3D0B! \[\mathop {\lim }\limits_{h \to 0} \]% MathType!End!2!1! $, $\mathop {lim}\limits_{x \to 0} x.\sin \frac1x$ f(0 - h) = 0.
At R.H.L, put x = 0 + h ,$\mathop {lim}\limits_{x \to 0} x.\sin \frac1x$$% MathType!Translator!2!1!LaTeX.tdl!LaTeX 2.09 and later! % MathType!MTEF!2!1!+- % feaagGart1ev2aaatCvAUfeBSjuyZL2yd9gzLbvyNv2CaerbuLwBLn % hiov2DGi1BTfMBaeXatLxBI9gBaerbd9wDYLwzYbItLDharqqtubsr % 4rNCHbGeaGqiVu0Je9sqqrpepC0xbbL8F4rqqrFfpeea0xe9Lq-Jc9 % vqaqpepm0xbba9pwe9Q8fs0-yqaqpepae9pg0FirpepeKkFr0xfr-x % fr-xb9adbaqaaeGaciGaaiaabeqaamaabaabaaqcfayaamaaxababa % GaciiBaiaacMgacaGGTbaabaGaamiAaiabgkziUkaaicdaaeqaaaaa % !3D0B! \[\mathop {\lim }\limits_{h \to 0} \]% MathType!End!2!1! $, f(0 + h) = 0.
Hence, L.H.L = f(0) = R.H.L.
f(x) is continuous at x = 0.

Q4. $\lim \limits_{x \to 0}\frac{\tan x-\sin x}{x^3}$ is equal to
    (A) 0
    (B) $\frac 1 2$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) 1
    (D) 4
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The function can be written as 
$\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{\sin x(1-\cos x)}{\left(x^{3}\right)(\cos x)}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim _\limits {x \rightarrow 0} \left(\frac{\sin x}{x}\right) \cdot\left(\frac{1-\cos x}{x^2}\right) \cdot\left(\frac{1}{\cos x}\right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $1 \cdot \frac{1}{2} \cdot 1$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{2}$

Q5. $\lim \limits_{x \to 0} \frac{x \log (1+x)}{1-\cos x}$ is equal to
    (A) $\frac 12$
    (B) 1
    (C) 0
    (D) 2   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{x \log (1+x)}{1-\cos x} \cdot \frac{x}{x}$
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0}\left(\frac{\log (1+x)}{x}\right) \cdot\left(\frac{x^{2}}{1-\cos x}\right)$
$\Rightarrow$ $1 \cdot \frac{1}{\frac{1}{2}}$
$\Rightarrow$ 2

Q6. $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{e^{p x}-e^{q x}}{x}$ is equal to
    (A) log (p - q)
    (B) p - q   <-- CORRECT
    (C) p^q
    (D) log p - log q
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{e^{p x}+1-1-e^{q x}}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim\limits_{x \to 0} \frac {{e}^{px}-1}{x}-\lim\limits_{x \to 0}\frac {{e}^{qx}-1}{x}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \left(\frac{e^{p x}-1}{x}\right)\left(\frac{p}{p}\right)-\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0}\left(\frac{e^{q x}-1}{x}\right)\left(\frac{q}{q}\right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ p - q

Q7. $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{(1-x)^n-1}{x}$ is
    (A) (n - 1) $\!$
    (B) -n   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $n^2$
    (D) n $\!$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The given limit is in the form f $\frac 00$ using L'hospital Rude
Putting x = 0 in $\frac{n(1-x)^{n-1}}{1}\cdot (-1)$

Q8. $\lim\limits_{x \to 0} \frac{\tan x-x}{x^2 \tan x}$ is equal to
    (A) 0
    (B) $\frac 1 3$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac 1 2$
    (D) 1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: The following limit is in the form of $\frac{0}{0}$ 
Using L'Hospital rule;
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \frac{\tan ^{2} x}{\left(x^{2}\right)+\left(x^{2} \tan ^{2} x\right)+(\tan x)(2 x)}$ = $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0} \left(\frac{(\tan x)^{2}}{x^{2}}\right) \cdot\left(\frac{1}{1+\tan ^{2} x+\left(\frac{2 \tan x}{x}\right)}\right)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $1 \cdot\left(\frac{1}{1+0+2}\right)$
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{1}{3}$

Q9. $\mathop {lim}\limits_{x \to 0} \;\;\left[ {\cos x} \right]$
    (A) is equal to – 1
    (B) does not exist
    (C) is equal to 1
    (D) is equal to 0   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: L.H.L. = $\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{lim}[\cos (x-h)]$ = 0
R.H.L = $\underset{x \rightarrow 0}{lim}[\cos (x+h)]$ = 0

Q10. $\lim\limits_{x \to 0}\frac{\sin x-x}{x^3}$ is equal to
    (A) $\frac 16$
    (B) 0
    (C) $ -\frac 1 3$
    (D) $-\frac 16$   <-- CORRECT
    Answer: D
    Explanation: Since the limit is in the form of $\frac{0}{0}$. By applying L'hospital first time we get, $\frac{\cos x-1}{3 x^2}$ 
Again using L'Hospital; $\frac{-\sin x}{6 x}$ 
Again using L'Hospital we get $\frac {-1}{6}$

Q11. $\lim\limits_{x \to 0} \left(\frac{\sin x-x}{x}\right) \cos \left(\frac{1}{x}\right)$ is equal to
    (A) 1
    (B) 0   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac 12$
    (D) -1
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\lim\limits_{x \to 0} \;[(\frac{\sin x}{x})-(\frac{x}{x})](\cos \frac1x)$ 
$\Rightarrow$ (0) finite number = 0

Q12. $\lim\limits_{x \to 0} \left(\frac{\sin x-x}{x^4}\right) \sin x$ equal to
    (A) $\frac1 3$
    (B) $ - \frac 1 6$   <-- CORRECT
    (C) $\frac 16$
    (D) $ - \frac 13$
    Answer: B
    Explanation: $\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0}\left(\frac{\sin x-x}{x^3}\right) \cdot\left(\frac{\sin x}{x}\right)=\lim \limits_{x \rightarrow 0}\left(\frac{\sin x-x}{x^3}\right)$ 
Now using L'Hospital we have, $\frac{\cos x-1}{3 x^2}$
Again using L'Hospital, $\frac {-\sin x}{6x}$
Again using L'hospital; $\frac {-1}{6}$

Q13. Let f(x) = $\frac{2-(256-7 x)^{1 / 8}}{(5 x+32)^{1 / 5}-2}, x \neq 0$, then for f to be continuous at x = 0, f(0) must be equal to
    (A) $\frac {7} {64}$   <-- CORRECT
    (B) -1
    (C) $ - \frac {7} {64}$
    (D) 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: f(x) = $\frac{2-(256-7 x)^{1 / 8}}{(5 x+32)^{1 / 5}-2}$ = f(x) = $\lim\limits_{x \to 0 } \frac{(256)^{\frac{1}{8}}-(256-7 x)^{\frac 1 8}}{(5 x+32)^{1 / 5}-(32)^{\frac{1}{5}}}$ 
Using L' Hospital
$\Rightarrow$ $\lim\limits_{x \to 0 }\frac{-\left(\frac{1}{8}\right)(256-7 x)^{-7 / 8}(-7)}{\left(\frac{1}{5}\right)(5 x+32)^{(-4) / 5}(5)}$
$\Rightarrow$ $\frac{7}{64}$

Q14. If $\begin{array}{c} \frac{\sin [x]}{[x]},[x] \neq 0 \\ 0 \quad,[x]=0 \end{array}$, where [.] denotes the greatest integer function, then $\lim \limits _{x \rightarrow 0} f(x)$ is equal to
    (A) does not exist   <-- CORRECT
    (B) is equal to 0
    (C) is equal to -1
    (D) is equal to 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: $\mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0^+}\frac{sin\;[x]}{[x]}$ = 1
$\Rightarrow \mathop {Lt}\limits_{x \to 0^-}\frac{sin\;[x]}{[x]}$ = sin 1
$\Rightarrow$ L.H.L.$\neq$ R.H.L.
hence limit does not exist.

Q15. $\mathop {lim}\limits_{x \to \infty } x\left( {{a^{1/x}} - 1} \right)$, where a > 0, is equal to
    (A) log_e a   <-- CORRECT
    (B) e
    (C) log_a e
    (D) 1
    Answer: A
    Explanation: Let x = $\frac{l}{t}$ 
$\Rightarrow$ $\underset{t \rightarrow 0}{lim} \frac{a^{t}-1}{t}$ = log_e a

Limits and Derivatives Test 02  (id 663) [PAID]
